Lineage When Woman in Iddah Claims Its Completion
Ruling on child's lineage based on timing of birth after woman's claim of iddah completion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on child's lineage when a woman in iddah falsely claims its completion, and explain the distinction based on timing.

Core Idea
If a woman in iddah falsely claims its completion and gives birth within less than six months, the child's lineage is established; at six months, it is not.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from the chapter on lineage. A woman in iddah declares that her waiting period has ended, then gives birth. The legal consequence depends on whether the birth occurs in less than six months or exactly six months after her declaration. The Hanafi school uses the minimum duration of pregnancy as a key indicator to determine the truth of her declaration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the two scenarios
The case is a woman in iddah who admits her iddah is over, then gives birth. There are two scenarios: birth in less than six months versus birth at six months.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
If birth is less than six months, lineage is established. If birth is at six months, lineage is not established.
3
Trace the reasoning: certainty vs. probability
Less than six months gives certainty that she was pregnant at the time of her claim, so her claim is false. At six months, there is probability that conception occurred after the claim, so the claim may be true.
4
Note the generality of the ruling
The author states that this ruling applies to all types of iddah: raj'i, ba'in, and death iddah.

و اذا اعترفت المعتدة بانقضاء عدتها ثم جاءت بالولد لاقل من ستة اشهر يثبت نسبه لانه ظهر كذبها بيقين فبطل الاقراروان جاءت به لستة اشهر لم يثبت لا نالم نعلم ببطلان الاقرار لاحتمال الحدوث بعده وهذا اللفظ باطلاق يتناول كل معتدة ترجمہ اور جب معدہ نے اپنی عدت گذرنے کا اقرار کیا پھر اس نے ( اقرار کے وقت سے ) چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنا تو اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ معتدہ کا جھوٹا ہونا یقین کے ساتھ معلوم ہو گیا۔ اس وجہ سے اس کا اقرار باطل ہو گیا اور اگر اس نے چھ ماہ میں بچہ جنا تو نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اقرار کے باطل ہونے کا ہمیں علم نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اقرار کے بعد حمل پیدا ہونے کا احتمال ہے اور یہ لفظ اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے ہر معدہ کو شامل ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معتدہ نے کہا کہ میری عدت گزرگئی۔ پھر اس کے اقرار کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم مدت میں بچہ ہو گیا تو اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب اقرار کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم مدت میں بچہ پیدا ہو گیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ اقرار کے وقت یہ معدہ حاملہ تھی اور چونکہ حاملہ کی عدت وضع حمل ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے یہ معتدہ انقضاء عدت کا اقرار کرنے میں جھوٹی ہوگی اور جب اقرار میں جھوٹی قرار پائی تو اقرار ہی باطل ہو گیا اور جب عدت گزرنے کے بارے میں اقرار باطل ہو گیا تو بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا اور اگر اقرار کے وقت سے پورے چھ ماہ میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں یہ احتمال ہے کہ اقرار کے بعد حمل پیدا ہوا ہو۔ اس وجہ سے بطلان اقرار کا یقین نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مائن کا قول اذا اعترفت المعتدہ اپنے اطلاق کی وجہ سے ہر معتدہ کو شامل ہے۔ خواہ معتدہ رجعیہ ہو یا معتدہ بائنہ اور یا معتدہ وفات سب کا حکم یہی ہے جو اوپر بیان کیا گیا۔
And when the woman in iddah admits the completion of her iddah, then she gives birth to a child in less than six months, his lineage is established because her falsehood becomes known with certainty, so the admission is void. And if she gives birth at six months, it is not established because we do not know the voidness of the admission due to the possibility of its occurring after it. And this word, by its generality, includes every woman in iddah. Translation: And when a woman in iddah admitted the completion of her iddah, then she gave birth to a child in less than six months from the time of admission, the child's lineage is established. Because the woman's falsehood became known with certainty, therefore her admission became void. And if she gave birth at six months, lineage is not established because we do not know the voidness of the admission, due to the possibility of pregnancy occurring after the admission. And this word, due to its generality, includes every woman in iddah. Explanation: The issue is that a woman in iddah said her iddah has passed, then within less than six months from the time of her admission a child is born, so the child's lineage is established. The proof is that when the child is born within less than six months from the time of admission, it becomes known that at the time of admission this woman was pregnant, and since the iddah of a pregnant woman ends with childbirth, therefore this woman is lying in her admission of completion of iddah. And when she is found to be lying in the admission, the admission itself becomes void. And when the admission regarding the passing of iddah becomes void, the child's lineage is established. And if the child is born at exactly six months from the time of admission, lineage is not established, because in that case there is a possibility that the pregnancy occurred after the admission, so the voidness of the admission is not certain. The author of Hidayah says that the statement 'when the woman in iddah admits' by its generality includes every woman in iddah, whether she is in raj'i iddah, ba'in iddah, or death iddah – all have the same ruling as explained above.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on establishing lineage. The case is: a woman in iddah declares that her iddah has ended, then gives birth. The ruling depends on the timing. If the birth occurs within less than six months from her declaration, the child's lineage is established to the husband. The reasoning is that the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months from conception; if the child is born less than six months after her declaration, it proves she was already pregnant at the time of declaration, and since a pregnant woman's iddah ends only with childbirth, her declaration was false. Therefore, her declaration is void, and the child is considered born during the iddah, so lineage is established. If the birth occurs exactly six months after the declaration, lineage is not established because it is possible she conceived after the declaration, making her declaration potentially true. The author notes that this ruling applies to all types of iddah: raj'i (revocable divorce), ba'in (irrevocable divorce), and death iddah.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before she can remarry.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity of a child, specifically the legal attribution of the child to the father.
اقرار (iqrar): An admission or declaration of a legal fact, here the woman's declaration that her iddah has ended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman in iddah claims her iddah has ended and then gives birth exactly six months later, is the child's lineage established according to this passage?
A) Yes, because she was lying.
B) No, because it is possible she conceived after the claim.
C) Yes, because the child was born within the iddah.
D) No, because she must provide witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The timing of birth relative to the woman's declaration of iddah completion determines lineage: less than six months voids her declaration, at six months it does not.

Witnesses for Lineage of Child Born During Iddah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of witnesses for birth during iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the testimony required to establish the lineage of a child born during iddah, and apply the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn to new scenarios.

Core Idea
The firash during iddah determines if complete testimony is needed for lineage or just a single woman's identification.

When a woman in iddah gives birth, and her former husband denies paternity, the question arises: what testimony is sufficient to prove the child's lineage? This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The disagreement is not merely numerical; it rests on a fundamental legal analysis of the nature of iddah and the presumption of the marital bed (firash). Understanding this dispute will sharpen your ability to trace legal reasoning within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the contested issue
Identify the exact legal question: what testimony is needed to establish the lineage of a child born to a woman during her iddah when the husband denies paternity?
The key is that the husband's denial triggers the need for proof; otherwise, acknowledgment or apparent pregnancy may suffice.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa requires two men or one man and two women (complete testimony). His reasoning: the woman's admission of birth ends the iddah, so the firash (marital bed) is no longer a valid basis for lineage. Thus, lineage must be established anew, requiring full testimony.
Note the exceptions: if the pregnancy was apparent before birth, or if the husband acknowledged the pregnancy, lineage is established before birth and no testimony is needed.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position and their proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that one upright Muslim woman's testimony suffices in all cases. They argue that the firash continues throughout iddah, so lineage is already presumed. The only need is to identify that this child is the one born to this woman, which a single woman's testimony accomplishes, just as in an ongoing marriage.
For the Sahibayn, the exceptions of visible pregnancy or husband's acknowledgment are irrelevant because they already accept one woman's testimony.
4
Analyze the root of the disagreement
The difference stems from the legal effect of the iddah period after the woman admits birth. Abu Hanifa sees the iddah as ended, breaking the firash link; the Sahibayn see the iddah as continuing to carry the firash presumption until it fully expires. This leads to different needs for proof.
Also note the qiyas (analogy) used: both sides analogize to an ongoing marriage, but disagree on whether the analogy holds.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, if only one woman testifies, lineage is not established (unless pregnancy was apparent or husband acknowledged). Under the Sahibayn, one woman's testimony always suffices. This affects court decisions and family law practice.
In later Hanafi fatwa, the Sahibayn's view is often considered more practical and is sometimes preferred, though both remain within the school.

اور گواہوں کو اس کا علم ہے کہ اس کمرے میں اس عورت کے سوا کوئی نہیں ہے۔ پھر
And when a woman in iddah gives birth to a child, his lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa unless two men or one man and two women testify to her giving birth, unless there is a visible pregnancy or an acknowledgment from the husband, then lineage is established without testimony. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: it is established in all cases by the testimony of one woman, because the marriage bed (firash) remains due to the continuance of the iddah, and it is binding for lineage, and the need is only to identify that the child is from her, so it is determined by her testimony as in the case of an ongoing marriage. And for Abu Hanifa: the iddah ends by her admission of giving birth, and what has ended is not a proof, so there is a need to establish lineage anew, thus complete testimony is required, unlike when the pregnancy is apparent or the husband acknowledged, because lineage is established before birth and identification is established by her testimony. Translation: And when a woman in iddah gives birth, her child's lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa unless two men or one man and two women testify to the birth, unless there is a visible pregnancy or an acknowledgment from the husband, then lineage is established without testimony. The Sahibayn said: it is established in all cases by the testimony of one woman. The Sahibayn's proof is that due to the existence of iddah, the woman is in her husband's marriage bed (firash), and being in the marriage bed necessitates lineage, and the need is only to identify that the child is from this woman, so this identification is established by her testimony, just as in the case of an ongoing marriage. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that when the woman admitted the birth, her iddah ended, and what has ended is not a proof, so there is a need to prove lineage anew; therefore, complete testimony is required. Unlike when the pregnancy is apparent or the husband acknowledged, because in those cases lineage is established before birth, and identification is established by her testimony. Explanation: If a woman in iddah gives birth and the pregnancy was previously apparent, or the husband had acknowledged the pregnancy, then in both cases lineage is established without testimony. If the woman gives birth and the husband denies the birth, then according to Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa), lineage is established only when two men or one man and two women testify to the birth. The Sahibayn said that in all cases, one free Muslim upright woman's testimony suffices to establish lineage, whether the pregnancy was previously apparent or not, and whether the husband acknowledged or not. Imam Ahmad held the same view. According to Imam Shafi'i, testimony of four women is required. Imam Malik and Ibn Abi Layla say two women's testimony suffices. The Sahibayn's proof: due to the existence of iddah, the woman is in her husband's marriage bed, and the marriage bed necessitates lineage; therefore there is no need to prove lineage anew. The only need is to identify that this child is born from this woman, and that is established by one woman's testimony, as in the case of an ongoing marriage where, by consensus, one woman's testimony establishes identification. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: when the woman admitted giving birth, her iddah ended, and what has ended is not a proof; rather proof is what is present. So there is a need to prove lineage anew, hence complete testimony is required. Complete testimony means two men or one man and two women. However, if the pregnancy was apparent or the husband had acknowledged, the condition of complete testimony is not required, because in that case lineage was established before birth, and the only matter is to identify that this child is from this woman; that is established by one woman's testimony. An objection may be raised on Imam Abu Hanifa's view: how can it be correct to require men's testimony for establishing lineage when it is haram for a man to look at the woman? The answer is that looking is not necessary; testimony can be given without looking, for example, the woman enters a room in front of witnesses, and the witnesses know that there is no one else in the room besides this woman. Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the testimony required to establish the lineage of a child born to a woman during her iddah when the husband denies paternity. Imam Abu Hanifa requires 'complete testimony' (shahadah kamilah): either two men or one man and two women. The Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the testimony of one upright Muslim woman is sufficient in all cases. The dispute centers on two points. First, the nature of the iddah: the Sahibayn argue that the woman is still considered in the marital bed (firash) during iddah, which itself necessitates lineage, so only identification of the child is needed, and a single woman's testimony suffices—analogous to an ongoing marriage where one woman's testimony identifies the child. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the woman's admission of birth causes the iddah to end retroactively? Actually, Abu Hanifa's reasoning: when the woman admits the birth, the iddah ends; the ended iddah is no longer a valid proof (hujjah) for lineage, so lineage must be proven anew like any other birth outside marriage, requiring full testimony. Second, the exceptions: if the pregnancy was visible (zahir) or the husband acknowledged the pregnancy, then lineage is established before birth, and no testimony is needed for the birth itself. The passage also notes positions of other imams: Ahmad agrees with the Sahibayn, Shafi'i requires four women, Malik and Ibn Abi Layla require two women. An objection is raised: how can men testify to birth when looking at the woman might be haram? The answer: men do not need to see the actual birth; they can testify by circumstantial evidence (e.g., the woman enters a room alone and emerges with a child). Thus the requirement of male witnesses does not necessitate sinful looking.

Key Terms
فراش (firash): The marital bed or conjugal relationship; in legal context, the presumption that a child born to a woman during marriage or iddah is attributed to the husband, even without proof of intercourse.
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony given in legal matters. Here, testimony regarding the birth of a child from a specific woman.
تعیین (tayin): Identification or specification; here, identifying that the child is born from that particular woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum testimony required by Imam Abu Hanifa to establish the lineage of a child born to a woman in iddah?
A) One woman
B) Two women
C) Two men or one man and two women
D) Four women

Key Takeaway
The establishment of lineage for a child born during iddah depends on whether the iddah is considered to have ended upon admission of birth (Abu Hanifa) or to continue (Sahibayn), affecting the required testimony.

Witness Requirements for Child Born During Iddah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness requirements for lineage during iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn) on witness requirements for lineage during iddah, explain the basis of each position, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Lineage of a child born during iddah requires witnesses: Abu Hanifa demands full testimony, Sahibayn accept one woman.

The birth of a child during a woman's iddah raises questions of lineage. This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: while both agree that in a subsisting marriage lineage is automatic, they differ on whether the iddah period preserves the marital bed's effect. Understanding this difference sharpens your ability to analyze how legal presumptions interact with procedural proof.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa’s ruling
Identify the witness requirements according to Imam Abu Hanifa: full testimony (two men or one man and two women) unless the pregnancy was apparent or the husband confessed.
Note the exceptions.
2
Identify the Sahibayn’s ruling
State the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: one woman’s testimony suffices in all cases.
They disagree with Abu Hanifa on the need for full testimony.
3
Follow the Sahibayn’s proof
Understand their argument: the woman is still in iddah and thus is her husband’s firash, so lineage is automatic; only identification of the child is needed, which one woman can provide.
Analogous to a subsisting marriage.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa’s rebuttal
Abu Hanifa responds that the woman’s acknowledgment of birth ends the iddah, so the firash no longer operates; lineage must be established anew, requiring complete testimony.
The exceptions (apparent pregnancy/husband confession) are cases where lineage was already fixed before birth.
5
Determine the practical difference
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, if the husband denies and no full testimony exists, lineage is not proven; under Sahibayn, one woman’s testimony is enough.
This affects the child’s status and inheritance rights.

Chapter on Establishing Lineage. Commentary: When a woman in iddah gives birth, her lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa unless two men or one man and two women testify to the birth, unless the pregnancy was apparent or the husband confessed, then lineage is established without witnesses. The two companions (Sahibayn) said that in all cases, one woman's testimony establishes lineage. Their proof: because the woman is still in iddah, she is in the bed of her husband, and being in the bed necessitates lineage; the only need is to identify which child is hers, and that is established by one woman's testimony, as in the case of an existing marriage. Abu Hanifa's proof: the woman's admission of birth means her iddah has passed, and what has passed cannot serve as proof; thus lineage must be established anew, requiring complete testimony. The exception when pregnancy was apparent or the husband confessed is because lineage was already established before birth, and identification is done by one woman's testimony. Explanation: If a woman in iddah gives birth and the pregnancy was apparent beforehand, or the husband acknowledged the pregnancy, then in both cases lineage is established without testimony. If the woman gives birth and the husband denies the birth, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, lineage is established only when two men or one man and two women testify. The Sahibayn said in all cases one free Muslim just woman's testimony establishes lineage, whether the pregnancy was apparent or not, and whether the husband confessed or not. Imam Ahmad holds the same view. Imam Shafi'i requires four women's testimony. Imam Malik and Ibn Abi Layla require two women's testimony. The Sahibayn's proof: because the woman is in iddah, she is in the bed of her husband; being in the bed makes lineage necessary; so there is no need to establish lineage anew; only identification of the child is needed, and that is established by one woman's testimony, just as in the case of an existing marriage where all agree one woman's testimony suffices. Abu Hanifa's proof: when the woman admits the birth, her iddah has passed; what has passed is not proof; only what exists is proof; therefore lineage must be established anew, requiring complete testimony. Complete testimony is two men or two women and one man. However, if the pregnancy became apparent or the husband confessed, the condition of complete testimony is not required, because lineage was already established before birth; only the identification of this child as hers remains, and that is established by one woman's testimony. An objection against Imam Abu Hanifa: how can requiring men's testimony be correct when a man looking at a woman is forbidden? Answer: looking is not necessary; testimony can be given without seeing, e.g., the woman enters a room in front of witnesses, and they know no one else is in the room, then she comes out with a child; that suffices for testimony.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the proof of lineage for a child born during a woman's iddah. The basic ruling: if a woman in iddah gives birth, the child's lineage to her ex-husband is not automatically established. Imam Abu Hanifa requires full testimony (two men or one man and two women) unless the pregnancy was apparent or the husband admitted it. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that one woman's testimony suffices in all cases. The key difference stems from how they view the legal effect of iddah. The Sahibayn argue that since the woman is still in iddah, she remains her husband's 'firash' (bed), which inherently links the child to him. The only uncertainty is whether this particular child is the one born from that bed, and that can be resolved by one woman's testimony, analogous to how in a subsisting marriage, one woman's testimony suffices to identify the child. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that by acknowledging the birth, the woman effectively confirms that her iddah has ended (since iddah ends with delivery). Once the iddah has ended, the basis for the automatic linkage (firash) is gone. Therefore, establishing lineage requires a fresh proof, namely complete testimony. The exception for apparent pregnancy or husband's confession arises because in those cases, the child's lineage was already fixed before birth, and only identification remains. The passage also addresses an objection: requiring male witnesses when looking at the birth may seem problematic, but the response clarifies that direct visual observation is not necessary; circumstantial evidence (e.g., entering a room empty except for the woman and exiting with a child) is sufficient for testimony.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage; the legal relation of a child to its father
فراش (firash): The marital bed; legal presumption that a child born to a woman during a valid marriage or iddah is from her husband
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony given in legal matters; for lineage, requires specific numbers and conditions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does a child born to a woman in iddah have lineage established without any witnesses?
A) In all cases, one woman's testimony is sufficient
B) Only if the pregnancy was apparent or the husband confessed
C) Only if two men testify
D) Only if four women testify

Key Takeaway
When a child is born during iddah, the witness requirement for lineage differs between Abu Hanifa (full testimony unless apparent or confessed) and the Sahibayn (one woman suffices because the iddah preserves firash).

Establishing Lineage When Heirs Affirm Birth During Death-Iddah
Ruling on nasab with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nasab when heirs affirm birth during death-iddah and apply the subsidiary principle to determine if 'shahada' is required.

Core Idea
Heirs' affirmation establishes inheritance; for others, lineage follows subsidiarily without requiring the word 'shahada'.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced scenario: a woman in the death-iddah gives birth, and the heirs of the deceased husband affirm the birth, but no one testified. The child is unanimously considered the deceased's son for inheritance. However, for lineage rights beyond inheritance—such as marriage restrictions and inheritance from other relatives—a debate arises among Hanafi scholars: does the affirmation require the explicit word 'shahada' to be effective for non-heirs? The passage presents both views and provides a rational proof for the view that it is not required, using the principle of subsidiary establishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Read the opening: if a woman in death-iddah gives birth and the heirs affirm, the child is unanimously the deceased's son. Note the consensus (qawluhum jami'an) for inheritance.
This is the clear ruling for inheritance, as it is purely the heirs' right.
2
Distinguish Between Inheritance and Lineage for Others
The passage then asks: does the affirmation establish lineage for non-heirs (e.g., other relatives)? Two conditions arise: the heirs must be qualified witnesses, and there is a dispute over whether they must utter 'shahada'.
Lineage for others includes rights like inheritance from paternal uncles and prohibitions of marriage.
3
Trace the Disagreement on 'Shahada'
Some mashayikh require the explicit word 'shahada' for proof; others say it is not required because lineage for others is subsidiary to the heirs' own affirmation.
The subsidiary principle: what is established as tābi' (subsidiary) does not require the conditions of the original.
4
Examine the Proof for the Second View
The text provides an analogy: when a master intends residency in travel, the conditions of residency apply only to the master, not to his slaves and servants, as they are subsidiary. Similarly, lineage for others follows the heirs' affirmation without extra conditions.
This is a qiyas based on the general rule that subsidiary matters follow the original with relaxed conditions.
5
Apply the Thamarah al-Khilaf
If the second view is taken, the child's lineage is fully established for all purposes without the word 'shahada'. If the first view is taken, lineage for others is not established unless the heirs explicitly testify.
The practical impact: marriage restrictions, inheritance from other relatives, and custody rights.

ترجمہ. پس اگر عورت (اپنے شوہر کی ) وفات سے عدت میں ہے ( اور اس نے ولادت کا دعوی کیا ) اور وارثوں نے ولادت میں اس کی تصدیق کی۔ مگر ولادت پر کسی نے گواہی نہیں دی۔ تو بالاتفاق یہ اس کے شوہر کا بیٹا ہے اور یہ ( ثبوت بنوت ) وراثت کے حق میں ظاہر ہے۔ کیونکہ میراث ان کا خالص حق ہے۔ لہذا میراث کے حق میں ان کا تصدیق کرنا قبول ہوگا۔ رہا نسب کے حق میں ۔ کیا ان کے علاوہ کے حق میں نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ تو مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اگر تصدیق کرنے والے ورثہ اہل شہادت میں سے ہوں ۔ تو (نسب ) ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حجت ( شرعیہ ) قائم ہوگئی۔ اسی وجہ سے کہا گیا کہ لفظ شہادت شرط ہے اور کہا گیا کہ شرط نہیں ۔ کیونکہ تصدیق کرنے والوں کے علاوہ کے حق میں نسب ثابت ہونا تابع ہے ان کے اقرار کی وجہ سے ان کے حق میں ثابت ہونے کے اور جو چیز تابع ہو کر ثابت ہوتی ہے، اس میں شرائط کی رعایت (ضروری) نہیں۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی عورت اپنے شوہر کے انتقال کی وجہ سے عدت میں ہے۔ پھر اس نے دو سال مکمل ہونے سے پہلے بچہ پیدا ہونے کا دعویٰ کیا اور اس کے تمام ورثہ یا بعض ورثہ ( جو جواز شہادت میں کفایت کر جائیں یعنی دو مرد یا ایک مرد اور دو عورتوں ) نے بچہ کی ولادت کا اقرار بھی کر لیا۔ لیکن کسی نے بچہ پیدا ہونے پر شہادت نہیں دی تو فقہاء احناف کے نزدیک بالاتفاق یہ بچہ مرنے والے کا بیٹا ہوگا۔ یعنی اس بچہ کا مرنے والے سے نسب ثابت ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بیٹا ہونے کا ثبوت میراث کے حق میں ظاہر ہے۔ یعنی یہ بچہ میراث لینے میں دوسرے ورثہ کا شریک ہو گا۔ کیونکہ میراث خالص ورثہ کا حق ہے۔ لہذا اپنے حق میں ان کا اقرار کرنا قبول ہوگا۔
رہی یہ بات کہ عام لوگوں کے حق میں اس بچہ کا نسب مرنے والے سے ثابت ہو گا یا نہیں تو اس بارے میں مشائخ کا قول یہ ہے کہ اگر تصدیق اور اقرار کرنے والے ورثہ اہل شہادت میں سے ہوں ۔ بایں طور کہ سب مرد ہوں ۔ یا عورتیں دو ہوں اور وہ عادل بھی ہیں تو تمام لوگوں کے حق میں اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حجت شرعی یعنی شہادت کاملہ پائی گئی۔ حتی کہ یہ بچہ مقرین اور منکرین دونوں کے ساتھ میراث میں شریک ہوگا اور دوسرے ورثہ کی طرح اس بچہ کو بھی میت کے مدیون سے دین کے مطالبہ کا حق ہوگا۔ اور چونکہ تصدیق کرنے والے ورثہ کا اہل شہادت میں سے ہونا شرط ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ لفظ شہادت شرط ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ شہادت کا لفظ شرط نہیں ہے۔ قول ثانی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ورثہ کے اقرار اور تصدیق کی وجہ سے اصل میں تو نسب انہیں کے حق میں ثابت ہوگا اور ان کے علاوہ کے حق میں ان کے تابع ہو کر نسب ثابت ہوگا اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز تابع ہو کر ثابت ہوتی ہے، اس میں شرائط کا لحاظ ضروری نہیں ہوتا ۔
مثلاً مولی نے سفر میں کسی جگہ اقامت کی نیت کی تو اقامت کے شرائط مولی کے حق میں معتبر ہوں گے نہ غلام اور خدام کے حق میں۔ کیونکہ یہ لوگ اپنے مولیٰ کے تابع ہیں۔
Chapter of Establishing Lineage. If she is in iddah from death and the heirs affirm her regarding the birth and no one testified to the birth, then he is his son in the opinion of all of them. This is apparent in the right of inheritance because it is purely their right, so their affirmation is accepted. As for the right of lineage, is it established for others? They said if they are among those qualified to testify, then it is established due to the establishment of a proof. For this reason it was said that the word 'shahada' is a condition, and it was said it is not a condition because the establishment for others is subsidiary to the establishment for them by their affirmation, and what is established as subsidiary does not require conditions.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage discusses the establishment of lineage (nasab) when a woman in the iddah of death gives birth. The key ruling is that if the heirs of the deceased husband affirm the birth, the child is considered the son of the deceased by unanimous agreement of the Hanafi jurists. This is clear for inheritance because it is purely the heirs' right, so their affirmation is accepted. However, regarding lineage for others (such as for the child's own rights of inheritance from other relatives, or for marriage restrictions), there is a discussion. The mashayikh state that if the affirming heirs are qualified to be witnesses (i.e., they are just and meet the requirements of testimony), then lineage is established for all because a complete proof (hujja shar'iyya) exists. There is a disagreement among the mashayikh whether the word 'shahada' (testimony) must be explicitly uttered. Some require it, others do not. The latter view is supported by the principle that when something is established as subsidiary, the conditions of the original do not apply. An example is given: when a master intends residence in a journey, the conditions of residence apply only to the master, not to his slaves and servants, because they are subsidiary to him.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity, the legal relationship between a child and father that carries rights of inheritance, custody, and marriage restrictions.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after the death of her husband or after divorce, during which she cannot remarry.
شہادت (shahada): Testimony, the legal act of bearing witness in court or establishing a fact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a woman in death-iddah gives birth and the heirs affirm the birth, what is the unanimous Hanafi ruling?
A) The child is not considered the deceased's son without testimony.
B) The child is the deceased's son only for inheritance.
C) The child is the deceased's son for all purposes with the word 'shahada'.
D) The child is the deceased's son in the opinion of all of them, at least for inheritance.

Key Takeaway
The heirs' affirmation establishes the child's lineage; for non-heirs, lineage follows subsidiarily, and the stronger Hanafi view does not require the word 'shahada'.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
6 min
Lineage of child born within six months of marriage
Ruling on nasab for child born less or more than six months after nikah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on lineage when a child is born less than six months after marriage and explain the Hanafi proof using the concept of firash and the minimum pregnancy period.

Core Idea
A child born less than six months after marriage is not attributed to the husband because conception must precede marriage.

This lesson addresses a fundamental question in family law: when is a child legally attributed to the husband? The Hanafi school provides a clear rule based on the minimum period of pregnancy. We will examine the two scenarios presented in Al-Hidayah and the reasoning behind them, including the role of the marital bed (firash) and the procedure of li'an when the husband denies paternity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage splits the cases: child born less than six months after marriage, and child born six months or more. For each, the ruling on lineage is different.
The exact day of marriage is the starting point for counting.
2
Apply the minimum pregnancy principle
The Hanafi school holds that the shortest possible pregnancy is six months (based on Quranic evidence). If a child is born earlier, conception must have occurred before the marriage, so the husband cannot be the father.
This is a rational inference from the known minimum gestation period.
3
Understand the role of firash (marital bed)
When the marriage is valid and the period is complete, the child is presumed to be from the husband due to the 'firash' — the bed of marriage. This presumption holds even if the husband remains silent.
Firash is a strong legal construct; it attributes the child to the husband unless disowned through li'an.
4
Analyze the husband's denial: testimony and li'an
If the husband denies the birth, a single woman's testimony (e.g., the midwife) suffices to prove the birth. If he denies paternity, he must perform li'an to break the lineage.
Li'an is a specific court procedure involving mutual oaths and curses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب مرد نے عورت سے نکاح کیا اس نے نکاح کے دن سے لے کر چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنا اس کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا
و اذا تزوج الرجل امرأة فجاءت بولد لاقل من ستة اشهر منذ يوم تزوجها لم يثبت نسبه لان العلوق سابق على النكاح فلا يكون منه و ان جاءت به لستة اشهر فصاعدا يثبت نسبه منه اعترف به الزوج او سكت لان الفراش قائم والمدة تامة فان جحد الولادة يثبت بشهادة امرأة واحدة تشهد بالولادة حتى لونفاه الزوج يلاعن لان النسب يثبت بالفراش القائم واللعان انما يجب بالقذف وليس من ضرورته وجود الولد فانه يصح بدونه
ترجمہ اور اگر مرد نے کسی عورت سے نکاح کیا ۔ پس نکاح کے دن سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں اس نے بچہ جنا، تو اس کا نسب ثابت نہ ہوگا کیونکہ نطفہ نکاح پر مقدم ہے۔ لہذا ( یہ ) نطفہ اس مرد سے نہ ہوگا اور اگر (وقت نکاح سے چھ ماہ پر یا زیادہ پر جنا تو شوہر سے اس کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ شوہر اس کا اقرار کرے یا خاموش رہے کیونکہ فراش قائم ہے اور مدت بھی پوری ہے۔ پھر اگر شوہر نے ولادت کا انکار کیا تو ولادت ایک عورت کی گواہی سے جو ولادت کی شاہد ہو ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ حتی کہ اگر شوہر بچہ کی نفی کر دے تو لعان کرے گا۔ اسلئے کہ نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے فراش کے موجود ہونے سے اور لعان واجب ہوتا ہے زنا کی تہمت لگانے سے اور لعان کیلئے بچہ کا موجود ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ لعان بغیر بچہ کے بھی ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مرد نے کسی عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کیا۔ پس نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم مدت میں اس عورت سے بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ تو اس بچہ کا نسب اس مرد سے ثابت نہیں ہو گا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ حمل کی کم سے کم مدت چھ ماہ ہیں اور بچہ پیدا ہوا چھ ماہ سے کم میں تو معلوم ہوا کہ نطفہ نکاح سے پہلے قرار پایا گیا تھا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ نطفہ اس شوہر سے نہیں ہے۔ اور جب نطفہ اس کا نہیں تو اس سے نسب بھی ثابت نہیں ہوگا اور اگر نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ یا زائد میں بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ تو اس بچہ کا نسب اس سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ شوہر اس بچہ کا اقرار کرے یا خاموش رہے ۔ کیونکہ عورت کا فراش ہونا بھی ثابت ہے اور حمل کی مدت بھی پوری ہے۔ اور اگر بچہ چھ ماہ یا اس سے زائد مدت میں پیدا ہو اگر شوہر نے بچہ پیدا ہونے کا انکار کیا تو ایک عورت جو ولادت کی شاہد ہو اس کی شہادت سے ولادت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ حتی کہ اگر شوہر نے اس بچہ کی نفی کی اور کہا کہ یہ بچہ میرے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے۔ تو شوہر اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ لعان کرے گا۔
And if a man marries a woman, and she gives birth to a child in less than six months from the day he married her, his lineage is not established because the conception preceded the marriage, so he cannot be from him. And if she gives birth to it after six months or more, his lineage is established from him, whether the husband acknowledges it or remains silent, because the bed (marital relationship) is established and the period is complete. Then if he denies the birth, it is established by the testimony of one woman who testifies to the birth, such that if the husband disavows the child, he will perform li'an, because lineage is established by the existing bed, and li'an is only obligatory due to slander, and its necessity does not require the existence of the child, as it can occur without it.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi rule for attributing a child born after marriage. The key principle is the minimum period of pregnancy, which is six months according to the Hanafi school (based on Quranic indications and hadith). If a child is born less than six months after the marriage contract, the husband's lineage is not established because conception must have occurred before the marriage, meaning the child is not from him. Conversely, if the child is born six months or more after the marriage, lineage is established even if the husband denies the birth; in such a case, the birth is proven by the testimony of a single woman (the midwife or any woman who attended the birth). If the husband unequivocally denies the child as his, he must perform li'an (mutual cursing) to formally disown the child. Li'an is not contingent on the child's existence; it is required when the husband accuses his wife of adultery. The reasoning is based on the concept of 'firash' (the marital bed), which gives a presumption of legitimacy. The passage also clarifies that for the child born after six months, the husband's acknowledgment is not necessary; silence suffices because the firash is established and the period is complete.

Key Terms
فراش (firash): The marital bed, i.e., the valid marriage relationship that gives a presumption of paternity for any child born within a legally recognized period.
لعان (li'an): Mutual cursing between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of adultery, leading to legal separation and denial of paternity.
علوق (uluq): Conception, the beginning of pregnancy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule stated in this passage, if a woman gives birth to a child exactly six months after her marriage, and the husband remains silent, what is the status of the child's lineage?
A) Not established because six months is the minimum and silence does not constitute acknowledgment.
B) Established because six months is the minimum period and the marital bed is present.
C) Only established if the husband explicitly acknowledges the child.
D) Not established because the husband must testify in court.

Key Takeaway
Lineage is established for any child born six months or more after marriage due to the firash presumption, but not for shorter periods because conception must have preceded the marriage.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Establishing Paternity by Time of Birth and Spousal Dispute
Rulings on paternity from marriage duration and spousal disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for establishing paternity based on the minimum pregnancy period and resolve a spousal dispute over marriage duration.

Core Idea
Paternity is established by the marital bed and a six-month minimum; the wife's word suffices in duration disputes.

In Hanafi fiqh, lineage (nasab) is a crucial legal status with implications for inheritance, custody, and marriage. This passage from Al-Hidayah presents two key rules: first, how the timing of birth relative to marriage determines paternity, and second, how a dispute between spouses about the marriage duration is resolved. Understanding these rules equips you to handle real cases of paternity establishment and denial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage contains two distinct rulings: (A) paternity is established if the child is born at six months or more after marriage, regardless of the husband's acknowledgment; (B) if the spouses dispute the duration, the wife's statement is accepted and the child is attributed to the husband.
Ruling (B) is conditional on the child being born; the dispute is about when the marriage occurred.
2
Examine the dalil for ruling (A)
The proof is the marital bed (firāsh) being established and the minimum pregnancy period (six months) being complete. The text states 'al-firāsh qā'im wa al-mudda tāmma' – the bed is present and the period is full. If the husband denies the birth, a single woman's testimony suffices to prove the birth.
The minimum pregnancy period is derived from Quranic and hadith sources; six months is the shortest possible viable pregnancy in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the li'an consequence
If the husband denies paternity after birth is proven, he must perform li'an (mutual imprecation) because his denial is an accusation of zina (qadhf). Li'an becomes wajib due to the accusation, not because of the child's existence – li'an is valid even without a child.
An objection is raised: li'an is akin to hadd, which cannot be proven by a woman's testimony. The answer is that li'an is required by the accusation itself, not by the child's testimony.
4
Analyze the dalil for ruling (B)
The proof is the apparent circumstance (ẓāhir) that a Muslim woman gives birth from marriage, not fornication. Also, the hadith 'al-bayyinatu ‘alā al-mudda‘ī' places the burden of proof on the plaintiff; the husband is the plaintiff (claiming shorter duration) and the wife is the defendant, so her statement is accepted.
The hadith principle applies even without specific evidence; the wife's statement is taken without an oath according to the preferred view.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani held that the wife should take an oath in the duration dispute. However, the relied-upon position in Al-Hidayah does not require an oath, as the ẓāhir suffices.
The practical difference: with oath, the wife must swear; without, her mere claim establishes paternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ثبوت النسب
انہیں کے حق میں ثابت ہوگا اور ان کے علاوہ کے حق میں ان کے تابع ہو کر نسب ثابت ہوگا اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو چیز تابع ہو کر ثابت ہوتی ہے، اس میں شرائط کا لحاظ ضروری نہیں ہوتا ۔
مثلاً مولی نے سفر میں کسی جگہ اقامت کی نیت کی تو اقامت کے شرائط مولی کے حق میں معتبر ہوں گے نہ غلام اور خدام کے حق میں۔ کیونکہ یہ لوگ اپنے مولیٰ کے تابع ہیں۔
جب مرد نے عورت سے نکاح کیا اس نے نکاح کے دن سے لے کر چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنا اس کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا
و اذا تزوج الرجل امرأة فجاءت بولد لاقل من ستة اشهر منذ يوم تزوجها لم يثبت نسبه لان العلوق سابق على النكاح فلا يكون منه و ان جاءت به لستة اشهر فصاعدا يثبت نسبه منه اعترف به الزوج او سكت لان الفراش قائم والمدة تامة فان جحد الولادة يثبت بشهادة امرأة واحدة تشهد بالولادة حتى لونفاه الزوج يلاعن لان النسب يثبت بالفراش القائم واللعان انما يجب بالقذف وليس من ضرورته وجود الولد فانه يصح بدونه
ترجمہ اور اگر مرد نے کسی عورت سے نکاح کیا ۔ پس نکاح کے دن سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں اس نے بچہ جنا، تھر اس کا نسب ثابت نہ ہوگا کیونکہ نطفہ نکاح پر مقدم ہے۔ لہذا ( یہ ) نطفہ اس مرد سے نہ ہوگا اور اگر (وقت نکاح سے چھ ماہ پر یا زیادہ پر جنا تو شوہر سے اس کا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ شوہر اس کا اقرار کرے یا خاموش رہے کیونکہ فراش قائم ہے اور مدت بھی پوری ہے۔ پھر اگر شوہر نے ولادت کا انکار کیا تو ولادت ایک عورت کی گواہی سے جو ولادت کی شاہد ہو ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ حتی کہ اگر شوہر بچہ کی نفی کر دے تو لعان کرے گا۔ اسلئے کہ نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے فراش کے موجود ہونے سے اور لعان واجب ہوتا ہے زنا کی تہمت لگانے سے اور لعان کیلئے بچہ کا موجود ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ لعان بغیر بچہ کے بھی ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مرد نے کسی عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کیا۔ پس نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم مدت میں اس عورت سے بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ تو اس بچہ کا نسب اس مرد سے ثابت نہیں ہو گا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ حمل کی کم سے کم مدت چھ ماہ ہیں اور بچہ پیدا ہوا چھ ماہ سے کم میں تو معلوم ہوا کہ نطفہ نکاح سے پہلے قرار پایا گیا تھا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ سی نطفہ اس شوہر سے نہیں ہے۔ اور جب نطفہ اس کا نہیں تو اس سے نسب بھی ثابت نہیں ہوگا اور اگر نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ یا زائد میں بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ تو اس بچہ کا نسب اس سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ خواہ شوہر اس بچہ کا اقرار کرے یا خاموش رہے ۔ کیونکہ عورت کا فراش ہونا بھی ثابت ہے اور حمل کی مدت بھی پوری ہے۔ اور اگر بچہ چھ ماہ یا اس سے زائد مدت میں پیدا ہو اگر شوہر نے بچہ پیدا ہونے کا انکار کیا تو ایک عورت جو ولادت کی شاہد ہو اس کی شہادت سے ولادت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ حتی کہ اگر شوہر نے اس بچہ کی نفی کی اور کہا کہ یہ بچہ میرے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے۔ تو شوہر اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ لعان کرے گا۔
دلیل یہ ہے عورت کے فراش ہونے کی وجہ سے بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو گیا اور رہا ولادت کا انکار تو وہ ایک عورت کی گواہی سے ثابت ہو گئی ۔
واللعان انما يجب بالقذف سے اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ یہاں بچہ کی نفی کر دینے سے لعان واجب ہوا ہے اور بچہ کی ولادت ایک عورت ( دایہ ) کی شہادت سے ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس نتیجہ نکلا کہ لعان ایک عورت ( دایہ ) کی شہادت سے ثابت ہو جائے گا حالانکہ یہ جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ لعان معنی حد ہے اور حد عورتوں کی شہادت سے ثابت نہیں ہوتی ۔
اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لعان واجب ہوتا ہے زنا کی تہمت لگانے سے اور یہاں زنا کی تہمت موجود ہے۔ اسلئے شوہر کا قول لیس هندی عورت کو زنا کی تہمت لگانا ہے اور تہمت لگانا وجود ولد کوستلزم نہیں کیونکہ بغیر ولد کے بھی قذف ( تہمت لگانا) ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ پس قذف میں اس ولد کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا جو ایک عورت ( دایہ) کی شہادت سے ثابت ہوا ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم
اگر بچہ جنا پھر اختلاف ہو گیا شوہر کہتا ہے میں نے چار مہینے سے نکاح کیا ہے اور عورت چھ ماہ گذرنے کا دعوی کرتی ہے کس کا قول معتبر ہوگا بچے کا نسب ثابت ہوگا یا نہیں؟
فان ولدت ثم اختلفا فقال الزوج تزوجتك منذ اربعة وقالت هى منذستة اشهر فالقول قولها وهو ابنه لان الظاهر شاهد لهافانها تلدظاهرا من نكاح لأمن سفاح ولم يذكر الاستحلاف وهو على الاختلاف ترجمہ . پس اگر عورت سے بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ پھر میاں بیوی نے اختلاف کیا۔ پس شوہر نے کہا میں نے تجھے چار ماہ سے نکاح میں لیا ہے اور عورت نے کہا کہ چھ ماہ سے تو قول عورت ہی کا ( قبول) ہوگا اور یہ بچہ اس کے شوہر کا بیٹا ہے۔ کیونکہ ظاہر اس عورت کا شاہد ہے۔ اسلئے کہ وہ نکاح سے بچہ بنے گی نہ کہ زنا سے اور امام محمد نے قسم لیناز کر نہیں فرمایا حالانکہ وہ مختلف فیہ ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت سے بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ پھر زوجین نے اختلاف کیا۔ چنانچہ شوہر کہتا ہے میں نے تجھے صرف چار ماہ سے نکاح میں لیا ہے اور بیوی کہتی ہے کہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ پورے چھ ماہ سے میں آپ کے نکاح میں ہوں ۔ تو اس صورت میں عورت ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور یہ بچہ اس کے شوہر کا برخوردار کہلائے گا۔ یعنی اس سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ظاہر حال عورت کے موافق ہے۔ کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ مسلمان عورت سے بچہ کی ولادت نکاح کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ زنا کی وجہ سے اور ظاہر حال جس کے موافق ہو وہ مدعی علیہ ہے۔ پس اس مسئلہ میں عورت (بیوی) مدعی علیہ اور اس کا شوہر مدعی ہے اور حديث البينة على المدعی الحدیث کی رو سے اگر مدعی کے پاس بینہ نہ ہوتے ۱۶ علیہ کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے اور چونکہ یہاں مسئلہ مفروضہ یہی ہے کہ شوہر کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے۔ اسوجہ سے عورت جو مدعلی علیہ ہے اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
Chapter on Establishing Lineage. ... And when a man marries a woman and she gives birth to a child in less than six months from the day he married her, his lineage is not established because the conception preceded the marriage, so it cannot be from him. And if she gives birth at six months or more, his lineage is established from him, whether the husband acknowledges it or remains silent, because the marital bed is established and the period is complete. If he denies the birth, it is established by the testimony of one woman who witnesses the birth, so that if the husband disavows the child, he performs li'an, because lineage is established by the existing marital bed, and li'an is only obligatory due to slander, and the existence of the child is not a necessary condition for it, for it (li'an) is valid without it. ... Then if she gives birth and they dispute, and the husband says, 'I married you four months ago,' and she says, 'Six months ago,' then the wife's statement is accepted, and he is his son, because the apparent circumstance testifies for her, for she gives birth apparently from marriage, not from fornication. And he (Imam Muhammad) did not mention requiring an oath, although it is subject to difference.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage from the Chapter on Establishing Lineage (Bāb Thubūt al-Nasab) contains two main rulings. First: if a child is born less than six months after marriage, paternity is not established because the minimum pregnancy term is six months; conception must have occurred before marriage. If born at six months or more, paternity is established regardless of the husband's acknowledgment or silence, because the marital bed (firāsh) is valid and the period is complete. Even if the husband denies the birth, the birth itself can be proven by the testimony of a single woman (e.g., a midwife). If the husband then denies the child, he must perform li'an, because the marital bed establishes lineage, and li'an becomes necessary due to his accusation of adultery. An objection is raised: li'an is akin to a fixed punishment (hadd), which cannot be proven by a woman's testimony. The answer is that li'an is required because of the husband's accusation (qadhf) of zina, which exists here regardless of the child; the child's existence is not a prerequisite for li'an. Second: if a child is born and then the spouses dispute the duration of marriage—husband says 4 months, wife says 6 months—the wife's statement is accepted and the child is attributed to the husband. This is because the apparent circumstance (ẓāhir) supports her: a Muslim woman gives birth from marriage, not fornication. Thus the wife is the defendant (mudda‘ā ‘alayhi) and the husband is the plaintiff (mudda‘ī); according to the hadith ‘al-bayyinatu ‘alā al-mudda‘ī’, the plaintiff bears the burden of proof, and lacking evidence, the defendant's statement is preferred. Imam Muhammad did not mention requiring an oath, though there is a difference of opinion on this point.

Key Terms
فراش (firāsh): The marital bed; the state of being in a valid marriage that makes the wife's offspring presumptively attributed to the husband.
نسب (nasab): Lineage; the legal relationship of parentage between a child and his/her father.
لعان (li‘ān): Mutual imprecation; a procedure in which the husband accuses his wife of adultery and denies paternity, and both parties swear oaths, leading to separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A child is born to a married couple, and the husband says 'We married only 4 months ago,' while the wife says 'We married 6 months ago.' According to the Hanafi position in Al-Hidayah, whose statement is accepted and is an oath required?
A) The husband's statement is accepted, no oath required.
B) The wife's statement is accepted, and an oath is required.
C) The wife's statement is accepted, and no oath is required.
D) The husband's statement is accepted, and an oath is required.

Key Takeaway
Paternity in Hanafi law is established by the marital bed and a six-month minimum pregnancy; in duration disputes, the wife's word is taken without oath.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Statement Accepted in Marriage Duration Dispute at Childbirth
Ruling on credibility when husband and wife disagree on marriage duration at childbirth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when spouses disagree on marriage duration at childbirth, apply the principles of mudda'a alayh and zahir al-hal, and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on oath requirement.

Core Idea
The wife's word is taken because she is the defendant and the apparent circumstance supports her.

When a child is born and the spouses dispute the duration of marriage, the Hanafi school gives priority to the wife's statement, establishing the child's lineage to the husband. This ruling is based on fundamental evidentiary principles: the wife is the defendant, and the apparent circumstance (zahir al-hal) favors her. The passage also addresses objections and an internal Hanafi disagreement about whether an oath is required from the wife. Understanding this case illuminates how Hanafi fiqh balances textual proofs, presumptions, and caution in matters of lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the ruling
The husband claims 4 months of marriage, the wife claims 6. The matn states her statement is accepted and the child is his son. Note this is the default ruling when no evidence is presented.
This is not a case of li'an (mutual imprecation) but a simple evidentiary conflict.
2
Determine plaintiff and defendant
The wife affirms a longer marriage (6 months) while the husband affirms a shorter one (4 months). Since the husband is making a claim that contradicts the apparent continuity of marriage, he is the plaintiff (mudda'i). The wife is the defendant (mudda'a alayh) because she denies his statement and affirms the status quo.
The hadith 'al-bayyina 'ala al-mudda'i' places the burden of proof on the plaintiff.
3
Apply the principle of zahir al-hal
The apparent circumstance is that a Muslim woman gives birth from marriage, not fornication. This presumption (zahir al-hal) supports the wife's claim that the marriage existed at the time of conception.
Zahir al-hal is a recognized proof in Hanafi fiqh for non-criminal matters.
4
Address the objections raised
Objection 1: The wife attributes conception to a time before the husband's claimed marriage, so she should be the plaintiff. The response recharacterizes the claim: the husband is claiming the conception occurred before marriage, making him the plaintiff. Objection 2: The principle of attributing events to the nearest time favors the husband. The response: in lineage, caution (ihtiyat) gives priority to establishing lineage (muthbit) over denial (nafi).
These objections from 'Inayah show the precision of Hanafi jurists in evidentiary reasoning.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on oath
Imam Muhammad did not mention an oath in Jami' al-Saghir. Imam Abu Hanifa holds no oath required; the Sahibayn require an oath from the wife. The practical effect: if an oath is required and the wife refuses, her statement is void and lineage is not established.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference within the school, with no explicit tarjih in this passage.

اگر بچہ جنا پھر اختلاف ہو گیا شوہر کہتا ہے میں نے چار مہینے سے نکاح کیا ہے اور عورت چھ ماہ گذرنے کا دعوی کرتی ہے کس کا قول معتبر ہوگا بچے کا نسب ثابت ہوگا یا نہیں؟
فان ولدت ثم اختلفا فقال الزوج تزوجتك منذ اربعة وقالت هى منذستة اشهر فالقول قولها وهو ابنه لان الظاهر شاهد لهافانها تلدظاهرا من نكاح لامن سفاح ولم يذكر الاستحلاف وهو على الاختلاف ترجمہ . پس اگر عورت سے بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ پھر میاں بیوی نے اختلاف کیا۔ پس شوہر نے کہا میں نے تجھے چار ماہ سے نکاح میں لیا ہے اور عورت نے کہا کہ چھ ماہ سے تو قول عورت ہی کا ( قبول) ہوگا اور یہ بچہ اس کے شوہر کا بیٹا ہے۔ کیونکہ ظاہر اس عورت کا شاہد ہے۔ اسلئے کہ وہ نکاح سے بچہ بنے گی نہ کہ زنا سے اور امام محمد نے قسم لینا ذکر نہیں فرمایا حالانکہ وہ مختلف فیہ ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت سے بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ پھر زوجین نے اختلاف کیا۔ چنانچہ شوہر کہتا ہے میں نے تجھے صرف چار ماہ سے نکاح میں لیا ہے اور بیوی کہتی ہے کہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ پورے چھ ماہ سے میں آپ کے نکاح میں ہوں ۔ تو اس صورت میں عورت ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور یہ بچہ اس کے شوہر کا برخوردار کہلائے گا۔ یعنی اس سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ظاہر حال عورت کے موافق ہے۔ کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ مسلمان عورت سے بچہ کی ولادت نکاح کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ زنا کی وجہ سے اور ظاہر حال جس کے موافق ہو وہ مدعی علیہ ہے۔ پس اس مسئلہ میں عورت (بیوی) مدعی علیہ اور اس کا شوہر مدعی ہے اور حديث البينة على المدعی الحدیث کی رو سے اگر مدعی کے پاس بینہ نہ ہوتے تو مدعی علیہ کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے اور چونکہ یہاں مسئلہ مفروضہ یہی ہے کہ شوہر کے پاس بینہ نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے عورت جو مدعلی علیہ ہے اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
صاحب عنایہ نے اس موقع پر دو اعتراض مع جواب ذکر کیئے ہیں۔ خادم بھی ان کو ذکر کرتا ہے۔ پہلا اعتراض یہ ہے کہ عورت علوق ( نطفہ ) شوہر کے بیان کردہ زمانے یعنی چار ماہ سے پہلے زمانے کی طرف منسوب کرتی ہے اور شوہر اس کا منکر ہے اور بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں منکر کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا شوہر کا قول معتبر ہونا چاہئے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ معارض ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ شوہر علوق کو نکاح سے پہلے زمانے کی طرف منسوب کرنے کا مدعی ہے اور عورت اس کی منکر ہے ۔ لہذا عورت کا قول معتبر ہونا چاہئے۔
دوسرا اعتراض یہ ہے کہ ظاہر حال شوہر کے قول کا شاہد ہے۔ اسلئے کہ نکاح امر حادث ہے اور حوادث میں اصل یہ ہے کہ ان کو اقرب اوقات کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے اور اقرب اوقات کا قائل شوہر ہے نہ کہ اس کی بیوی۔ پس شو ہر مدعی علیہ ہوا اور چونکہ مدعی علیہ کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے شوہر کا قول معتبر ہونا چاہئے ۔ جواب۔ نسب ثابت کرنے میں احتیاط کی جاتی ہے۔ پس جب دو ظا ہر متعارض ہو گئے تو مثبت کو نانی پر ترجیح ہوگی اور چونکہ عورت کا قول مثبت للنسب ہے اور شوہر کا قول نافی للنسب ہے۔ اسلئے عورت کا قول راج ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں یہ ذکر نہیں فرمایا کہ عورت سے قسم لی جائے یا نہ لی جائے ۔ حالانکہ یہ بات مختلف فیہ ہے ۔ چنانچہ صاحبین کے نزدیک قسم لی جائے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک نہ لی جائے ۔ واللہ اعلم
If a child is born, then they disagreed, the husband saying 'I married you four months ago' and she saying 'six months ago', then the [accepted] statement is hers, and he is his son, because the apparent circumstance witnesses for her, as she gives birth apparently from marriage, not from fornication. And [Imam] Muhammad did not mention taking an oath, though it is a matter of disagreement. Explanation: The wife's statement is accepted because the apparent circumstance supports her (a Muslim woman gives birth from marriage, not fornication). The wife is the defendant (mudda'a alayh) and the husband is the plaintiff (mudda'i). Based on the hadith 'al-bayyina ala al-mudda'i', the defendant's statement is accepted if the plaintiff has no evidence. Two objections are addressed: (1) The wife attributes the conception to a time before the husband's claimed marriage, but the husband denies, so the husband should be believed; answer: the husband claims the conception occurred before marriage, so he is the plaintiff, thus the wife's denial stands. (2) The apparent circumstance supports the husband because a new event is attributed to the nearest possible time; answer: in matters of lineage, caution is taken, and when two apparent circumstances conflict, the one that establishes lineage is preferred. Imam Muhammad did not mention whether an oath is required; the Sahibayn say an oath is taken, while Imam Abu Hanifa says no.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a dispute between spouses about the duration of marriage at the time of childbirth. The matn states: if the husband claims he married four months ago and the wife claims six months, the wife's statement is accepted and the child's lineage to the husband is established. The proof is based on two principles: (1) The apparent circumstance (zahir al-hal) favors the wife, as Muslim women give birth from marriage, not fornication. (2) The wife is the defendant (mudda'a alayh) because she affirms a longer marriage duration, so the hadith 'al-bayyina ala al-mudda'i' applies: the plaintiff (husband) must provide proof; without it, the defendant's statement is accepted. The commentary then addresses two objections from Sahib al-Inayah. First, if the wife claims conception occurred before the husband's stated marriage time, she becomes the plaintiff? The answer is that the husband claims the conception happened before marriage, making him the plaintiff. Second, the principle of attributing events to the nearest time (aqrab al-awqat) favors the husband? The answer is that in lineage, caution (ihtiyat) requires preferring the statement that establishes lineage (muthbit) over the one that denies it (nafi). Finally, the matn notes that Imam Muhammad in his Jami' al-Saghir did not mention whether an oath is required from the wife. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say an oath is to be taken, while Imam Abu Hanifa says no oath is needed.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage: the legal relationship of a child to its father.
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a alayh): Defendant: the party against whom a claim is made; their statement is accepted if the plaintiff lacks evidence.
ظاہر حال (zahir al-hal): Apparent circumstance: the factual presumption derived from common practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute where the husband says 'I married you 4 months ago' and the wife says '6 months ago', why is the wife's statement accepted?
A) Because she is the plaintiff.
B) Because she has evidence.
C) Because the apparent circumstance (nikah) supports her, and the husband is the plaintiff who lacks evidence.
D) Because the husband admitted to the marriage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when spouses dispute marriage duration at childbirth, the wife's statement is accepted to establish lineage, based on her status as defendant and the presumption of marriage.

Nikah — Marriage

Duration of Pregnancy: Maximum Two Years, Minimum Six Months
Hanafi position on pregnancy duration with inter-madhhab dispute and commentary on apparent contradiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maximum and minimum pregnancy duration, explain the proof from Quran and Hadith, and contrast the Hanafi view with the Shafi'i/Maliki view.

Core Idea
Pregnancy maximum is 2 years (hadith), minimum 6 months (Quranic deduction).

This lesson examines the Hanafi legal position on the maximum and minimum duration of pregnancy. These rulings are critical for establishing lineage and legal presumptions in family law. We will explore the primary textual proofs, the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools, and a subtle contradiction in Al-Hidayah's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Ruling
State the Hanafi ruling for both maximum and minimum duration of pregnancy. Note that it is a hukm wad'i (declaratory ruling) that sets time limits for legal attribution of a child.
Maximum: 2 years; Minimum: 6 months.
2
Examine the Proof for the Maximum
Analyze the hadith of Aisha (radiAllahu anha) that the child does not remain in the womb more than two years. Understand why this is considered a strong proof (based on hearing from the Prophet, not mere conjecture).
Even a tiny foetus (shadow of a spindle) stays at most two years.
3
Deduce the Minimum from the Quran
Combine two Quranic verses: Surah al-Ahqaf (46:15) says gestation and weaning total 30 months; Surah Luqman (31:14) says weaning is 24 months. Subtract to get 6 months as the minimum gestation period.
This is a standard Hanafi deduction (ta'wil of Ibn Abbas).
4
Contrast with Shafi'i/Maliki Position
State the opposing view (4 years) and their proof (anecdotes of long pregnancies). Then evaluate the Hanafi response: anecdotes cannot override an authentic hadith.
The thamarah al-khilaf: lineage attribution differs if birth occurs between 2 and 4 years.
5
Address the Apparent Contradiction in Al-Hidayah
Note that in the Book of Radā', the author argued each of pregnancy and weaning is 30 months (with reduction by hadith), but here he divides 30 months into 6+24. Understand that this is due to using Ibn Abbas's ta'wil for the minimum, while the earlier argument was for a different context.
The contradiction is not fully resolved, but reflects different methods of istinbat.

Source Text

حمل کی اکثر مدت دو سال ہے
قال واكثر مدة الحمل سنتان لقول عائشة الولد لا يبقى فى البطن اكثر من سنتين ولو بظل مغزل واقله ستة اشهر لقوله تعالى وحمله وفصاله ثلثون شهرا ثم قال وفصاله فى عامين فبقى للحمل ستة اشهر والشافعي يقدر الاكثر باربع سنين والحجة عليه مارويناه والظاهر انها قالته سماعا اذ العقل لا يهتدى اليه
ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا کہ حمل کی اکثر مدت دو سال ہیں۔ دلیل حضرت عائشہ کا قول ہے کہ بچہ پیٹ میں دو برس سے زیادہ نہیں رہتا، اگر چہ تکلے کے سایہ بھر ہو۔ اور حمل کی کم از کم مدت چھ ماہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا 'و حمله و فصاله ثلاثون شهرا' (بچہ کا پیٹ میں رہنا اور دودھ چھوڑنا تیس مہینے ہیں)۔ پھر فرمایا 'و فصاله فی عامین' (اور بچہ کا دودھ چھوڑنا دو برس میں ہوتا ہے) تو حمل کے واسطے چھ ماہ باقی رہے۔ اور شافعی کی اکثر مدت حمل کا اندازہ چار برس لگایا ہے اور امام شافعی کے خلاف وہ حدیث حجت ہے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا اور ظاہر یہی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے اس کو آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے سن کر بیان کیا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عقل کو ایسا اندازہ لگانے کی کوئی راہ نہیں ہے۔

تشریح: ہمارے نزدیک حمل کی زیادہ سے زیادہ مدت دو سال ہے اور امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے نزدیک چار سال ہیں۔
امام شافعی اور امام مالک بعضی حکایات سے استدلال کرتے ہیں۔ مثلاً فرمایا کہ محمد بن عجلان اپنی ماں کے پیٹ میں چار برس رہے۔ ایسے ہی ہرم بن حبان اور ضحاک بن مزاحم اپنی ماں کے پیٹ میں چار برس رہے۔
ہماری دلیل حضرت عائشہ کا قول ہے۔ فرمایا کہ بچہ ماں کے پیٹ میں دو سال سے زیادہ نہیں رہتا اگر چہ تکلے کے سایہ بھر ہو اور ظاہر یہی ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ نے اس کو آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے سن کر بیان کیا ہے۔ پس حدیث امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہوگی اور حکایات روایات کے معارض نہیں ہو سکتیں۔

اور حمل کی اقل مدت بالاتفاق چھ ماہ ہے۔ دلیل قرآن پاک کی آیت 'و حمله و فصاله ثلاثون شهراً' ہے۔ یعنی پیٹ میں رہنے اور دودھ چھوڑنے کی مدت تیس مہینے ہے۔ پھر اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا 'و فصاله فی عامین' یعنی بچہ کا دودھ چھوڑنا دو برس میں ہوتا ہے۔ پھر پس مدت حمل چھ ماہ رہی۔

صاحب ہدایہ کے کلام میں تناقض ہے۔ اس طرح پر کہ کتاب الرضاع میں امام صاحب کی دلیل بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا تھا کہ حمل اور فصال دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی مدت تیس تیس ماہ ہیں۔ مگر یہ کہ مدت حمل میں منقص موجود ہے۔ یعنی حدیث عائشہ 'الولد لا يبقى فى البطن أكثر من سنتين' یعنی وہاں اس مدت کو دونوں پر تقسیم نہیں فرمایا تھا بلکہ دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی مدت پورے تیس ماہ قرار دے کر حدیث عائشہ سے مدت حمل میں کمی کی گئی تھی اور یہاں جب اس آیت کو پیش کیا تو حمل اور فصال دونوں پر اس مدت کو تقسیم فرمایا۔ بایں طور کہ چوبیس ماہ مدت فصال مقرر کی ہے آیت 'و فصاله فی عامین' کی وجہ سے اور باقی چھ ماہ اقل مدت حمل کی مقرر کی ہے۔ دراصل اقل مدت حمل کو بیان کرتے ہوئے صاحب ہدایہ نے جو طریقہ استدلال اختیار کیا ہے یہ ابن عباس کی تاویل ہے۔ چنانچہ مروی ہے،
ان رجلا تزوج امرأة فولدت لستة اشهر فهم عثمان برحمها فقال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما اما انها لو خاصمتكم بكتاب الله تعالى لخصمتكم قال الله تعالى و حمله و فصاله ثلاثون شهراً و قال و فصاله في عامين فلم يبق للحمل الاستة اشهر قدراً عثمان رضی الله تعالى عنه الحد عنها. (فتح القدير )
ایک مرد نے ایک عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کیا۔ پس چھ ماہ پر اس عورت سے بچہ پیدا ہوا تو حضرت عثمان نے اس عورت کو سنگسار کرنے کا ارادہ فرمایا تو ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما نے کہا کہ اگر یہ عورت آپ حضرات سے کتاب اللہ کے ذریعہ جھگڑا کرے گی تو میں بھی آپ سے جھگڑا کروں گا اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے 'و حمله و فصاله ثلاثون شهراً' اور فرمایا 'و فصاله في عامین'۔ پس حمل کی مدت صرف چھ ماہ رہی۔ (یہ سن کر) حضرت عثمان نے اس عورت سے حد دور کر دی۔ پس حضرت عثمان کا حد دفع کرنا اور کسی صحابی کا مخالفت نہ کرنا اجماع کی دلیل ہے۔ بہر حال اگر ابن عباس کی تاویل کے مطابق استدلال کیا جائے جیسا کہ یہاں کہا گیا تو کتاب الرضاع میں جو طریقہ استدلال اختیار کیا گیا ہے وہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور اگر وہ صحیح ہے تو یہ باطل ہو گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ مصنف پر سے تناقض کا اشکال ختم نہیں ہوا۔
The maximum duration of pregnancy is two years. He (al-Quduri) said: The maximum duration of pregnancy is two years, due to the saying of Aisha: 'The child does not remain in the womb more than two years, even if it is the shadow of a spindle.' And its minimum is six months, due to the saying of the Exalted: 'And his gestation and weaning is thirty months.' Then He said: 'And his weaning is in two years.' So six months remain for pregnancy. Al-Shafi'i estimates the maximum as four years. The proof against him is what we have narrated, and it is apparent that she said it by hearing, because reason cannot arrive at it. Translation: Al-Quduri said: The maximum duration of pregnancy is two years. The proof is the saying of Aisha: The child does not remain in the womb more than two years, even if it is the shadow of a spindle. And the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months, because Allah the Exalted said: 'And his gestation and weaning is thirty months.' Then He said: 'And his weaning is in two years.' So for pregnancy six months remain. And al-Shafi'i estimated the maximum duration as four years. The hadith we narrated is proof against him, and it is apparent that Aisha said it having heard it from the Prophet, peace be upon him, because reason cannot find a way to such an estimation. Explanation: According to us, the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years, and according to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik it is four years. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik argue with some anecdotes: for example, they said that Muhammad ibn Ajlan remained in his mother's womb for four years. Similarly, Harm ibn Hayyan and Dahhak ibn Muzahim remained in their mothers' wombs for four years. Our proof is the saying of Aisha. She said: The child does not remain in the mother's womb more than two years, even if it is the shadow of a spindle, and it is apparent that she said it having heard it from the Prophet, peace be upon him. So the hadith is proof against al-Shafi'i, and anecdotes cannot oppose hadith. And the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months by consensus. The proof is the Quranic verse: 'And his gestation and weaning is thirty months,' meaning the period of gestation and weaning is thirty months. Then Allah the Exalted said: 'And his weaning is in two years,' meaning the child's weaning occurs in two years. Then the duration of pregnancy remains six months. There is a contradiction in the speech of the author of al-Hidayah. In the Book of Radā', while explaining the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa, he had said that each of pregnancy and weaning has a duration of thirty months. However, there is a reduction in the duration of pregnancy due to the hadith of Aisha: 'The child does not remain in the womb more than two years.' That is, there he did not divide the duration between both, but rather set each at a full thirty months and then reduced the pregnancy duration by the hadith of Aisha. Here, when presenting this verse, he divided the duration between pregnancy and weaning, making the weaning period twenty-four months due to the verse 'And his weaning is in two years,' and the remaining six months as the minimum pregnancy duration. Actually, in stating the minimum pregnancy duration, the method of deduction chosen by the author of al-Hidayah is the interpretation (ta'wil) of Ibn Abbas. As narrated: A man married a woman, and she gave birth after six months. Uthman intended to stone her. Ibn Abbas said: If she argues with you by the Book of Allah, she would defeat you. Allah said: 'And his gestation and weaning is thirty months' and said: 'And his weaning is in two years.' So only six months remain for pregnancy. Uthman then waived the hadd punishment from her. Uthman's waiving of the hadd and no companion opposing it is proof of consensus. In any case, if one argues according to Ibn Abbas's ta'wil as is said here, then the method of argument chosen in the Book of Radā' becomes invalid, and if that is correct, this becomes invalid. The result is that the issue of contradiction in the author's work is not resolved.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi ruling on the maximum and minimum duration of pregnancy, along with an inter-madhhab dispute and a critical note about an apparent contradiction in the author's reasoning. The passage type is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years, based on the hadith of Aisha that a child does not stay in the womb more than two years, even if the child is as small as the shadow of a spindle (a metaphor for a very tiny foetus). The minimum duration is six months, deduced from two Quranic verses: Surah al-Ahqaf (46:15) states that gestation and weaning together total thirty months, and Surah Luqman (31:14) states that weaning is completed in two years (24 months). Subtracting 24 from 30 leaves 6 months as the minimum possible gestation period. The Hanafi position is contrasted with that of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik, who set the maximum at four years, citing anecdotes of individuals who reportedly remained in the womb for four years. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the hadith of Aisha is authoritative because it is based on hearing from the Prophet, and anecdotes (hikayat) cannot override an authentic hadith. The minimum of six months is uncontested by consensus. The commentary then identifies a contradiction in the author's earlier argument in the Book of Radā' (chapter on breastfeeding) regarding the same Quranic verse. There, the author had argued that both pregnancy and weaning are each thirty months, with a reduction in pregnancy due to the hadith. Here, the author uses Ibn Abbas's ta'wil, which divides the thirty months between pregnancy (6 months) and weaning (24 months). The commentator notes that these two methods are inconsistent. The incident of Uthman and Ibn Abbas is cited as a proof that the minimum of six months was recognized by the Companions and led to a consensus (ijma).

Key Terms
حمل (haml): pregnancy; the period from conception to birth.
اقل مدت (aqall muddah): minimum duration; the shortest possible period for pregnancy to be considered valid for establishing lineage.
اکثر مدت (akthar muddah): maximum duration; the longest possible period after which a child cannot be attributed to the husband.
تکلے کے سایہ (taklay kay saya): shadow of a spindle; an expression used in the hadith to indicate a very small, undeveloped foetus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How do Hanafis derive the minimum duration of pregnancy (6 months) from the Quran?
A) From the verse 'And his gestation and weaning is thirty months', subtracting the weaning period of 24 months from another verse.
B) From the hadith of Aisha about two years.
C) From consensus of the Companions.
D) From a direct statement that pregnancy is six months.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets the maximum pregnancy duration at two years based on a hadith, and the minimum at six months based on Quranic deduction.

Lineage of Child Born to Purchased Slave-Woman After Divorce
Ruling on lineage when a man marries, divorces, then purchases a slave-woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on lineage when a man purchases his divorced slave-woman, distinguishing between one and two divorces based on timing conditions.

Core Idea
For one divorce, lineage within 6 months of purchase is automatic; for two, within 2 years of divorce.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in Hanafi family law: a man marries a slave-woman, divorces her, then purchases her. The key question is whether a child born after the purchase is attributed to him automatically or requires a claim. The ruling hinges on the number of divorces and the timing of birth relative to both divorce and purchase. We will explore the legal reasoning, including the concept of hurmah ghalizah (severe prohibition) and the interplay of Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
1. State the scenario and the basic ruling
A man marries another's slave-woman, divorces her, then purchases her. For one divorce: if the child is born less than 6 months after purchase, lineage is automatic; otherwise, a claim is needed.
The key factor is whether conception occurred before purchase.
2
2. Understand the reasoning for one divorce
If birth within 6 months, conception must have occurred before purchase, during the iddah period. The child is of the mu'taddah, so lineage is established without claim. If after 6 months, conception likely after purchase; then the child is of the owned slave-woman, requiring a claim.
3
3. Contrast with two divorces
Two divorces create a severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah), making intercourse haram even through ownership. Therefore, to avoid attributing a sinful act, conception is presumed to have occurred before divorce, and lineage is automatic if birth within 2 years of divorce.
This shows the principle that prohibitive evidence takes priority over permissive.
4
4. Respond to the objection
An objection: after purchase, ownership should permit intercourse per Quran 23:5-6. The answer: Quran 2:230, which forbids remarriage after three divorces, is analogically applied to two divorces for a slave-woman. This prohibitive verse overrides the permissive one in case of conflict.
The Hanafi principle of preferring muharrim over mubih.
