نہ ہو تو پھوپھیوں اور خالاؤں کی بہ نسبت بہنیں زیادہ حقدار ہیں۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کی ماں باپ کی لڑکیاں ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ بہنیں میراث میں مقدم ہیں ۔ یہ مبسوط کی کتاب النکاح کی روایت ہے۔ اس میں قرب قرابت کی رعایت کی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بہن خالہ کی بہ نسبت اقرب ہے۔ کیونکہ بہن اس کے باپ کی بیٹی ہے۔ اور خالہ اس کی نانا کی بیٹی ہے۔ مگر مبسوط کی کتاب الطلاق میں ہے کہ بچہ کی زیادہ حقدار خالہ ہے۔ یہ نسبت باپ شریکی بہن کے۔ کیونکہ خالہ ماں سے زیادہ قریب ہے۔ اور اس کی تائید اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔ جس کو بخاری اور مسلم نے روایت کیا ہے۔
ان عليا و جعفر الطيار و زيد بن حارثه اختصموا فى بنت حمزة فقال على انا احق بها هي ابنة عمى و قال زيد بنت اخی و قال جعفر بنت عمی و خالتها تحتی فقضى بها النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لخالتها و قال الخالة بمنزلة الام و قال لعلى انت منی و انا منك و قال لجعفر اشبهت خلقی و خلقی و قال لزيد انت اخونا و مولانا
صحیحین میں ہے کہ حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہہ سے عمرہ قضاء میں حدیث طویل مروی ہے۔ اور اس میں آیا کہ جب ہم لوگ مکہ سے باہر نکلے تو حضرت حمزہ کی بیٹی اے پچا اے چا کہتی ہوئی ہمارے پیچھے دوڑی تو علی جعفر طیار اور زید حضرت حمزہ کی لڑکی کے بارے میں جھگڑنے لگے ۔ پس حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ نے کہا کہ میں اس کا زیادہ حقدار ہوں۔ کہ میرے چچا کی بیٹی ہے۔ اور زید بن حارثہ نے کہا کہ یہ تو میرے بھائی کی بیٹی ہے ( زید کی والدہ نے حضرت حمزہ ابن عبد المطلب کو دودھ پلایا تھا اس وجہ سے کہا کہ یہ میرے بھائی کی بیٹی ہے ) اور حضرت جعفر بن ابی طالب نے کہا کہ یہ میرے چچا کی بیٹی ہے اور اس کی خالہ میرے تحت ( نکاح ) میں ہے۔ پس آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حکم فرمایا کہ (جعفر کے یہاں اپنی خالہ کے پاس رہ اور فر مایا کہ خالہ بمنزلہ ماں کے ہے اور حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہ کو فرمایا تو مجھ سے ہے اور میں تجھ سے ہوں۔ اور حضرت جعفر کو کہا کہ تو میری صورت و سیرت سے مشابہ ہے۔ اور زید بن حارثہ کو فرمایا کہ تو ہمارے بھائی اور مولی ہے۔ اس حدیث سے ظاہر ہوا کہ خالہ مقدم ہے۔ اور ایک روایت میں ہے الخالة والدہ اور ایک میں الخالفه ام ۔ اور رفع ابو یہ علی العرش کی تفسیر میں کہا گیا کہ ابو یہ سے مراد حضرت یوسف علیہ السلام کے والد اور خالہ ہیں ۔ اس سے بھی خالہ کا حق ہونا ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ کن کن عورتوں کو پرورش کا حق بالترتیب حاصل ہے
وتقدم الاخت لاب وام لانها اشفق ثم الاخت من الام ثم الاخت من الاب لان الحق لهن من قبل الام ثم الخالات اولى من العمات ترجيحا لقرابة الام وينزلن كمانزلنا الاخوات معناه ترجيح ذات قرابتين ثم قرابة الام ثم العمات ينزلن كذالك
ترجمہ اور جو بہن باپ اور ماں دونوں کی طرف سے ہو وہ دوسری بہنوں پر مقدم ہوگی کیونکہ اس کی شفقت زیادہ ہے۔ پھر جو بہن صرف ماں کی طرف سے ہو۔ پھر جو بہن فقط باپ کی طرف سے ہو ۔ کیونکہ ان عورتوں کا حق ماں کی جانب سے ہے۔ پھر خالائیں یہ نسبت پھوپھیوں کے مقدم ہیں۔ کیونکہ مادری قرابت کو ترجیح حاصل ہے۔ پھر خالائیں درجہ بدرجہ اتریں گی ۔ جیسے ہم نے بہنوں کو اتارا ۔ اس کے معنی ہیں دو قرابت والی کو تر جیح ہوگی۔ (ایک قرابت والی پر ) پھر ماں والی کو پھر خالاؤں کی طرح پھوپھیاں اتریں گی۔
۲۱۹
باب حضانة انزل و من
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جس عورت کے ساتھ دو طرح کی قرابت ہووہ ایک قرابت والی سے زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ حقیقی زنان یعنی جو باپ اور ماں دونوں کی طرف سے ہو وہ دوسری بہنوں یعنی فقط ماں شریکی اور فقط باپ شریکی پر مقدم ہوگی۔ کیونکہ حقیقی بہن کی اسری بہنوں سے زیادہ ہے اس لئے اس کو ترجیح دی گئی ۔ پھر ماں شریکی بہن کو باپ شریکی بہن پر ترجیح ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بہنوں
لئے پرورش کرنے کا حق ماں ہی کی جانب سے ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ماں شریکی بہن کو باپ شریکی بہن پر ترجیح ہوگی امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ حقیقی بہن اور ماں شریکی بہن پرورش کرنے میں دونوں برابر میں کسی کو کسی پر ترجیح نہیں ہے۔ پھر خالا نہیں پھوپھیوں پر مقدم ہیں۔ کیونکہ خالہ کو ماں کے ساتھ قرابت حاصل ہے نہ کہ پھوپھی کو ۔ اور پرورش کرنے میں مادری قرابتداری کو تر جیح ہے نہ کہ پدری قرابت کو پھر خالائیں درجہ بدرجہ اسی طرح رکھی جائیں گی جیسے ہم نے بہنوں کو بیان کیا۔ یعنی بچہ کی جو خالہ اس کی ماں کی حقیقی بہن ایک ماں باپ سے ہو وہ ادنی ہے۔ پھر اس کی ماں کی بہن جو ماں شریکی بہو پھر جو فقط باپ شریکی ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ دو قرابت والی کو ایک قرابت والی پر ترجیح ہو گی ۔ پھر قرابت ام کو قرابت اب پر تر جیح ہو گی۔ پھر اسی طرح درجہ بدرجہ پھوپھیاں ہیں ۔ یعنی باپ کی حقیقی بہن مقدم ہے پھر باپ کی ماں شریکی بہن پھر باپ کی باپ شریکی بہن ہے۔
Chapter of Custody of the Child and Who is More Entitled to It. ... If not, then sisters are more entitled than paternal aunts and maternal aunts because they are the daughters of his father and mother. That is why sisters are given precedence in inheritance. This is the narration in al-Mabsut's Kitab al-Nikah. In it, closeness of relation is considered, because a sister is closer than a maternal aunt; a sister is the daughter of his father, while a maternal aunt is the daughter of his maternal grandfather. However, in al-Mabsut's Kitab al-Talaq, it is stated that the maternal aunt is more entitled to the child, in comparison to the consanguine sister, because the maternal aunt is closer to the mother. This is supported by the hadith narrated by Bukhari and Muslim: 'Ali, Ja'far al-Tayyar, and Zayd ibn Harithah disputed concerning the daughter of Hamzah. 'Ali said: I am more entitled to her; she is the daughter of my paternal uncle. Zayd said: She is the daughter of my brother. Ja'far said: She is the daughter of my paternal uncle, and her maternal aunt is under my marriage. So the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed that she be given to her maternal aunt and said: The maternal aunt occupies the position of the mother. He said to 'Ali: You are from me and I am from you. He said to Ja'far: You resemble my creation and character. He said to Zayd: You are our brother and freed slave. In the two Sahihs, it is narrated that 'Ali (may Allah honor his face) on the occasion of the 'Umrah of al-Qada' narrated a long hadith. It mentions that when we left Mecca, the daughter of Hamzah followed us saying: O uncle, O uncle. Then 'Ali, Ja'far al-Tayyar, and Zayd disputed about the daughter of Hamzah. 'Ali said: I am more entitled to her; she is the daughter of my paternal uncle. Zayd said: She is the daughter of my brother (Zayd's mother had suckled Hamzah ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib, so he said she is the daughter of my brother). Ja'far said: She is the daughter of my paternal uncle, and her maternal aunt is under my marriage. So the Prophet (peace be upon him) decreed that she stay with her maternal aunt in Ja'far's house, and said: The maternal aunt is in the position of the mother. He said to 'Ali: You are from me and I am from you. He said to Ja'far: You resemble my form and character. He said to Zayd: You are our brother and freed slave. This hadith indicates that the maternal aunt is given precedence. In one narration: 'The maternal aunt is a mother,' and in another: 'The maternal aunt is the mother.' In the interpretation of 'Raise Abu Yahya 'alal-'Arsh,' it is said that 'Abu Yahya' refers to the father and maternal aunt of Prophet Yusuf (peace be upon him). This also indicates the right of the maternal aunt. Which women are entitled to custody in order? And the full sister from father and mother is given precedence because she is more compassionate, then the uterine sister, then the consanguine sister, because the right for them is from the mother's side. Then maternal aunts are given precedence over paternal aunts, giving preference to maternal lineage. And they descend in degrees as we descended the sisters. Meaning: preference for the one with two relations, then maternal lineage, then paternal aunts descend likewise. Translation: And the sister from both father and mother is given precedence over other sisters because her compassion is greater. Then the sister from only the mother. Then the sister from only the father. Because the right of these women is from the mother's side. Then maternal aunts are given precedence over paternal aunts because maternal lineage is preferred. Then maternal aunts descend in degrees as we descended the sisters. That is, the one with two relations is given preference (over one relation), then the one from the mother, then paternal aunts descend like maternal aunts. Explanation: The issue is that a woman who has two types of relation is more entitled than one with one relation. Thus, it is said that the full sister—i.e., from both father and mother—is given precedence over other sisters, i.e., only uterine and only consanguine. Because the full sister's compassion is greater than that of other sisters, so she is preferred. Then the uterine sister is preferred over the consanguine sister, because the right of sisters comes from the mother's side. For this reason, the uterine sister is preferred over the consanguine sister. Imam Zufar said that the full sister and the uterine sister are equal in custody; no one is preferred over the other. Then maternal aunts are given precedence over paternal aunts because the maternal aunt has relation to the mother, not the paternal aunt. And in custody, maternal lineage is preferred, not paternal lineage. Then maternal aunts are placed in degrees in the same way as we described for sisters. That is, the child's maternal aunt who is his mother's full sister (from same father and mother) is the highest, then his mother's uterine sister, then his mother's consanguine sister. The conclusion is that the one with two relations is preferred over the one with one relation, then maternal lineage is preferred over paternal lineage, then similarly by degrees for paternal aunts: the father's full sister is given precedence, then the father's uterine sister, then the father's consanguine sister.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi ranking of female custodians for a child. It begins by noting a conflict in al-Mabsut: the Kitab al-Nikah gives precedence to sisters over aunts due to closer blood relation, while Kitab al-Talaq gives precedence to the maternal aunt over the consanguine sister because of closeness to the mother. The author then cites the well-known hadith of the dispute over Hamzah's daughter, in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) awarded custody to the maternal aunt, saying 'the maternal aunt is in the position of the mother.' This hadith establishes the maternal aunt's superiority over paternal relatives. The core ruling then lists the order: first, the full sister (from both parents) because she has dual relation and greater compassion; second, the uterine sister (from mother only); third, the consanguine sister (from father only). This order is based on the principle that the right of custody for sisters comes from the mother's side. Then maternal aunts are preferred over paternal aunts, again prioritizing maternal lineage. Within each category, those with two relations (closer to the child) precede those with one. The commentary mentions Imam Zufar's dissenting opinion that the full sister and uterine sister are equal. This intra-Hanafi dispute does not affect the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, which is the ordered ranking given by the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The passage also grades the aunts similarly: the child's maternal aunt who is his mother's full sister is first, then uterine, then consanguine; likewise for paternal aunts. The entire ranking prioritizes maternal lineage and closeness of relation.

Key Terms
حضانة (hadanah): The right and duty of a female relative to physically care for and raise a young child in her home.
الاخت لاب وام (al-ukht li-ab wa umm): Full sister: sister sharing both father and mother with the child.
خالة (khalah): Maternal aunt: the sister of the child's mother.
عمه (ammah): Paternal aunt: the sister of the child's father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ranking of female custodians, who comes after the full sister?
A) The consanguine sister
B) The uterine sister
C) The maternal aunt
D) The paternal aunt

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of female custodians prioritises closeness of relation and maternal lineage, with the full sister at the top, followed by uterine sister, consanguine sister, then maternal aunts, and finally paternal aunts.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Marriage and Custody: The Rule and Its Exception
Ruling on marriage of female custodian and its effect on custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a female custodian loses custody upon marriage to a non-mahram, identify the exception when the husband is a mahram, and explain how the right is restored.

Core Idea
Marriage to a non-mahram terminates custody; marriage to a mahram preserves it.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a critical question in Hanafi family law: Does a female custodian lose her right to custody when she marries? The answer is nuanced: generally yes, but with a key exception when the new husband is a mahram relative of the child. The ruling is supported by a hadith and a rational argument about the stepfather's likely lack of compassion. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly determining custody arrangements after remarriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the marriage of a female custodian. The ruling: her right to custody falls (saqit), except when the husband is a mahram.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text cites two proofs: (1) the hadith 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry'; (2) a rational argument that a non-mahram stepfather will not care for the child properly.
The hadith is the primary textual evidence; the rational argument serves as a supporting explanation (talil).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly makes marriage a terminating condition for the mother. By analogy (qiyas), the same applies to all female custodians because the underlying reason (illah) – lack of compassion from a non-mahram stepfather – is common to all.
4
Note the exception
When the custodian marries a mahram of the child (e.g., grandfather), her right is preserved because natural compassion exists due to close blood relation.
The mahram relationship must be based on blood or fosterage; not all relatives are mahram.
5
Note the restoration of right
If the right falls due to marriage, it returns when the marriage ends (by divorce or death) because the impediment (marriage) is removed.
Restoration occurs automatically; no new court order needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ان عورتوں کا حق حضانت کب ساقط ہوتا ہے
وكل من تزوجت من هؤلاء يسقط حقها لماروينا ولان زوج الام اذا كان اجنبيا يعطيه نزرا وينظر اليه شزر افلا نظر قال الا الجدة اذاكان زوجها الجدلانه قام مقام ابيه فينظر له و کذالک کل زوج هو ذو رحم محرم منه لقيام الشفقة نظرا الى القرابة القريبة ومن سقط حقها بالتزوج يعود اذا ارتفعت الزوجية لان المانع قد زال ترجمہ اور ان عورتوں میں سے ہر وہ عورت جس نے اپنا نکاح کر لیا ہو اس کا حق ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم روایت کر چکے۔ اور اس لئے کہ جب ماں کا شو ہر اجنبی ہے تو وہ اس کو حقیر چیز دے گا ۔ اور اس کو تیز نگاہ سے دیکھے گا۔ تو (بچہ کے حق میں ) کوئی نگہداشت نہیں ہے۔ سوائے نانی کے جبکہ اس کا شوہر ( بچہ کا ) دادا ہو۔ کیونکہ دادا بچہ کے باپ کے قائم مقام ہے۔ پس اس پر نظر شفقت رکھے گا ۔ اور یہی حال ہر ایسے شوہر کا ہے جو اس بچہ کا ذور تم محرم ہو۔ کیونکہ قرابت قریبہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے شفقت موجود ہے اور جس عورت کا حق پرورش نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو گیا۔ تو جب بھی زوجیت دور ہو جائے (اس کا حق پرورش ) لوٹ آئے گا کیونکہ مانع دور ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جن عورتوں کو بچہ کی پرورش کرنے کا حق ہے۔ ان میں سے اگر کسی نے نکاح کر لیا تو اس کا حق پر ورش ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو سابق میں روایت کر چکے۔ یعنی حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بچہ کی ماں سے فرمایا تھا انت احق به مالم تتزوجی تو بچہ کی زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ جب تک تو نکاح نہ کرے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس بچہ کی ماں کا شوہر جب اجنبی مرد ہے تو وہ اس بچہ کو تھوڑی چیز دے گا۔ اور تیز نگاہ سے دیکھے گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ی شخص اس بچہ کی طرف کم التفات کرے گا۔ لہذا بچہ کو ان کی پرورش میں دینا اس کے حق میں کچھ نظر شفقت نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اگر اس بچہ کی نانی نے اپنا نکاح اس بچہ کے دادا سے کیا یا اس کی دادی نے اپنا نکاح بچہ کے نانا سے کیا تو اس نہانی یا دادی کا حق پرورش ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
When is the right of custody of these women lost? And every woman among these who marries, her right falls, due to what we have narrated, and because the husband of the mother, if he is a stranger, gives the child a scanty thing and looks at him with an angry glance, so there is no care. Except for the paternal grandmother (i.e., the child's mother's mother, the grandmother) if her husband is the child's father's father (i.e., the grandfather), because he stands in place of the child's father, so he will look upon him with compassion. Likewise, every husband who is a mahram (prohibited in marriage) to the child due to close kinship, because compassion exists considering the close relation. And the woman whose right has fallen due to marriage, it returns when the marital tie is removed because the impediment has ceased. Translation: And every woman among these who marries, her right will fall due to the hadith we have narrated, and because when the mother's husband is a stranger, he gives the child a scanty thing and looks at him with an angry glance, so there is no care. Except for the maternal grandmother when her husband is the child's paternal grandfather, because the grandfather stands in place of the child's father, so he will look upon him with compassion. And likewise every husband who is a mahram relative of the child, because compassion is present considering the close relation. And the woman whose right of custody has fallen due to marriage, when the marital tie is removed, her right returns because the impediment is gone. Explanation: The issue is that if any of the women who have the right to custody marries, her right to custody falls. The proof is the hadith we narrated earlier: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the child's mother: 'You are more entitled to him as long as you do not marry.' The second proof is that when the husband is a stranger, he will give the child a scanty thing and look at him with an angry glance. In short, that person will pay little attention to the child. Therefore, giving the child into their custody is not a compassionate look for the child. Yes, if the child's maternal grandmother marries the child's paternal grandfather, or the child's paternal grandmother marries the child's maternal grandfather, then the right of that grandmother is not lost.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the effect of marriage on the right of custody (hadanah). The ruling states that any female custodian who marries a man who is not a mahram to the child loses her right to custody. This is based on two proofs: (1) The hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told the mother 'You are more entitled to the child as long as you do not marry'—this explicitly makes marriage a bar. (2) Reason: a non-mahram husband (stranger) will not care for the child properly; he will give little and look angrily. The exception is when the custodian marries a mahram of the child, such as the maternal grandmother marrying the paternal grandfather, or vice versa, because the husband is a close relative who naturally shows compassion. The text also states that if the right falls due to marriage, it returns when the marriage ends (by divorce or death), because the impediment is removed. This ruling applies to all female custodians in the order mentioned previously.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim muharram): A male who is a mahram (unmarriageable kin) to the child due to blood relationship, such as grandfather, uncle, etc.
ساقط (saqit): To fall or become void; here, the right of custody is rendered null due to marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition does the right of a female custodian to custody NOT fall upon her marriage?
A) If she marries a wealthy man
B) If she marries a man who is a mahram to the child
C) If she marries with the child's father's permission
D) If she marries within the family

Key Takeaway
Marriage to a non-mahram terminates custody, but marriage to a mahram preserves it, and the right returns when the marriage ends.

Custody of a Girl: Mother's Right until Menstruation and the Age of Desire
Ruling on mother and grandmother's entitlement to custody of a girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on custody of a girl, explain the reasoning for the mother's priority, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad regarding the timing of transfer to the father.

Core Idea
A girl's custody shifts from mother to father at menstruation, but Imam Muhammad advances it to the age of desire for protection.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses the crucial question of custody of a young girl. The Hanafi school establishes that the mother (and grandmother) are primarily entitled to raise the girl until she reaches a stage where protection becomes paramount. The text presents the general rule, its rationale, and an important internal difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling and identify the entitled persons
Identify that the mother and grandmother are more entitled to custody of a girl. Note the duration: until she menstruates (or becomes independent).
The general rule is based on the need for feminine education.
2
Analyze the reasoning for mother's priority before menstruation
Understand the talil: before menstruation, the girl needs to learn feminine etiquettes (sewing, cooking, etc.). Women are more capable of teaching these. Also, presence with father may reduce modesty.
Modesty is considered a key adornment for women.
3
Analyze the reasoning for father's priority after puberty
After puberty (menstruation), the girl needs protection from fornication and arrangement of marriage. The father is stronger and more guiding in these matters.
The father is considered better for protective custody.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Muhammad holds that the girl should be given to the father when she reaches the age of desire (hadd al-shahwah), even if before menstruation. This is based on the need for protection from potential harm.
The age of desire varies according to jurists (6-11 years).
5
Determine the practical consequence and mufta bihi
The thamarah al-khilaf: if a girl reaches the age of desire before menstruation, Muhammad's view transfers custody earlier. Later Hanafi practice often follows Muhammad's view for protective reasons.
The mufta bihi in many contexts is the age-of-desire rule.

Chapter of custody of the child and who is more entitled. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume five. The mother and grandmother are more entitled to the girl until she menstruates, because after being in need of upbringing, she needs to learn the etiquettes of women, and the woman is more capable of that. And after puberty, she needs protection and preservation, and the father is stronger and more guiding in that. And from Muhammad: she is given to the father when she reaches the age of desire, due to the verification of the need for protection. Translation: And the mother and grandmother are more entitled in the upbringing of the girl until she menstruates, because after being independent from upbringing she needs to learn the etiquettes of women. And the woman is more capable of this task. And after reaching puberty (through marriage) she needs protection and preservation (from fornication). And the father has more strength and guidance in this matter. And it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that when the girl reaches the age of desire, she should be given to the father, because she needs protection. Commentary: Quduri said that the girl will remain in the upbringing of the mother and grandmother until the time of menstruation, because after being independent from upbringing, she needs to learn the etiquettes of women, such as spinning, sewing, threading, cooking, washing clothes. And the woman is more capable of these than the man, because if the girl is handed over to the father, due to mixing with men, her modesty will decrease, whereas modesty is the adornment of women. And after reaching puberty, she needs to be made protected through marriage and protected from fornication, and the father has more power and guidance in this matter. Therefore, after reaching puberty, the one most entitled to the girl is her father. And Hisham narrated from Imam Muhammad that when the girl reaches the age of desire, she will be handed over to the father, because now she needs protection. And there is disagreement among jurists regarding the age of desire: some hold that the age of desire is eleven years, and Faqih Abu al-Bath said it is nine years, and there is a saying about six years, and about seven years, and about eight years. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with evidence on the entitlement of the mother and grandmother to custody of a girl. The author begins by establishing the general rule: the mother and grandmother are more entitled to the custody of a girl until she menstruates. The reasoning provided is that before menstruation, the girl is not independent and needs to learn feminine etiquettes such as sewing, cooking, etc. Women are more capable of teaching these. After puberty and menstruation, the need shifts to protection from immoral acts and the need for marriage arrangement. The father is considered stronger and more capable in this regard. The passage also includes a narration from Imam Muhammad that once the girl reaches the age of desire (sexual awareness), she should be given to the father for protection. The commentator (Quduri) explains these points and notes a difference of opinion among jurists on what constitutes the age of desire, with estimates ranging from 6 to 11 years. This reflects an intra-madhhab variance within the Hanafi school. The overall ruling is that the mother/grandmother have custody of a girl from birth until the onset of menstruation or the age of desire, whichever comes first according to Imam Muhammad, after which the father takes over.

Key Terms
حضانة (zanah): The physical custody and upbringing of a young child, including care, education, and protection.
حد الشهوة (hadd al-shahwah): The age at which a girl becomes sexually desirable, i.e., attracts sexual attention. It is not a fixed age but varies by individual and societal context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mother retains custody of a girl until menstruation, but Imam Muhammad's protective view transfers custody at the age of desire, which is often adopted in practice.

Custody Duration for Female Relatives Other Than Mother and Grandmother
Ruling on custody duration for female relatives other than mother/grandmother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the duration of custody by female relatives other than mother and grandmother, and explain the legal reasoning based on the right to take service.

Core Idea
Non-mother/grandmother relatives lose custody once the girl can serve herself, because only mothers/grandmothers may lawfully take service.

Custody of a minor girl is not unlimited for all female relatives. While the mother and grandmother have extensive rights, other female relatives (like aunts and sisters) have a shorter period. This lesson clarifies that period according to two leading Hanafi authorities: Imam al-Quduri and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The key distinction hinges on the legal right to take service (khidma) from the child, which only the mother and grandmother possess.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two markers
Locate the two opinions in the text: Quduri says custody ends when the girl reaches 'the age of desire' (bulugh al-shahwa), while Imam Muhammad says it ends when she is 'independent' (mustaghniya), meaning she can eat and dress alone.
These markers are not identical; independence usually occurs earlier than puberty.
2
Understand the right to take service
Read why the custodian's inability to take service is central. The text states that non-mother/grandmother women cannot legally take service from the girl because she is not a mahram, nor can they hire her out. This defeats the purpose of custody, which includes teaching feminine etiquettes through some reciprocal service.
The right to take service is established by sharia for mothers and grandmothers only.
3
Trace the reasoning (ta'lil)
The argument is: if the custodian cannot lawfully benefit from the girl's service after a certain age, then keeping the girl with her no longer serves the objective (teaching etiquette). Therefore, custody must transfer to the father or a mahram guardian who can oversee her until marriage.
This is a purposive interpretation: custody aims at the child's welfare and training.
4
Apply the rule to a scenario
Given a girl aged 6 who can dress herself but is not yet pubescent, under Quduri's view custody continues; under Imam Muhammad's view custody ends immediately. Determine the practical outcome for the girl's living arrangement.
The mufta bihi generally follows Imam Muhammad's view for caution and welfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

و من سوى الام والجدة احق بالجارية حتى تبلغ حداتشتهى وفى الجامع الصغير حتى تستغنى لانها لا تقدر على استخد امها وهذا لا تواجرها للخدامة فلا يحصل المقصود بخلاف الام والجدة لقدر تهما عليه شرعا
ترجمہ اور ماں اور نانی کے علاوہ (باقی عورتیں ) صغیرہ لڑکی کی پرورش میں اس حد تک حقدار ہیں کہ لڑکی مردوں کی خواہش کے قابل ہو جائے ۔ اور جامع صغیرہ میں ہے کہ وہ ( دوسرے کی مدد گاری سے مستغنی ہو جائے کیونکہ ماں اور نانی کے علاوہ کوئی عورت اس لڑکی سے خدمت لینے پر قادر نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے اس لڑکی کو خدمت کے لئے اجارہ اور نوکری پر نہیں دے سکتی تو مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ برخلاف ماں اور نانی کے۔ اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں شرعا خدمت لینے پر قادر ہیں۔ تشریح شیخ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ صغیرہ کو ماں اور نانی اور دادی کے علاوہ دوسری عورتوں کے پاس حد شہوت کو پہنچنے تک رکھا جاسکتا ہے
اور امام محمد نے جامع صغیرہ میں فرمایا کہ صغیرہ کو ماں اور نانی ، دادی کے علاوہ کے پاس اتنی مدت رکھا جائے کہ وہ صغیرہ دوسرے کی مدد کی محتاج نہ رہے۔ یعنی اکیلی کھا سکے اور اکیلی پہن سکے۔ کیونکہ صغیرہ اگر چہ عورتوں کے آداب سیکھنے کی محتاج ہے۔ لیکن آداب سکھانے میں صغیرہ سے ایک گونہ خدمت لینا پڑتا ہے۔ اور ماں اور نانی، دادی کے علاوہ کو شرعاً خدمت لینے کا حق نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ لڑکی کو خدمت کے لئے اجرت پر دینا ممنوع ہے۔ پس اگر حد شہوت کو پہنچنے کے بعد لڑکی کو ماں اور نانی ، دادی کے علاوہ کے پاس چھوڑا گیا تو مقصود ( آداب سکھانا ) حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔
اس کے برخلاف ماں اور نانی ، دادی کہ ان کے پاس لڑکی کو چھوڑا جا سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ ماں اور نانی لڑکی سے خدمت لینے پر شرعاً
قادر ہے۔
For how long does a woman other than mother and grandmother have the right of custody? And whoever is other than the mother and grandmother is more entitled to the girl until she reaches the age of desire, and in al-Jami' al-Saghir, until she is independent (of help), because she (the custodian) is not able to take service from her, and she cannot hire her out as a servant, so the objective is not achieved, unlike the mother and grandmother, because they are able to do so legally. Translation: And women other than the mother and grandmother (other female relatives) are entitled to the custody of the minor girl to the extent that the girl becomes desirable to men. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir, it is that she becomes independent (from needing others' help), because no woman other than the mother and grandmother is able to take service from this girl. And for this reason, she cannot give this girl for hire for service, so the objective will not be achieved. Unlike the mother and grandmother, because these two are legally capable of taking service. Commentary: Sheikh Quduri said that the minor girl can be kept with women other than mother, grandmother, and paternal grandmother until she reaches the age of desire. And Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir that the minor girl should be kept with those other than mother, grandmother, and paternal grandmother for a period until the minor girl is not in need of help from others, i.e., she can eat alone and dress alone. Because although the minor girl needs to learn feminine etiquettes, in teaching etiquettes, some service is taken from the minor girl. And besides mother, grandmother, and paternal grandmother, no one legally has the right to take service. This is why it is prohibited to give the girl for hire for service. So if after reaching the age of desire the girl is left with someone other than mother, grandmother, and paternal grandmother, the objective (teaching etiquettes) will not be achieved. In contrast, with mother, grandmother, and paternal grandmother, the girl can be left, because the mother and grandmother are legally capable of taking service from the girl.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage deals with the custody rights of female relatives other than the mother and grandmother. The rule stated is that such women (e.g., aunts, sisters) have the right to custody of a girl only until the girl reaches the age of desire or becomes independent (able to eat and dress alone). The reasoning is that these non-mahram women cannot lawfully take service from the girl, nor can they hire her out for service, unlike the mother and grandmother who are permitted to take service from their children/grandchildren. The commentator notes two views: Quduri's view that custody ends at the age of desire, and Imam Muhammad's view in al-Jami' al-Saghir that it ends when the girl becomes independent of help. The consequence is that once the girl reaches that stage, she must be transferred to the father or a suitable guardian. The underlying rationale is that the purpose of custody (teaching feminine skills) cannot be achieved without some reciprocal service, which only the mother and grandmother can lawfully require.

Key Terms
خدمة (khidma): Service or assistance in household chores; the right of the mother to take service from her child is recognized by sharia.
استغناء (istighna'): Independence from needing help; in this context, the girl can eat and dress without assistance.
حد الشهوة (hadd al-shahwa): The age of desire; puberty or the age when the girl becomes desirable to men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Until the girl reaches the age of desire
C) Until the girl becomes independent (can eat and dress alone)
D) Until the girl gets married

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits custody by non-mother/grandmother female relatives to the period before the girl reaches independence or the age of desire, based on the custodian's inability to legally take service.

Custody Rights of Freed Slave Women and Umm Walad
Ruling on the custody right of a freed slave woman and umm walad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a slave woman or umm walad gains custody rights and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind it.

Core Idea
A freed slave woman or umm walad gains full custody rights because at the moment of claim she is free.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in family law: the custody rights of a slave woman or umm walad after being freed by the master. The Hanafi school rules that once freed, they have the same rights as a free woman. This lesson explains the condition for the right to arise and the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and their statuses
Recognize that the ruling concerns a slave woman (ama) or an umm walad (slave mother of the master's child) who has been freed by her master. The child is from her marriage to another man.
The umm walad is a specific category of slave woman who has a child from the master.
2
Determine the time of the right's establishment
The right of custody (hidana) is not automatic at birth; it is established at the time of the claim or when custody becomes an issue. The status of the mother at that moment is decisive.
The text emphasizes 'at the time of the establishment of the right' (hina thubut al-haqq).
3
Apply the rule: freedom at that time gives full rights
If the mother is free at the moment the right is established, she has the same right to custody as any free woman. The master's previous ownership does not affect her claim after freedom.
The reasoning (ta'lil) is that she is no longer occupied with the master's service, so she can fulfill the duties of custody.
4
Note the pre-freedom ineligibility
Before being freed, the slave woman or umm walad has no right to custody because her time is dedicated to serving the master, making her unable to care for the child.
This is consistent with the general principle that custody requires capability and availability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باندی کو جب اس کے مولیٰ نے آزاد کر دیا اور ام ولدہ جب آزاد کر دی گئی ولد کی پرورش میں آزاد عورت کی طرح ہیں
قال والامة اذا اعتقها مولاها وام الولد اذا اعتقت كالحرة فى حق الولد لا نهما جرتان او ان ثبوت الحق وليس لهما قبل العتق حق فى الولد لعجزهما عن الحضانة بالاشتغال بخدمة المولى
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا باندی کو جب اس کے مولیٰ نے آزاد کر دیا اور ام ولد جب آزاد کر دی گئی تو بچہ کے حق میں آزاد عورت کے مانند ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ حق ثابت ہونے کے وقت یہ دونوں بھی آزاد ہیں۔ اور آزاد ہونے سے پہلے ان دونوں کا بچہ کی ( پرورش ) میں کوئی حق نہیں ہے کیونکہ مولیٰ کی خدمت میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ دونوں پرورش کرنے سے عاجز ہیں۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر باندی کو اس کے مولیٰ نے آزاد کر دیا اور جب ام ولد آزاد کر دی گئی ۔ تو بچہ کی پرورش میں ان کا حق بھی آزاد عورت کے مانند ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مولیٰ نے اپنی باندی کا کسی مرد سے نکاح کیا۔ اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا۔ پھر موٹی نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو اس بچہ کی پرورش کرنے کی زیادہ حقدار اس کی یہ ماں ہوگی۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ پرورش کرنے کا حق ثابت ہونے کے وقت یہ دونوں آزاد ہیں۔ لہذا اپنے مولی کے مقابلہ میں یہ دونوں بچہ کی پرورش کرنے کی زیادہ حقدار ہوں گی۔ اور آزاد ہونے سے پہلے باندی اور ام ولد بچہ کی پرورش میں کوئی حق نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں مولی کی خدمت میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے بچہ کی پرورش کرنے سے عاجز ہیں یہی قول امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا ہے۔
The slave woman when her master frees her and the umm walad when she is freed are like the free woman concerning the child, because at the time of the establishment of the right, both are free. And they have no right over the child before being freed, due to their inability to take care of the child because of being busy with the service of the master. Translation: Quduri said: When a slave woman is freed by her master and when an umm walad is freed, they are like a free woman regarding the child. Because at the time the right is established, both are free. And before being freed, these two have no right to the upbringing of the child, because due to being busy with the service of the master, they are unable to provide custody. Commentary: The issue is that if a master marries his slave woman to a man, and she has a child from him, then the master frees her, then this mother becomes more entitled to the custody of that child. The evidence is that at the time the right of custody is established, both are free. Therefore, in competition with their master, these two will be more entitled to custody. And before freedom, a slave woman and umm walad have no right to custody because they are occupied with the master's service. This is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage addresses the custody rights of a slave woman and an umm walad (a slave woman who has borne a child to her master). The ruling is that once they are freed, they have the same right to custody of their child as a free woman. The reasoning is that the right of custody is established at the time of claim, and at that time they are free. Before being freed, they have no right because their time is occupied with the master's service, making them unable to fulfill the duties of custody. The text also notes that this ruling is agreed upon by al-Shafi'i and Ahmad. The practical scenario is that if a master marries his slave woman to another man, and she has a child, then later the master frees her, she becomes more entitled to custody than anyone else. The master has no competing right.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who has given birth to a child from her master.
حضانہ (hidana): Custody or upbringing of a child, primarily the right of the mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) After the child reaches a certain age
C) After she is freed by her master
D) Only if the father agrees

Key Takeaway
A freed slave woman or umm walad has the same custody rights as a free woman, provided she is free at the time the right is claimed.

Custody of a Muslim Child by a Dhimmi Mother
Ruling on duration of dhimmi mother's custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a dhimmi mother's custody of her Muslim child and identify the condition that triggers transfer of custody.

Core Idea
A dhimmi mother retains custody of her Muslim child until the child discerns religions or there is fear of kufr influence.

This lesson addresses a sensitive intersection of custody law and religious identity. The Hanafi school balances the mother’s natural right of custody with the paramount need to protect the child’s Islamic faith. The ruling establishes a clear temporal limit based on the child’s religious awareness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize that the mother is a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Islamic rule) and the child is Muslim. This determines the applicable ruling.
2
State the default ruling
The dhimmi mother is entitled (ahaqq) to custody of her Muslim child. This is the starting point.
3
Identify the condition
The entitlement continues only as long as two conditions hold: the child does not yet understand religious differences, and there is no fear that the child will become accustomed to kufr.
Either condition triggers termination of custody.
4
Understand the talil (reasoning)
Before the threshold, the mother's care is based on compassion and benefits the child. After it, exposure to kufr poses probable harm to the child's faith.
The ruling is built on considering the child's best interest and religious protection.
5
Apply to practice
Once the child shows religious discernment or there is a tangible risk of kufr influence, custody must be transferred to a Muslim guardian, typically the father.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زمیہ اپنے مسلمان بچے کی خضانت کی کب تک مستحق ہے
والذمية احق بولدها المسلم مالم يعقل الاديان او يخاف ان يالف الكفر للنظر قبل ذالك و احتمال الضرر بعده
ترجمہ اور زمیہ عورت اپنے مسلمان بچہ کی زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ تا وقتیکہ بچہ دینوں کو نہ پہچانے یا یہ خوف نہ ہو کہ وہ کفر سے مانوس ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس سے بچہ کے حق میں ) نظر شفقت ہے۔ اور اس کے بعد ضرر کا احتمال ہے۔
For how long is a dhimmi woman entitled to the custody of her Muslim child? And the dhimmi woman is more entitled to her Muslim child as long as he does not comprehend the religions, or unless it is feared that he will become accustomed to disbelief, because before that there is kindly consideration (for the child), and after that there is probability of harm. Translation: And a dhimmi woman is more entitled to her Muslim child until the child does not recognize the different religions or until it is not feared that he will become accustomed to disbelief. Because before that, there is compassion for the child, but after that, there is possibility of harm.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage deals with the specific situation where the mother is a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Islamic state) and the child is Muslim (presumably because the father is Muslim). The ruling is that the mother has custody of the child as long as the child does not yet comprehend religious differences, or as long as there is no fear that the child will become accustomed to disbelief. The reasoning is that before this point, the mother's care is based on compassion and is beneficial for the child. After this point, there is a risk that the child may be influenced towards kufr (disbelief), so custody should be transferred to a Muslim guardian (like the father). This ruling protects the child's Islamic identity.

Key Terms
ذمية (dhimmī): A non-Muslim woman living under Islamic rule, protected by the state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi mother may retain custody of her Muslim child only until the child can distinguish religions or there is fear of kufr influence — after that, custody must transfer to a Muslim guardian.

Duration for Leaving a Young Girl with Non-Mahram Guardians
States the ruling on custodial duration for a young girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how long a young girl may be left with non-mahram female guardians and explain the rational basis (self-sufficiency and prohibition of taking service).

Core Idea
A young girl may be left with non-mahram guardians only until she can eat and dress alone.

Custody (حضانة) law answers the question of who may care for a child and under what conditions. This passage from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir addresses a specific sub-issue: for how long may a young girl be placed with a female guardian who is not her mother or grandmother? The ruling hinges on the girl's independence and the guardian's right to take service from her.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is placing a young girl (صغیرہ) in the custody of a female guardian other than her mother or maternal/paternal grandmothers. Determine the legal limit on the duration of such placement.
2
State the ruling from Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad rules: the girl may be left with such a guardian only for as long as she does not need someone else's help with basic tasks—specifically, she can eat and dress herself.
The ruling is from al-Jami' al-Saghir, a core Zahir al-Riwayah text.
3
Understand the rational basis (dalil aqli)
The reasoning is teleological: the purpose of leaving the girl with the guardian is to teach her manners. Teaching requires taking some service from the girl (e.g., helping around). However, Shariah grants the right to take service from the girl only to the mother and grandmothers; others may not take service. If the girl cannot serve, the teaching purpose is defeated.
This is a rational proof based on the prohibition of hiring out a girl for service and the limited right to take service.
4
Identify the threshold: hadd al-shahwa
The text refers to 'حد شہوت'—the age at which a girl begins to experience sexual desires. Once she reaches this age, she cannot be left with non-mahram guardians because the purpose (teaching) cannot be achieved without service, which is forbidden to them.
This age is not numerically defined; it is assessed individually.
5
Note the exception for mother and grandmothers
The mother and both grandmothers (paternal and maternal) are exempted because they have the legal right to take service from the girl, thus they can continue to teach her even after she reaches hadd al-shahwa.
This exception confirms the general rule.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد اور امام محمد نے جامع صغیرہ میں فرمایا کہ صغیرہ کو ماں اور نانی ، دادی کے علاوہ کے پاس اتنی مدت رکھا جائے کہ وہ صغیرہ دوسرے کی مدد کی محتاج نہ رہے۔ یعنی اکیلی کھا سکے اور اکیلی پہن سکے۔ کیونکہ صغیرہ اگر چہ عورتوں کے آداب سیکھنے کی محتاج ہے۔ لیکن آداب سکھانے میں صغیرہ سے ایک گونہ خدمت لینا پڑتا ہے۔ اور ماں اور نانی، دادی کے علاوہ کو شرعاً خدمت لینے کا حق نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ لڑکی کو خدمت کے لئے اجرت پر دینا ممنوع ہے۔ پس اگر حد شہوت کو پہنچنے کے بعد لڑکی کو ماں اور نانی ، دادی کے علاوہ کے پاس چھوڑا گیا تو مقصود ( آداب سکھانا ) حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔

Chapter on custody of the child and who is more entitled to it. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah. And Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A young girl is to be kept with someone other than her mother, paternal grandmother, and maternal grandmother only as long as that young girl does not need someone else's help. Meaning she can eat alone and she can wear clothes alone. Because the young girl, although she needs to learn the manners of women, however, in teaching manners, some service has to be taken from the young girl. And for someone other than mother and grandmothers, it is not legally permissible to take service from her. This is the reason that it is prohibited to hire out a girl for service. So if after reaching the age of desire, a girl is left with someone other than mother and grandmothers, the purpose (teaching manners) will not be achieved. On the contrary, a girl can be left with mother and grandmothers because mother and grandmothers are legally able to take service from the girl.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on custody (حضانہ). It presents a ruling from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding the appropriate duration for a young girl to be placed in the care of female relatives who are not her mother or grandmothers (maternal and paternal). The criterion is that the girl must be self-sufficient in eating and dressing. The reason is that teaching proper manners requires the guardian to take some service from the girl, and only the mother and grandmothers have the legal right (shar'an) to take such service. Others are not permitted to take service, and it is even prohibited to hire out a girl for service. Therefore, if a girl has reached the age of sexual desire (سن شہوت), she cannot be left with others, as the objective of teaching manners would be lost. The exception is the mother and grandmothers, who can take service from the girl and thus can properly instruct her.

Key Terms
حد شہوت (hadd al-shahwa): The age at which a girl begins to experience sexual desires, which is the threshold beyond which she cannot be left with non-mahram custodians who are not her mother or grandmothers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A young girl may only be left with non-mahram female guardians as long as she is self-sufficient in eating and dressing; the right to take service from her belongs exclusively to her mother and grandmothers.

Custody Right of a Dhimmī Mother over Her Muslim Child
Ruling on dhimmī mother's custody duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a dhimmī mother retains custody of her Muslim child and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A dhimmī mother has custody of her Muslim child only until the child is capable of religious discernment.

This passage addresses a nuanced family law scenario: the child of a Muslim father and a Kitābiyya mother is Muslim, but the mother's custody right is recognized for a limited period. The ruling balances maternal care with the child's religious welfare, using a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) based on benefit and harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the legal question
The case involves a Muslim father, a dhimmī (Kitābiyya) mother, and their child. Determine who is entitled to custody (ḥaḍāna) and for how long.
The child follows the better religion, i.e., Islam.
2
State the ruling and its condition
The mother is entitled to custody as long as two conditions hold: (1) the child does not yet understand religions, and (2) there is no fear that the child will become accustomed to kufr. If either condition is breached, custody transfers to the father.
These conditions are cumulative; both must be satisfied.
3
Extract the proof (dalīl)
The author provides a rational proof: before the child attains religious discernment, leaving him with the mother is compassionate (naẓar shafaqa); after that, there is potential harm (iḥtimāl al-ḍarar) to his faith.
This is a dalīl ʿaqlī (rational proof), not a textual one.
4
Analyze the legal reasoning (taʿlīl)
The ruling is based on the welfare (maṣlaḥa) of the child: the mother's care is beneficial when the child is young, but the risk of religious corruption overrides that benefit once the child can understand.
The principle of preventing harm (darʾ al-mafāsid) takes precedence.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Consider a scenario: the child is four years old, does not know about religion, and the mother is a practicing Christian but does not teach the child her faith. The custody condition is satisfied. If the child starts asking about religion or the mother begins to teach Christianity, custody transfers.
The exact age is not specified; it depends on the child's understanding.

Source Text

تشریح مسئلہ ! اگر کسی مسلمان مرد نے کسی زمیہ کتابیہ عورت سے نکاح کیا۔ پھر اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا تو یہ بچہ خیر الا بوین دینا یعنی مسلمان باپ کے تابع ہو کر مسلمان ہوگا۔ مگر اس کی پرورش کرنے کی زیادہ ستحق اس کی ذمیہ ماں ہوگی لیکن یہ استحقاق زمیہ کے واسطے اس وقت تک ہو گا جب تک کہ بچہ میں دین کی سمجھ نہ ہو۔ اور بچہ کے کفر سے مانوس ہونے کا ڈر نہ ہو۔ اور جب بچہ دین و مذہب کو سمجھنے لگے۔ یا بچے کے کفر سے مانوس ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو تو ایسی حالت میں بچہ کی پرورش کرنے کی مستحق زمیہ عورت نہیں ہوگی ۔

How long is a dhimmī woman entitled to custody of her Muslim child? The dhimmī woman is more entitled to her Muslim child as long as the child does not understand religions, or it is not feared that he will become accustomed to kufr, because before that there is compassion (in leaving him with her), and after that there is potential harm. Translation: A dhimmī woman is more entitled to her Muslim child until the child does not recognize the religions, or there is no fear that he will become accustomed to kufr, because before that there is compassion towards the child, and after that there is possibility of harm. Explanation of the issue: If a Muslim man marries a dhimmī Kitābiyya woman, then a child is born, this child follows the better of the parents, meaning he becomes a Muslim following the Muslim father. However, his dhimmī mother is more entitled to his custody, but this entitlement is for the dhimmī only as long as the child does not have understanding of religion, and there is no fear of him becoming accustomed to kufr. When the child begins to understand religion, or there is fear of him becoming accustomed to kufr, then in such a situation the dhimmī woman is not entitled to custody. The proof is that before this state, entrusting the child to the dhimmī is compassionate, and after this state there is possibility of harm. Therefore, when the child begins to understand religion, he is taken from the dhimmī and given to the Muslim father.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: a Muslim man marries a Jewish or Christian (Kitābiyya) woman, and they have a child. The child is Muslim by virtue of following the better religion (Islam) of the father. The mother, being dhimmī, has the initial right to custody as long as the child is too young to understand religious matters and there is no risk of the child becoming accustomed to kufr. Once the child reaches an age where he can understand religion, or if there is a fear that he will be influenced towards kufr, the mother loses her custody right and the father becomes entitled. The reasoning is based on consideration of the child's welfare: before that age, the mother's care is compassionate and beneficial; after that, there is a risk of spiritual harm.

Key Terms
ذمیہ (dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject of the Islamic state who has a covenant (dhimma) guaranteeing protection and religious freedom.
خضانت (ḥaḍāna): Custody of a child, including physical care and upbringing.
کتابیہ (Kitābiyya): A woman from the People of the Book (Jews/Christians).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) At birth

Key Takeaway
A dhimmī mother's custody of her Muslim child is conditional on the child's religious naivety and absence of kufr risk; once either condition fails, the right transfers to the Muslim father.

Dispute on Whether the Child Has Choice Between Parents in Custody
Hanafi view rebuts Shafi'i view on child's choice in custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on child's choice in custody and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument by analysing the hadith of Rafi' bin Sinan.

Core Idea
A child's immature intellect disqualifies him from choosing custody; the Hanafi school prioritizes welfare over preference.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does a child have the right to choose between parents in custody? Imam al-Shafi'i invokes a Prophetic hadith where a child was given a choice. The Hanafi school counters by analyzing the child's limited capacity and reinterpreting the hadith. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate textual evidence and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to the matn, the boy and girl have no choice (la khiyar). Confirm that the Hanafi school does not grant the child the right to choose.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a child who has reached the age of discrimination (tamyeez) may choose between parents.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith of Rafi' bin Sinan: a girl initially leaned to her mother, but after the Prophet's du'a she chose her father. Al-Shafi'i uses this as evidence that a child can choose.
The hadith is quoted in the source.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the child's weak intellect leads to choosing immediate comfort, not true welfare. The hadith is explained as a special case where the Prophet's prayer guided the child, or it applies to a mature (baligh) child. Also, the Companions did not give children a choice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi fiqh, custody is determined by legal priority without child's vote. In Shafi'i fiqh, a mumayyiz child can choose.

رافع بن سنان انه اسلم وایت امرته ان تسلم فانت النبي فقالت ابنتى وهى فطیم و قال رافع ابنتی فقال النبى اقعد ناحية و قال لها اقعدى ناحية فاقعد الصبية بينهما ثم قال ادعواها فمالت الصبية الى امها فقال النبى اللهم اهدها فمالت الى ابيها فاخذها
And the boy and girl have no choice. Al-Shafi'i said: they have a choice because the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave them a choice. Our proof is that due to his weak intellect, the child will choose the one with whom he finds comfort, because leaving him free between himself and play, so due consideration (of welfare) is not actualized. And it is correct that the Companions did not give children a choice. As for the hadith, we say: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'O Allah, guide him,' so he was guided to a proper choice by his prayer, or the hadith is interpreted for a child who has reached puberty. Explanation: The issue is that a boy and girl have no choice themselves. That is, it will not happen that the boy and girl are given the choice to prefer one of the parents. Al-Shafi'i said: when the boy and girl reach the age of discrimination (tamyeez), they will be entrusted to whomever they choose. Al-Shafi'i's proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a boy the choice to choose between his parents, and it is narrated: Rafi' bin Sinan embraced Islam, and his wife refused to embrace Islam, so she came to the Prophet and said, 'My daughter is weaned,' and Rafi' said, 'My daughter.' The Prophet said, 'Sit aside,' and said to her, 'Sit aside,' so the girl sat between them. Then he said, 'Call her,' so the girl leaned towards her mother, then the Prophet said, 'O Allah, guide her,' so she leaned towards her father, so he took her.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether a child can choose between parents in custody matters. The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that a child has no choice (la khiyar). Imam al-Shafi'i argues for the child's right to choose, citing a hadith where the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) gave a child a choice. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, the child's limited intellect means he will choose based on immediate comfort and play, not true welfare; second, the hadith is interpreted as a special case where the Prophet's prayer (du'a) guided the child to the right choice, or it applies when the child has reached puberty. Additionally, the practice of the Companions (sahaba) did not include giving children a choice. The text provides the story of Rafi' bin Sinan (Radiyallahu anhu) as the basis of the Shafi'i proof. The Hanafis respond by pointing out that the outcome was determined by the Prophet's du'a, not the child's independent choice.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): In this context, it means the child's right to choose between parents in custody matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject the child's right to choose in custody?
A) The child is too young
B) The child's limited intellect leads him to choose based on immediate pleasure not welfare
C) The parents have equal rights
D) The hadith is weak

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a child's immature judgment prevents him from having a choice in custody; the decision rests on legal priority and welfare, not preference.

Custody of Child from a Dhimmi Mother
Ruling on custody when mother is a dhimmi and father Muslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on custody when the mother is a dhimmi and identify the condition that terminates her custody right.

Core Idea
A dhimmi mother has custody until her child understands religion or faces religious harm.

This passage addresses a delicate scenario: when a Muslim father and a dhimmi mother have a child. The Hanafi school recognizes the mother's right to custody during early childhood based on welfare (maslahah), but protects the child's faith by transferring custody to the father once religious discernment or risk arises. The ruling is based on the principle of preventing harm (dar' al-mafasid).

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their religions
A Muslim man married a dhimmi kitabiyya woman. Their child follows the better religion, i.e., Islam due to the father.
2
Determine the default custody holder
The dhimmi mother is more entitled to custody initially, despite being non-Muslim.
3
Identify the condition for the mother's entitlement
The child must not yet understand religion, and there must be no fear of the child becoming accustomed to kufr.
Two conditions must both be satisfied.
4
Identify the event that ends the mother's entitlement
When the child begins to understand religion, or if there is fear of religious corruption, the mother loses custody and it transfers to the Muslim father.
Either condition triggers the transfer.
5
Understand the rational proof (dalil 'aqli)
Before the threshold, entrusting the child to the mother is kindness (benefit). After, there is potential harm (corruption of faith). The ruling balances benefit and harm.
This is a clear example of istihsan or maslahah in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حضانة الولد و من احق به
۲۲۴
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو برای جلد میانه تشریح مسئلہ ! اگر کسی مسلمان مرد نے کسی زمیہ کتابیہ عورت سے نکاح کیا۔ پھر اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا تو یہ بچہ خیر الا بوین دینا یعنی مسلمان باپ کے تابع ہو کر مسلمان ہوگا۔ مگر اس کی پرورش کرنے کی زیادہ ستحق اس کی ذمیہ ماں ہوگی لیکن یہ استحقاق زمیہ کے واسطے اس وقت تک ہو گا جب تک کہ بچہ میں دین کی سمجھ نہ ہو۔ اور بچہ کے کفر سے مانوس ہونے کا ڈر نہ ہو۔ اور جب بچہ دین و مذہب کو سمجھنے لگے۔ یا بچے کے کفر سے مانوس ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو تو ایسی حالت میں بچہ کی پرورش کرنے کی مستحق زمیہ عورت نہیں ہوگی ۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس حالت سے پہلے بچہ کو زمیہ کے سپرد کرنے میں اس پر شفقت ہے۔ اور اس حالت کے بعد ضرر کا احتمال ہے۔ اس لئے بچہ جب دین کو سمجھنے لگے تو اس کو زمیہ سے لیکر مسلمان باپ کو دیدیا جائے۔
Chapter of custody of the child and who is more entitled to it. Explanation of the issue: If a Muslim man married a dhimmi kitabiyya woman, then a child was born, this child follows the better of the two parents in religion, i.e., becomes Muslim following the Muslim father. But the mother (dhimmi) is more entitled to his upbringing. However, this entitlement for the dhimmi is only as long as the child has no understanding of religion and there is no fear of the child becoming accustomed to disbelief. And when the child begins to understand religion, or there is fear of the child becoming accustomed to disbelief, then in such a state the dhimmi woman is not entitled to raise the child. The proof is that before this state, entrusting the child to the dhimmi is kindness to him, and after this state, there is potential harm. Therefore, when the child begins to understand religion, he is taken from the dhimmi and given to the Muslim father.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi fiqh regarding custody (hadanah) when the parents are of different religions. The base ruling is that the child follows the better religion, meaning the child is Muslim because the father is Muslim. However, the mother, despite being a dhimmi, is entitled to custody as long as the child is too young to understand religious matters and there is no danger of the child being influenced towards kufr. The reasoning is that during this early stage, the mother's care is beneficial (maslahah) and there is no harm. Once the child attains discernment (tamyiz) regarding religion, the father takes precedence to protect the child's faith. This is based on the principle of dar' al-mafasid (preventing harm), which is a fundamental maxim in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حضانة (hadanah): The right and duty of raising and caring for a child, including physical care and education.
ذمیہ (dhimmiyyah): A non-Muslim woman living under the protection of the Islamic state, specifically from the People of the Book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi passage, when does a dhimmi mother lose her right to custody of her child from a Muslim father?
A) When the child turns seven years old
B) When the child understands religion and there is fear of corruption
C) When the father demands custody
D) When the mother remarries

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi mother has custody until the child understands religion or religious corruption is feared, based on balancing kindness and harm.

Definition of Nafaqa and Its Three Causes
Opening definition and classification of nafaqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of nafaqa and identify the three causes that make it obligatory.

Core Idea
Nafaqa is wajib due to marriage, lineage, or ownership — each with distinct conditions.

This passage opens the chapter on nafaqa in Ashraf al-Hidayah, connecting it to the prior chapter on custody. The author defines nafaqa both linguistically and technically, then lists the three causes of obligation: marriage (zawjiya), lineage (nasab), and ownership (milk). Understanding these causes is essential because each generates different rules regarding who must provide and who is entitled.

Guided Path
1
Define nafaqa technically
Identify the technical definition from the text: the daily sustenance that continues to maintain life. Note that it is a continuous obligation, not a one-time payment.
The term 'daily sustenance' (روز بینہ) implies regular provision.
2
Distinguish linguistic and technical meanings
The text says nafaqa is a verbal noun meaning spending (انفاق) generally, but in fiqh it is restricted to maintenance for survival.
This distinction is important to avoid confusing general spending with legal maintenance.
3
List the three causes
Extract the three causes: marriage (زوجیت), lineage (نسب), and ownership (ملک). Understand that each cause will be elaborated in the chapter.
These are not merely examples; they are the exhaustive grounds for nafaqa in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply the causes to scenarios
For each cause, think of a typical case: husband for wife (marriage), child for elderly parent (lineage), owner for slave or pet (ownership).
Conditions like poverty or ability to earn affect the obligation, but those are detailed later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النفقة
ترجمہ (یہ) باب نفقہ کے احکام کے بیان میں ) ہے۔
تشریح پہلے باب میں مصنف نے بچہ کی پرورش کرنے حق کو بیان فرمایا اور ان کو بیان فرمایا جن کے لئے پرورش کرنے کا حق ہے۔ اس سے فراغت کے بعد اس باب میں نفقہ کے احکام اور جن پر نفقہ واجب ہے ان کو بیان کریں گے۔ نفقہ اسم ہے انفاق کے معنی میں اور اصطلاح میں نفقہ وہ روز بینہ ہے جو زندگی باقی رکھنے کے واسطے برابر جاری رہے۔ اور نفقہ کا واجب ہونا چند اسباب سے ہوتا ہے۔ منجملہ ان میں سے زوجیت ہے نسب ہے اور ملک ہے۔ ہر ایک کا بیان بالترتیب مذکور ہے۔
Chapter of Nafaqa. Translation: (This) is a chapter on the rulings of nafaqa. Explanation: In the previous chapter, the author explained the right to raise the child and those for whom the right to raise exists. After finishing that, in this chapter he will explain the rulings of nafaqa and those upon whom nafaqa is obligatory. Nafaqa is a verbal noun in the meaning of spending. In technical terms, nafaqa is the daily sustenance that continues continuously to maintain life. The obligation of nafaqa occurs due to several causes: among them are marriage, lineage, and ownership. Each will be mentioned in order.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on alimony (nafaqa) in Ashraf al-Hidaya. The author connects it to the previous chapter on custody, indicating a logical progression from the child's upbringing to financial maintenance. He defines nafaqa both linguistically (as a verbal noun meaning spending) and technically (as daily sustenance necessary for life). The causes of obligation are three: marriage (zawjiya), where a husband must support his wife; lineage (nasab), where one must support certain relatives like parents and children; and ownership (milk), where one must provide for slaves or animals. These will be elaborated in order in the chapter. This definition sets the stage for detailed rulings on who is entitled to nafaqa and in what amount.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqa): Daily sustenance or maintenance required to preserve life; the financial support a person must provide to those entitled.
زوجیت (zawjiya): The marital relationship; a cause for obligation of nafaqa by husband to wife.
نسب (nasab): Blood relationship/lineage; a cause for obligation of nafaqa to certain relatives (e.g., parents, children).
ملک (milk): Ownership; a cause for obligation of nafaqa for owned persons (slaves) and animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A one-time payment to a divorced wife.
B) Daily sustenance that continues to maintain life.
C) A charitable donation to the poor.
D) A gift to relatives on special occasions.

Key Takeaway
Nafaqa is a continuous financial obligation arising from marriage, lineage, or ownership.

Obligation of Spousal Maintenance (Nafaqah)
Establishes the ruling and proofs for nafaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafaqah, identify the key proofs, and apply the condition of the wife's submission.

Core Idea
Nafaqah is wajib on the husband as compensation for the wife's confinement, regardless of her faith.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author establishes the obligation of spousal maintenance (nafaqah) on the husband. He cites explicit textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah and supplements them with a rational analogy that nafaqah is recompense for the wife's confinement in the marital home. Understanding this ruling is essential for grasping the Hanafi framework of marital rights and obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and condition
The passage states that nafaqah (food, clothing, housing) is wajib on the husband for his wife, provided she surrenders herself to his house. Note that the wife's faith (Muslim or kitabiyya) does not affect the obligation.
The condition of surrender is key; if she does not submit, nafaqah may not be due.
2
Examine the textual proofs (dalil naqli)
The author cites Quranic verses (65:7 and 2:233) and the Prophet's hadith in Hajjat al-Wada'. In Hanafi usul, the imperative form indicates wujub.
These proofs establish the obligation but are considered zanni al-thubut, hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Analyze the rational proof (qiyas)
The analogy: nafaqah is compensation for confinement (habs). The wife is confined to the husband's home for his exclusive right, so the husband must provide maintenance. This is analogous to a judge or zakat collector who is confined for public service and receives from the treasury.
The analogy underscores that the one for whose benefit the confinement occurs bears the cost.
4
Resolve the objection about mortgaged property
The text anticipates an objection: if a mortgaged item (rahn) is confined for the mortgagee's right, why isn't its maintenance on the mortgagee? The answer: the confinement benefits both parties – the mortgagee gets security, the mortgagor repays the debt – so it's not purely for the mortgagee's right.
This distinction strengthens the analogy: the wife's confinement is solely for the husband's benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النفقة
قال النفقة واجبة للزوجة على زوجها مسلمة كانت او كافرة اذا سلمت نفسها الى منزله فعليه نفقتها وكسوتها وسكناها والاصل فيه ذالك قوله تعالى الينفق دوسعة من سعته ، وقوله تعالى وعلى المولودله رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف وقوله عليه السلام فى حديث حجة الوداع ولهن عليكم رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف ولان النفقة جزاء الاجتاس وكل من كان محبوسا بحق مقصود لغيره كانت نفقة عليه اصله القاضي و العامل فى الصدقات وهذه الدلائل لافصل فيها فتستوى فيها المسلمة والكافرة

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ بیوی کے واسطے اس کے شوہر پر نفقہ واجب ہے۔ خواہ وہ بیوی مسلمان ہو یا کا فرجبکہ وہ اپنی ذات کو شوہر کے گھر سپر د کر دے تو شوہر پر اس کا نفقہ، لباس اور سکنی واجب ہے۔ اور نفقہ اللہ علیہ وسلم نے حجتہ الوداع کے خطبہ میں فرمایا کہ تمہارے اوپر تمہاری عورتوں کے لئے ان کا کھانا اور کپڑا بطور اعتدال واجب ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ نفقہ روکنے کا عوض ہے۔ اور جو کوئی دوسرے کے حق مقصود کی وجہ سے محبوس ہو تو نفقہ اسی پر ہوگا۔ اس کی اصل قاضی ہے۔ اور جو شخص زکوۃ کے واسطے عامل ہوں۔ اور ان دلیلوں میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے لہذا حق نفقہ میں مسلمان بیوی اور کافر دونوں برابر ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ بیوی کا نفقہ اس کے شوہر پر واجب ہے۔ بیوی خواہ مسلمان ہو یا کتابیہ بشر طیکہ وہ اپنی ذات اپنے شوہر کے گھر سپرد کر دے۔ پس شوہر پر اس کا نفقہ اس کا کپڑا اور اس کی سکونت واجب ہے۔ اور نفقہ واجب ہونے میں دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا فاتقوا الله فى النساء فانهن عوان عند كم اخذ تموهن بامانة الله واستحللتم فروجهن بكلمة الله ولكم عليهن ان لا يوطين فرشكم احد اتكـر هـونـه فان فعلن فاضربوهن ضرباً غير مبرح ولهن عليكم رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف (رواہ مسلم) عورتوں کے بارے میں اللہ سے ڈرو اس لئے کہ تمہارے پاس مقید ہیں ۔ تم نے انکو اللہ کی امانت کے ساتھ لیا۔ اور ان کی شرمگاہوں کو اللہ کے حکم سے حلال کیا۔ اور تمہارے واسطے ان پر واجب ہے کہ وہ تمہارے بچھونے کو کسی ایسے آدمی سے نہ روند وائیں جس کو تم نا پسند کرتے ہو ۔ اگر انھوں نے ایسا کیا تو ان کو آہستہ مارو۔ اور ان کے واسطے تمہارے اوپر ان کا کھانا، کپڑا اعتدال کے طور پر واجب ہے۔ دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ نفقہ محسوس کرنے کا عوض ہے۔ تو جو کوئی دوسرے کے حق مقصود کی وجہ سے محبوس ہوگا تو نفقہ بھی اسی پر ہوگا۔ پس چونکہ درت بھی اپنے شوہر کے واسطے محبوس ہے۔ لہذا عورت کا نفقہ بھی شوہر پر واجب ہوگا۔ اور اس کی اصل قاضی ہے۔ اور جو شخص زکوۃ کے واسطے عامل ہو اسلئے کہ یہ دونوں اپنی ذات کے واسطے کوئی کام نہیں کرتے بلکہ مسلمانوں کے مصالح پورے کرتے ہیں۔ لہذا مسلمانوں کے عام حق یعنی بیت المال سے بقدر کفایت ان کو دینا واجب ہے۔ اور یہی حکم مفتی کا اور وقف کے متولی کا اور وصیت کے وصی کا ۔ اور کفار سے لڑنے والے مسلمانوں کا ہے۔ اور چونکہ ان دلائل میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں۔ اسلئے نفقہ میں مسلمان بیوی اور کتابیہ سب برابر ہونگی۔ یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ محبوس کا نفقہ اس پر واجب ہوگا جس کے حق کی وجہ سے اس کو محبوس کیا گیا ہے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ۔ کیونکہ رہن کا نفقہ راہن پر واجب ہے۔ درانحالیکہ رہن مرتہن کے حق کی وجہ سے محبوس ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ہمیں یہ تو تسلیم ہے کہ رہن مرتہن کے پاس محبوس ہے۔ مگر یہ تسلیم نہیں کہ وہ صرف مرتہن کے حق کی وجہ سے محبوس ہے بلکہ جس طرح مرتہن کا مقصود حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح راہن کا مقصود بھی حاصل ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اگر دین ہلاک ہو جائے تو راہن ، رہن ہی کے ذریعہ دین ادا کرے گا۔ اسی لئے نفقہ مرتہن پر واجب نہیں کیا گیا۔
Chapter of Nafaqah: He said: Nafaqah is obligatory for the wife upon her husband, whether she is Muslim or disbeliever, when she surrenders herself to his house. Then upon him is her nafaqah, clothing, and dwelling. The basis for that is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Let him of wealth spend from his wealth' (65:7), and His saying: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable' (2:233), and his saying, peace be upon him, in the hadith of the Farewell Pilgrimage: 'And upon you is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable.' And because nafaqah is recompense for confinement, and everyone who is confined due to a right intended for another, nafaqah is upon that other – its basis is the judge and the worker in charity. And these proofs have no specification, so the Muslim and disbelieving wife are equal in it.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the Hanafi school. It states the obligation of nafaqah (maintenance) on the husband for his wife, regardless of her faith (Muslim or Kitabiyya), provided she submits herself to his home. The proofs are: Quranic verses (65:7 and 2:233), the Prophet's hadith in Hajjat al-Wada', and a rational analogy (qiyas) that nafaqah is compensation for confinement (habs) for another's right. The author draws an analogy with a judge and a zakat collector, who are confined for the public benefit and thus receive maintenance from the public treasury. The passage then addresses an objection: why is maintenance of a mortgaged item (murtahan) not on the mortgagee (murtahin) if it is confined for his right? The answer is that the mortgaged item serves both parties' interests – the mortgagee's right to security and the mortgagor's right to benefit from the debt. So the analogy is not perfect, and the ruling stands only for the wife's confinement which is exclusively for the husband's benefit.

Key Terms
النفقة (al-nafaqah): Spousal maintenance including food, clothing, and housing
محبوس (mahbus): Confined or restrained, here referring to the wife being confined to the husband's house for his exclusive right

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the rational proof (dalil 'aqli) given for the obligation of nafaqah?
A) Nafaqah is a form of charity
B) Nafaqah is compensation for confinement (habs)
C) Nafaqah is a gift from husband to wife
D) Nafaqah is a debt owed to the wife's family

Key Takeaway
The husband must provide maintenance to his wife as compensation for her confinement, regardless of her faith, as proven by Quran, Sunnah, and qiyas.
