Determining Nafaqah: Both Spouses' Status Considered
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whose status sets nafaqah amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi view on determining nafaqah amount by applying the principle of kifayah and the hadith of Hind, and distinguish it from al-Karkhi's and al-Shafi'i's positions.

Core Idea
Nafaqah is for sufficiency; both spouses' conditions set the level, not the husband's wealth alone.

When a husband must provide maintenance (nafaqah), how do we decide the amount – based on his income, her needs, or both? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute, with the relied-upon position considering the financial status of both spouses. This lesson unpacks the proofs and rational basis for this view, contrasting it with the opinion that only the husband's capacity matters.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi mufta bihi position
Identify that the preferred view (choice of al-Khassaf) considers both spouses' financial conditions: rich/rich → rich nafaqah; poor/poor → poor; rich husband/poor wife → intermediate between the two.
This is a three-tier graduated scale.
2
Identify the opposing view and its evidence
Al-Karkhi (and al-Shafi'i) argue only the husband's condition is relevant, citing Quran 65:7 'Let him of wealth spend from his capacity.'
The text is from Surah al-Talaq.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Quranic verse
The Hanafis do not reject the verse; they interpret it as addressing the husband's obligation to spend according to his means, but if he does not fulfil what is needed, the shortfall remains a debt on him. The verse does not exclude the wife's condition.
The verse commands the husband, but does not forbid considering the wife's need.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof: hadith and rational argument
The Prophet (ﷺ) told Hind bint 'Utbah to take from her husband's wealth what suffices her and her child, which considers the wife's need. Rationally, nafaqah is for kifayah (sufficiency), so a poor wife does not need a wealthy wife's amount.
The hadith is a primary textual proof; kifayah is the underlying rationale.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the mufta bihi view, a rich husband with a poor wife gives her an intermediate amount. Under al-Karkhi's view, he would give her the full nafaqah of a wealthy wife – a significant financial difference.
The dispute directly affects the amount payable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و تعتبر فى ذالك حالهما جميعا قال العبد الضعيف وهذا اختيار الخصاف و عليه الفتوى و تفسيره انما اذا كنان موسرين تجب نفقة اليساروان كانا معسرين فنفقة الاعساروان كانت معسرة و الزوج موسرا فنفقتها دون نفقة الموسرات و فوق نفقة المعسرات وقال الكرخى يعتبر حال الزوج وهو قول الشافعي لقوله تعالى لينفق ذوسعة من سعته وجه الاول قوله عليه السلام لهند امرأة ابی سفیان خذی من مال زوجک مایکفیک وولدک بالمعروف اعتبر حالها وهو الفقه فان النفقة تجب بطريق الكفاية والفقيرة لاتفتقر الى كفاية الموسرات فلامعنى للزيادة واما النص فنحن نقول بموجبه انه بخاطب بقدر وسعه والباقى دين في ذمة ومعنى قوله بالمعروف الوسط وهو الواجب و به يتبين انه لا معنى للتقدير كما ذهب اليه الشافعي انه على الموسر مدان وعلى المعسر مد واعلى المتوسط مد ونصف مد لان ما وجب كفاية لا يتقدر شرعا في نفسه
And consideration in that is of both their conditions. Al-‘Abd al-Da‘if (the author) said: This is the choice of al-Khassaf, and upon it is the fatwa. Its interpretation: When both are wealthy, the nafaqah of the wealthy is obligatory; if both are poor, the nafaqah of the poor; if the wife is poor and the husband wealthy, her nafaqah is less than that of wealthy women and more than that of poor women. Al-Karkhi said: The husband’s condition is considered – this is also the saying of al-Shafi‘i, due to His saying: 'Let him of wealth spend from his wealth' (65:7). The proof of the first (Khassaf’s view) is his saying, peace be upon him, to Hind the wife of Abu Sufyan: 'Take from your husband’s wealth what suffices you and your child in a goodly manner' – he considered her condition. And that is the fiqh (understanding), because nafaqah is obligatory by way of sufficiency (kifayah), and a poor woman does not need the sufficiency of wealthy women, so there is no meaning to increase. As for the text (Quran), we affirm its purport: he is addressed according to his capacity, and what remains is a debt in his liability. And the meaning of 'bi al-ma‘ruf' (according to what is acceptable) is the middle (wasat), which is the wajib. And by this it becomes clear that there is no sense in fixing a specific quantity as al-Shafi‘i held: that for the wealthy is two mudd (half sa‘), for the poor is one mudd, and for the intermediate is one and a half mudd, because what is obligatory as sufficiency is not fixed by itself in the Shari‘ah.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whose financial status determines the amount of nafaqah. The preferred view (choice of al-Khassaf, and the mufta bihi) is that both spouses' conditions are considered. The author details three scenarios: both wealthy, both poor, and mixed (wife poor, husband wealthy) with graduated scales. Al-Karkhi argues that only the husband's condition matters, which is also the Shafi'i position. The proof for Khassaf's view is the hadith of Hind bint 'Utbah, where the Prophet (ﷺ) told her to take what suffices her and her child, thus considering her need. The rational proof is that nafaqah is for sufficiency (kifayah), so a poor wife needs only what suffices her, not the luxurious level of wealthy women. The text refutes the Shafi'i practice of fixing specific amounts (mudd) because what is wajib as kifayah cannot be rigidly quantified by Shari'ah. The Quranic verse 'let him of wealth spend from his capacity' is interpreted as addressing the husband according to his means, with the surplus remaining as a debt if he does not pay voluntarily.

Key Terms
الكفاية (al-kifayah): Sufficiency – the amount needed to meet basic needs
بالمعروف (bi al-ma'ruf): According to what is acceptable or customary, interpreted here as the middle (wasat) level
الوسط (al-wasat): The middle, moderate level – the wajib amount of nafaqah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'bi al-ma'ruf' in the context of nafaqah?
A) The amount that is generous and plentiful
B) The amount that is the middle (wasat) level, which is wajib
C) The amount that the husband decides unilaterally
D) The amount equal to the wife's previous lifestyle

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi view determines nafaqah by considering both spouses' financial status, applying the principle of kifayah and the Prophetic guidance to give what suffices the wife, not a fixed quantity or the husband's capacity alone.

Determining Nafaqah Amount: Whose Status Matters?
Resolves ikhtilaf on nafaqah amount criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on nafaqah determination, explain the proofs for considering both spouses, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Nafaqah is based on sufficiency, not a fixed measure; both spouses' financial status are considered in the Hanafi school.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a key intra-Hanafi (and inter-madhhab) dispute on whether nafaqah should consider only the husband's wealth or both spouses. The author resolves it by adopting the view of Imam al-Khasaf, which considers both, and provides proofs from the hadith of Hind and rational argument. Understanding this ruling is crucial for correctly calculating spousal maintenance in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the central question: whose financial status determines the amount of nafaqah? State the Hanafi view (al-Khasaf: both spouses) and the opposing view (al-Karkhi / al-Shafi'i: only husband).
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences for the amount owed.
2
Identify the Hanafi position and its four scenarios
According to al-Khasaf, nafaqah amount depends on whether both spouses are affluent, both poor, husband affluent and wife poor, or husband poor and wife affluent. For the last two, an average nafaqah is given.
The underlying principle is kifayah (sufficiency).
3
Locate the Hanafi dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The primary proof is the hadith of Hind bint 'Utbah, where the Prophet (SAW) commanded her to take what suffices her and her child. This shows consideration of the wife's need, not just the husband's wealth.
The imperative 'khudhi' indicates obligation, and 'ma yakfik' ties the amount to sufficiency.
4
Examine the Shafi'i/Karkhi dalil and the Hanafi response
The opposing proof is Quran 65:7, which commands spending according to capacity. The Hanafi response reconciles it: the husband must give according to his means, but any shortfall becomes a debt on him. The wife's need is still considered via 'bi'l-ma'ruf' (customary average).
The Hanafi school does not reject the verse but interprets it in light of the hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: if the wife is from a higher class, Hanafi law requires a higher nafaqah (though not equal to her affluent equals), while Shafi'i law only requires the husband's standard. Also, Hanafi rejects fixed measurements. The mufta bihi is al-Khasaf's view.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah explicitly states 'upon it is the fatwa'.

شافعی کا امام کرخی کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول ہے لينفق ذو سعة من سعة ومن قدر عليه رز قه فلينفق مما اتاه الله یعنی وسعت والا اپنی وسعت کے مطابق خرچ کرے اور تنگدست اس میں سے خرچ کرے جو اسکو اللہ نے دیا ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے دونوں حالتوں میں مرد کے حال کا اعتبار کیا ہے اور اس کو خرچ کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے۔ اور اول یعنی امام خصاف کے قول کی وجہ وہ حدیث ہے جس کو امام بخاری نے روایت کیا ہے حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا فرماتی ہیں ۔ ان هنداً بنت عتبة امرأة ابي سفيان قالت يا رسول الله ان ابا سفيان رجل شحيح لا يعطيني ما يكفيني وولدى الا ما اخذت منه وهو لا يعلم فقال خذی من مال زوجک و ما يكفیک وولدك بالمعروف یعنی ہندو بنت عقبہ (ابوسفیان کی بیوی ) نے کہا اے اللہ کے رسول ابوسفیان بہت بخیل آدمی ہے۔ وہ مجھ کو اتنا نہیں دیتا جو مجھ کو اور میری اولا د کو کفالت کرے ۔ مگر یہ کہ میں بغیر بتلائے لے لوں۔ پس آپ نے فرمایا کہ تو اپنے شوہر کے مال میں سے اس قدر لے لے جو تجھ کو اور تیری اولا د کو اعتدال کے طور پر کفایت کر جائے۔ اس واقعہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ حضور اقدس صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے عورت کے حال کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔ اور سمجھ کی بات بھی یہی ہے کہ عورت کے حال کا اعتبار کیا جائے کیونکہ نفقہ تو بطور کفایت واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور جو عورت غریب ہو اس کو مالدار عورتوں کی کفایت درکار نہیں ہے۔ تو زیادتی کے کچھ معنی نہیں ہیں ۔ اور ابوسفیان مالدار آدمی تھے ۔ پس اگر مرد ہی کا اعتبار ہوتا تو فراغت کی مقدار لینے کا حکم دیا جاتا۔ اور رہی نص قرآنی یعنى لينفق ذوسعة من سعتہ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہم بھی اس کے حکم کے موافق قائل ہیں۔ یعنی اس آیت میں حکم یہ ہے کہ مرد اپنی وسعت کے لائق نفقہ دے اور جو باقی رہا وہ اس کے ذمہ قرضہ رہے گا۔ مثلا فقیر مرد پر مالدار عورت کا یومیہ ادھ درجہ کا نفقہ آٹھ روپیہ ہیں اور مرد اس کو نگی کا نفقہ پانچ روپیہ یومیہ کے حساب سے دیتا رہا تو تین روپیہ اس پر قرضہ رہیگا۔ حتی کہ جب اس کو وسعت ہو تو ادا کر دے۔ اور باری تعالیٰ کے قول بالمعروف سے اوسط درجہ کا نفقہ مراد ہے۔ اور یہی واجب ہے۔ اور حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ہندہ امراۃ ابی سفیان سے جو فرمایا که خذی من مال زوجک مایکفیک وولدک اس سے یہ بات واضح ہوگئی کہ نفقہ کی کوئی مقدار مر نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ حضرت امام شافعی کا مذہب ہے۔ کہ خوشحالی کے ذمہ یومیہ دو مد یعنی نصف صاع ہے اور تنگدست کے ذمہ ایک مد واجب ہوتی ہے وہ شرعاً اپنی ذات سے کسی اندازہ سے متعین نہیں ہوتی ۔ اس لئے کہ لوگوں کے حالات مختلف ہیں۔ بڑھاپے اور جوانی کی غذا میں فرق ہے۔ اور اوقات اور جگہوں کے اختلاف سے بھی لوگوں کے حالات بدلتے رہتے ہیں۔ پس مقدار مقرر کرنے سے بھی ضرر بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کوئی مقدار مقرر نہیں کی جاسکتی۔
And consideration in that matter is of the status of both of them jointly. Al-‘Abd al-Da‘if said: This is the choice of al-Khasaf and upon it is the fatwa. Its interpretation: if both are affluent, nafaqah of the affluent is obligatory; if both are straitened, then nafaqah of the straitened; if the wife is straitened and the husband affluent, then her nafaqah is less than that of affluent women and above that of straitened women. Al-Karkhi said: The husband’s status is considered, and this is the saying of al-Shafi‘i, due to Allah’s saying: ‘Let the one of ample means spend according to his ample means.’ The proof of the first is his saying (peace be upon him) to Hind, wife of Abu Sufyan: ‘Take from your husband’s wealth what suffices you and your child in a fitting manner.’ He considered her status, and this is the fiqh, for nafaqah is obligatory by way of sufficiency, and the poor woman does not need the sufficiency of the affluent, so there is no meaning to increase. As for the text, we accept its implication: it addresses him according to his capacity, and the remainder is a debt upon his liability. And the meaning of His saying ‘bi’l-ma‘ruf’ is the middle, which is obligatory. And by this it becomes clear that there is no meaning to estimation as al-Shafi‘i held: for the affluent two mudds, for the straitened one mudd, and for the middling one and a half mudds, because what is obligatory as sufficiency is not quantifiable in itself by Shari‘ah. Translation: And in the amount of nafaqah, the status of both husband and wife is considered. ‘Abd al-Da‘if (the author) said: This is the chosen madhhab of al-Khasaf, and upon it is the fatwa. Its interpretation: When both are well-off, nafaqah of ease is obligatory. If both are poor, nafaqah of hardship is obligatory. If the wife is poor and the husband rich, nafaqah is above that of poor women and below that of rich women. Imam al-Karkhi said: Only the husband’s status is considered, and this is the saying of Imam al-Shafi‘i, because Allah says: ‘Let him who has abundance spend of his abundance.’ The proof of the first view is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Hind, wife of Abu Sufyan: ‘Take from your husband’s wealth what is sufficient for you and your children in a fitting manner.’ In this hadith, the Prophet considered the woman’s status, and this is also the fiqh (understanding), because nafaqah is obligatory by way of sufficiency, and a poor woman does not need the sufficiency of rich women, so there is no meaning to increase. As for the ruling of the text, we accept it: it commands him to give according to his capacity, and whatever remains is a debt on his responsibility. And the meaning of Allah’s word ‘bi’l-ma‘ruf’ is the middle level, and that is obligatory. And from this speech it becomes clear that there is no meaning to specification of amount, as al-Shafi‘i went towards, that for the rich two mudds (half a sa‘), for the poor a quarter sa‘ (one mudd), and for the middling one and a half mudds, because what is obligatory as sufficiency is not inherently specified by Shari‘ah. Explanation: In this passage, the author is clarifying this issue: whose status will be considered in nafaqah and its amount. Thus, Imam al-Quduri said: In nafaqah, the status of both husband and wife is considered. The author of al-Hidayah said: The chosen madhhab of Imam al-Khasaf is this, and upon it is the fatwa. The interpretation of Imam al-Khasaf’s saying is that rationally there are four categories: both wealthy, both poor, husband rich and wife poor, or the opposite (husband poor and wife rich). In the first, nafaqah of ease; in the second, nafaqah of hardship; in the third and fourth, the wife gets an average nafaqah—less than the nafaqah of rich women and more than the nafaqah of poor women. Imam al-Karkhi said: The husband’s status will be considered, and this is also the saying of Imam al-Shafi‘i. Al-Karkhi’s proof is Allah’s saying: ‘Let him who has abundance spend according to his abundance, and he whose provision is restricted, let him spend from what Allah has given him.’ In both situations, Allah considered the man’s status and commanded him to spend. As for the first view (of Khasaf), its proof is the hadith narrated by Imam al-Bukhari from ‘A’ishah (may Allah be pleased with her): Hind bint ‘Utbah, wife of Abu Sufyan, said: O Messenger of Allah, Abu Sufyan is a miser, he does not give me enough for me and my children except what I take from him without his knowledge. He said: ‘Take from your husband’s wealth what suffices you and your child in a fitting manner.’ This incident shows that the Prophet considered the woman’s status. And understanding also dictates this, because nafaqah is obligatory by way of sufficiency, and a poor woman does not need the sufficiency of rich women, so increase has no meaning. Abu Sufyan was a wealthy man; if only the man’s status were considered, he would have been commanded to give what is comfortable. As for the Quranic text (let him who has abundance spend according to his abundance), its answer is that we accept its ruling: it commands the man to give according to his capacity, and whatever remains is a debt. For example, if a poor man’s wife is rich, her daily average nafaqah is eight rupees, and he gives five rupees daily, three rupees remain as a debt until he becomes able to pay. And Allah’s word ‘bi’l-ma‘ruf’ means the middle level, and that is obligatory. And the Prophet’s statement to Hind—‘Take from your husband’s wealth what suffices you and your child’—makes it clear that nafaqah has no fixed amount, unlike Imam al-Shafi‘i’s view that for the wealthy two mudds (half a sa‘) daily and for the poor one mudd are obligatory. For whatever is obligatory as sufficiency is not fixed by Shari‘ah in itself, because people’s conditions differ, old age and youth have different food requirements, and differences in time and place change conditions. Therefore, fixing an amount could cause harm, so no fixed amount can be set.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the criterion for determining the amount of spousal maintenance (nafaqah). The author presents two positions: (1) Imam al-Khasaf's view (supported by al-Quduri and adopted in al-Hidayah as the mufta bihi) that the financial status of both spouses is considered, and (2) Imam al-Karkhi's view (also held by Imam al-Shafi'i) that only the husband's status matters. The Hanafi position, as per al-Khasaf, distinguishes four scenarios: both affluent, both straitened, husband affluent with wife straitened, and husband straitened with wife affluent. In the last two, an average nafaqah is given—less than that of affluent women and more than that of poor women. The proof for the first view is the hadith of Hind bint 'Utbah, where the Prophet (SAW) considered her need, not just Abu Sufyan's wealth. The proof for the second view is the Qur'anic verse (65:7) that commands spending according to capacity. The Hanafi response reconciles the verse by stating that the husband is commanded to give according to his means, but any shortfall remains a debt on him. The passage also rejects the Shafi'i fixed measurement (mudd) for nafaqah, arguing that since nafaqah is determined by sufficiency (kifayah), it cannot be fixed by Shari'ah; it varies with circumstances. The relied-upon Hanafi position (al-mu'tamad) is that of al-Khasaf, and the fatwa is upon it.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Spousal maintenance: food, clothing, and housing that a husband must provide for his wife.
اعتبار حال (i‘tibar hal): Consideration of the financial status (affluent or poor) of the person in determining nafaqah amount.
کفایت (kifayah): Sufficiency; the amount that covers basic needs without excess or deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view (mufta bihi), whose financial status is considered when determining the amount of nafaqah?
A) Only the husband's status
B) Only the wife's status
C) Both spouses' status
D) The status of the wife's family

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that nafaqah amount considers both spouses' financial status, based on sufficiency, not a fixed measure.

Wife's Entitlement to Nafaqah When Withholding for Unpaid Mahr
Ruling with proof on nafaqah when wife withholds for mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's nafaqah when she withholds herself due to unpaid prompt mahr, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) using the concept of ihtibas.

Core Idea
A wife who withholds for her mahr keeps her nafaqah because the impediment is from the husband's side.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi marital maintenance (nafaqah). The key issue is whether a wife who refuses to submit to her husband until he pays her prompt mahr forfeits her right to maintenance. The Hanafi school rules that she does not, based on a careful analysis of the cause (sabab) of nafaqah: the wife's ihtibas (availability). The lesson shows how the law attributes the loss of availability to the husband's breach of duty, preserving the wife's entitlement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the wife's withholding of herself due to unpaid mahr. The ruling is that she retains her right to nafaqah.
The ruling is wajib (obligatory) upon the husband.
2
Understand the condition for nafaqah
The condition (sabab) for nafaqah is the wife's ihtibas, i.e., her being available for her husband. Normally, if she is not available, nafaqah drops.
The text states: 'the loss of confinement is from his side'.
3
Analyze the ta'lil (legal reasoning)
The text argues that the wife's withholding is 'with a right' (bi haqq). Because it is for a legitimate cause (unpaid mahr), the absence of ihtibas is treated as if it came from the husband's side.
The effective cause ('illa) is the husband's failure to pay mahr.
4
Apply the concept of legal fiction
The husband's failure to pay mahr is the effective cause; thus, legally, ihtibas is deemed to exist, and nafaqah remains wajib.
The ruling is derived by qiyas (analogy).
5
Note the practical consequence
The wife can lawfully refuse submission and still receive maintenance. The husband must pay mahr to restore the normal state.
This ruling protects the wife from being pressured to waive her mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان امتنعت من تسليم نفسها حتى يعطيها مهرها فلها النفقة لانه منع بحق فكان فوت الاحتباس بمعنى من قبله فيجعل كالفائت.
ترجمہ: اور اگر عورت نے اپنی ذات کو سپرد کرنے سے انکار کیا یہاں تک کہ شوہر اس کو اس کا مہر دیدے تو عورت کے واسطے نفقہ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ روکنا ایک حق کے ساتھ ہے تو (عورت کا محبوس نہ ہونا ایک ایسی وجہ سے ہوا جو شوہر کی طرف سے پیدا ہوئی پس ایسا قرار دیا جائے گا) کہ محبوس کرنا فوت نہیں ہوا۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت نے اپنے آپ کو شوہر کے حوالہ کرنے سے روک لیا یہاں تک کہ شوہر اس کا مہر معجل دیدے تو اس صورت میں عورت کا نفقہ ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ شوہر پر واجب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کا اپنے آپ کو روکنا اپنے حق کی وجہ سے ہے۔ جب شوہر کی طرف سے احتباس فوت ہی نہیں ہوا۔ اور جب عورت کی جانب سے احتباس فوت نہیں ہوا تو اس کا نفقہ بھی ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
And if she refrains from surrendering herself until he gives her her mahr, then she has the right to nafaqah, because this withholding is due to a right, so the loss of confinement (ihtibas) is (considered) from his side, thus it is treated as if it were not lost. Translation: And if a woman refuses to hand over herself until her husband pays her her mahr, then nafaqah is obligatory for her, because this withholding is with a right, so (the failure of the woman to be confined is a cause that arose from the husband's side, so it will be treated as if the confinement was not lost). Explanation: The issue is that if a woman refrains from handing herself over to her husband until her husband pays her her prompt mahr, then in this case the woman's nafaqah is not dropped. Rather, it is obligatory upon the husband. The proof is that the woman's withholding is due to her right. Since the confinement was not lost from the husband's side, and since the confinement was not lost from the woman's side, her nafaqah will not be dropped.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This lesson presents a ruling from the chapter on nafaqah (maintenance). The passage type is a ruling with proof. The author, citing the Hidayah, states that if a wife refuses to submit to her husband until he pays her the prompt mahr (mahr mu'ajjal), she remains entitled to nafaqah. The legal reasoning (ta'lil) is that her refusal is a legitimate exercise of her right (haqq). The husband's obligation of nafaqah is conditioned on the wife's 'ihtibas' (availability/confinement for the marital relationship). Here, although the wife is not physically available, the reason for her unavailability is the husband's failure to pay mahr. Therefore, legally, the confinement is attributed to the husband, and the wife's nafaqah does not lapse. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the wife's nafaqah remains wajib (obligatory) and is not dropped. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
احتباس (ihtibas): In this context, the wife's physical availability and confinement for the husband's access for marital relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi fiqh, if a wife refuses to submit to her husband until he pays her prompt mahr, what is the ruling on her nafaqah?
A) She loses her nafaqah because she is not physically available.
B) She is still entitled to nafaqah because her refusal is based on a right.
C) She is entitled to only half of the nafaqah.
D) Nafaqah is suspended until she submits.

Key Takeaway
A wife's refusal to submit due to unpaid mahr does not forfeit her nafaqah because the impediment is legally attributed to the husband.

Nashizah: Nafaqah Suspended Until Return to Marital Home
Ruling with proof on nafaqah for nashizah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a wife's nafaqah is suspended under Hanafi law and distinguish the two scenarios of nushuz.

Core Idea
A wife who leaves the marital home loses nafaqah; staying but refusing access does not.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common marital dispute: a wife who rebels (nashizah) by leaving the home. The Hanafi school ties the obligation of nafaqah directly to the wife's physical presence and availability (ihtibas). Understanding when nafaqah is suspended—and when it is not—is essential for applying Islamic family law accurately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The wife's nushuz (rebellion) by leaving the marital home. The ruling: no nafaqah until she returns.
This is a conditional suspension, not permanent loss.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas: nafaqah is compensation for ihtibas (confinement). If the wife ends ihtibas by leaving, the compensation ceases.
The 'illa is the loss of ihtibas from her side.
3
Trace the 'illa (effective cause)
The cause of the ruling is the wife's action that removes ihtibas. When she returns, ihtibas is restored, and nafaqah resumes.
Ihtibas means physical presence in the home, not merely the marriage contract.
4
Analyze the contrast case
If the wife stays at home but refuses sexual access, nafaqah is not dropped. Why? Because ihtibas remains, and the husband can legally compel intercourse.
This distinguishes Hanafi position from other schools.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The mufta bihi position is clear: nafaqah is due only when ihtibas exists from the wife's side. The ruling is based on a sound 'illa.
Other schools may define nushuz differently and thus have different rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان نشرت فلا نفقة لها حتى تعود الى منزله لان فوت الاحتباس منها واذا عادت جاء الاحتباس فتجب النفقة بخلاف ما اذا امتنعت من التمكين فى بيت الزوج لان الاحتباس قائم والزوج يقدر على الوطى كرها.
ترجمہ: اور اگر عورت نے نافرمانی اور سرکشی کی تو اس کے واسطے نفقہ نہیں ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ اپنے شوہر کے گھر کی طرف لوٹ آئے۔ اس لئے کہ احتباس کا فوت ہونا عورت کی جانب سے ہوا اور جب واپس آگئی تو احتباس بھی واپس آگیا۔ پس نفقہ واجب ہو گیا۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ عورت نے شوہر کے گھر میں (اپنے اوپر) قدرت دینے سے روکا۔ کیونکہ احتباس موجود ہے۔ اور شوہر زبردستی وطی کرنے پر قادر ہے۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت نے نافرمانی اور سرکشی کی تو اس کے واسطے نفقہ نہیں ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ سرکشی چھوڑ کر شوہر کے گھر واپس آئے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنا محبوس ہونا اپنی طرف سے دور کیا۔ یعنی نفقہ اس کے احتباس پر واجب تھا اور جب اس نے احتباس خود ختم کیا تو نفقہ بھی ساقط ہو گیا۔ اور جب وہ لوٹ کر شوہر کے گھر آگئی تو پھر محبوس ہوگئی۔ لہذا پھر نفقہ واجب ہو جائے گا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر عورت شوہر کے گھر رہتے ہوئے اس کو وطی کی قدرت نہ دے تو عورت کا نفقہ ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ احتباس موجود ہے۔ اور شوہر اس سے زبردستی کر سکتا ہے۔
And if she rebels (nushuz), then there is no nafaqah for her until she returns to his home, because the loss of confinement is from her side. And when she returns, confinement comes, so nafaqah becomes obligatory. Unlike the case where she refuses to grant access within the husband's home, because confinement is present, and the husband is able to have intercourse forcibly. Translation: And if a woman commits disobedience and rebellion, then there is no nafaqah for her until she returns to her husband's home, because the loss of confinement is from her side. And when she returns, confinement returns, so nafaqah becomes obligatory. Unlike the case where the woman refuses to allow (herself) within the husband's home, because confinement is present, and the husband can force intercourse. Explanation: The issue is that if a woman rebels, she does not get nafaqah until she abandons rebellion and returns to the husband's home, because she removed her confinement herself. That is, nafaqah was obligatory due to her confinement, and when she ended confinement, nafaqah was dropped. And when she returns to the husband's home, she becomes confined again, so nafaqah becomes obligatory again. In contrast, if the woman refuses to allow vaginal access while staying in the husband's home, her nafaqah is not dropped, because confinement exists and the husband can force her.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This lesson is a ruling with proof concerning the nashizah (rebellious wife) and her entitlement to nafaqah. The author explains that if a wife leaves the marital home without a valid excuse (nushuz), she loses her right to maintenance until she returns. The legal reason ('illa) is that the loss of ihtibas (confinement/availability) is due to her own action. Since nafaqah is a reward for ihtibas, when she removes herself from that state, nafaqah ceases. Upon returning, ihtibas is reestablished and nafaqah resumes. The text then distinguishes an important exception: if the wife stays in the husband's home but refuses to allow sexual access, she does not lose nafaqah. This is because ihtibas (being physically present in the home) is still in effect, and the husband can legally compel her (by force if necessary) for intercourse. Thus, the refusal does not negate his ability to access her, and nafaqah remains wajib. This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school and reflects the centrality of spatial confinement rather than actual submission.

Key Terms
نشوز (nushuz): Rebellion or disobedience of the wife, specifically leaving the marital home without a valid excuse or refusing to fulfill marital duties without lawful reason.
احتباس (ihtibas): The wife's physical presence and availability in the marital home, making her accessible for the husband's marital rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife leaves her husband's home without a valid excuse. Under Hanafi fiqh, when does her nafaqah resume?
A) Immediately after she leaves.
B) Only after she returns to the husband's home.
C) After one month of return.
D) Never, if the divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
Nafaqah is tied to ihtibas: if the wife breaks confinement by leaving, nafaqah stops until she returns; refusing access at home does not break confinement.

Minor Wife: Nafaqah Conditioned on Marital Capability
Ruling on nafaqah for a minor wife with Shafi'i opposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafaqah for a minor wife and compare it with the Shafi'i position, identifying the different proofs and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
A minor wife's ihtibas triggers no nafaqah until she is capable of intercourse.

This passage addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: is a minor wife who cannot yet engage in intercourse entitled to nafaqah from her husband? The Hanafi school says no, while Imam al-Shafi'i says yes. The disagreement stems from a fundamental difference in understanding the nature of nafaqah in marriage — is it a compensation for ownership (iwad) or a support obligation tied to effective confinement (ihtibas)? The lesson unpacks the proofs on both sides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its condition
The Hanafi school holds that a minor wife who cannot be enjoyed (sexually) has no right to nafaqah. The condition is that ihtibas must be a means to the marital objective (intercourse or its preliminaries).
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Nafaqah is not a compensation for ownership (mahr is that); it is tied to ihtibas. Since a minor cannot fulfill the marital purpose, her ihtibas does not obligate nafaqah. She is analogous to a nashizah (rebellious wife).
The Hanafi proof also distinguishes the sick wife, whose nafaqah remains.
3
Present the Shafi'i opposing position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that nafaqah is compensation for the husband's ownership (milk) over the wife, similar to a slave. Need is the cause, and minor and adult are equal in need.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes mahr as contractual compensation, while nafaqah is not a compensative exchange. Two compensations cannot combine. So the minor gets mahr only.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: In Hanafi, minor wife receives only mahr; in Shafi'i, she receives both mahr and nafaqah.

Source Text

ترجمہ: اور اگر صغیرہ ہو جس سے تمتع (جماع) نہیں ہو سکتا تو اس کے واسطے نفقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ وطی سے منتفع ہونا ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے ہے جو عورت میں موجود ہیں۔ اور جو احتباس نفقہ واجب کرتا ہے یہ وہ احتباس ہے جو نکاح کا مقصود حاصل ہونے کا وسیلہ ہو۔ اور ایسا احتباس نہیں پایا گیا برخلاف مریضہ عورت کے چنانچہ ہم عنقریب بیان کریں گے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ صغیرہ کے واسطے نفقہ واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ نفقہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک شوہر کی ملک کا عوض ہے۔ جیسا کہ اس عورت کا نفقہ جس کی ذات کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ملک کا معوض تو مہر ہے۔ اور ایک معوض کے دو عوض جمع نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔ پس صغیرہ عورت کے لئے مہر ہے نفقہ نہیں۔
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت ایسی صغیرہ ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ جماع نہیں کیا جا سکتا تو اس کے لئے شوہر پر نفقہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ خواہ یہ شوہر کے مکان میں ہو یا شوہر کے مکان میں نہ ہو یہاں تک کہ جماع کے قابل ہو جائے۔ یہی جمہور علماء کا قول ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جماع کا منتفع نہ ہونا ایسی وجہ سے ہے جو عورت میں موجود ہے۔ یعنی صغیرہ کا اپنے آپ کو شوہر کے سپرد نہ کرنا۔ پس صغیرہ ایسی ہو گئی جیسا کہ ناشزہ (نافرمان) اور جو احتباس نفقہ واجب کرتا ہے یہ وہ ہے جو نکاح کے مقصود (جماع یا دواعی جماع) حاصل ہونے کا وسیلہ ہو۔ اور ایسا احتباس پایا نہیں گیا اس وجہ سے صغیرہ کے لئے اس کے شوہر پر نفقہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ برخلاف مریضہ کے کہ اس کا نفقہ ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ صغیرہ کے واسطے نفقہ واجب ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک نفقہ شوہر کی ملک کا عوض ہے جیسے اس عورت کا نفقہ جس کی ذات کا مالک ہوتا ہے۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ نفقہ واجب ہونے کا سبب حاجت ہے۔ اور حاجت میں صغیرہ اور کبیرہ سب برابر ہیں۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ملک کا عوض تو مہر ہے۔ کیونکہ عوض وہ ہے جو داخل عقد ہو کر مذکور ہو۔ اور عقد کے تحت مہر داخل ہوتا ہے نہ کہ نفقہ۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ ملک کا عوض مہر ہے۔ اور جب ملک کا عوض مہر ہے تو نفقہ عوض نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اس لئے کہ ایک شئی کے کئی عوض جمع نہیں ہوتے۔ پس صغیرہ کے واسطے مہر ہوگا نہ کہ نفقہ۔
And if she is a minor with whom intercourse cannot be enjoyed, then there is no nafaqah for her, because the prevention of enjoyment is due to a quality in her, and the confinement that obligates nafaqah is that which is a means to the objective that is valid by marriage, and it is not found. Unlike a sick woman, as we will explain. And al-Shafi'i said: She has nafaqah, because in his view nafaqah is a compensation for ownership, just as in the case of a female slave owned by right of possession. And our proof is that mahr is the compensation for ownership, and two compensations cannot be combined for one countervalue, so for her is mahr, not nafaqah. Translation: And if she is a minor who cannot be enjoyed (intercourse), then there is no nafaqah for her, because the inability to benefit from intercourse is due to a quality present in the woman. And the confinement that makes nafaqah obligatory is that which is a means to obtain the purpose of marriage, and such confinement is not found. Unlike a sick woman, as we will soon explain. And Imam al-Shafi'i said that nafaqah is obligatory for the minor, because in his view nafaqah is compensation for the husband's ownership, like the nafaqah of a woman whose person is owned (i.e., a slave). And our proof is that the compensation for ownership is mahr, and two compensations cannot be combined for one countervalue, so for a minor woman is mahr, not nafaqah. Explanation: The issue is that if a woman is so minor that intercourse cannot be had with her, then nafaqah is not wajib upon the husband, whether she is in the husband's house or not, until she becomes capable of intercourse. This is the view of the majority of scholars. The proof is that the inability to benefit from intercourse is due to a quality in the woman, i.e., the minor's not surrendering herself to the husband. So the minor becomes like a nashizah. And the confinement that makes nafaqah obligatory is that which is a means to obtain the purpose of marriage (intercourse or its preliminaries), and such confinement is not found, so nafaqah is not wajib for the minor. Unlike a sick woman, whose nafaqah is not dropped. Imam al-Shafi'i said nafaqah is wajib for the minor because in his view nafaqah is compensation for the husband's ownership, like the nafaqah of a female slave. The reason is that the cause for nafaqah being wajib is need, and in need, minor and adult are equal. And our proof is that the compensation for ownership is mahr, because compensation is that which is entered into the contract and mentioned. And under the contract, mahr is included, not nafaqah. So it is established that the compensation for ownership is mahr. And when the compensation for ownership is mahr, then nafaqah cannot be compensation, because multiple compensations cannot be combined for one thing. So for a minor, mahr is given, not nafaqah.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding nafaqah for a minor wife who is not yet capable of intercourse. The Hanafi position is that such a wife is not entitled to nafaqah, because ihtibas (confinement) that is the basis for nafaqah must be a means to achieve the marital objective (intercourse or its preliminaries). Since she is physically incapable, her confinement does not function as a means to that end. The Hanafis analogize her to a nashizah (rebellious wife) in that the inability stems from her side. She is distinguished from a sick wife, whose nafaqah remains because her inability is temporary and does not negate the possibility of fulfillment later. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that nafaqah is compensation (iwad) for the husband's ownership (milk) over the wife, similar to a slave woman owned by right of possession. Since the husband owns her, she deserves nafaqah regardless of her ability to consummate. The Hanafi response is that the true compensation for ownership in marriage is the mahr (dower), not nafaqah. Nafaqah is not a contractual compensation but a post-contractual obligation arising from ihtibas. Since two compensations cannot be exacted for one countervalue (the marriage contract), the wife gets mahr (which is agreed upon), and nafaqah is conditional. The Hanafi argument is based on the principle that the contract mentions mahr as the specified exchange, whereas nafaqah is not mentioned and is thus not an exchange but a support obligation tied to ihtibas.

Key Terms
صغیرہ (saghirah): A minor female who has not reached the age of physical maturity (bulugh) capable of sexual intercourse.
عوض (iwad): Compensation or exchange; in this context, something given in return for ownership (milk) in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because she is not yet married.
B) Because her ihtibas does not serve as a means to the marital objective.
C) Because her father must support her.
D) Because her husband is not obligated to support minors.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school denies nafaqah to a minor wife until she can engage in intercourse, as her ihtibas is not a means to the marital objective; mahr alone suffices as compensation.

Nafaqah for Adult Wife of Minor Husband
Ruling on nafaqah for an adult wife married to a minor husband incapable of intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafaqah for an adult wife married to a minor husband incapable of intercourse and explain the qiyas to a majbub or 'innin.

Core Idea
A wife's submission (taslim) entitles her to nafaqah even if the husband cannot consummate.

This lesson addresses a nuanced scenario: what happens to the wife's maintenance (nafaqah) when her husband is a minor and unable to engage in intercourse? Intuitively, one might think nafaqah is suspended until consummation is possible. However, Hanafi fiqh takes a different approach, focusing on the wife's role in the marriage contract. The key is her submission (taslim), not the husband's physical capability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core case and ruling
Read the opening sentence: the husband is a minor (saghir) unable to have intercourse, the wife is an adult (kabirah). The ruling: she is entitled to nafaqah from his wealth.
The ruling is clear: nafaqah is wajib.
2
Locate the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The text gives the rationale: 'because submission is achieved from her side, and inability is only from his side.' The condition for nafaqah is the wife's ihtibas (confinement/submission), not the husband's ability to consummate.
This is a key principle in Hanafi law.
3
Trace the qiyas analogy
The text compares the minor husband to a majbub (castrated) or 'innin (impotent) husband. In both cases, the wife's submission is complete, so nafaqah remains wajib. Identify the effective cause (illah): the wife's taslim is present, and the deficiency is from the husband.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Note the exception: both minors
The commentary (from al-Dhakhirah) clarifies that if both spouses are minors and unable to consummate, nafaqah is not wajib by consensus. This is because the wife's submission is not legally effective from a minor.
This is an important boundary case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان الزوج صغيرا لايقدر على الوطى وهى كبيرة قلها النفقة من ماله لان التسليم تحقق منها وانما العجز من قبله فصار كالمجبوب والعنين.
ترجمہ: اور اگر شوہر صغیر ہے جو جماع پر قادر نہیں ہے حال یہ کہ عورت بالغہ ہے تو اس کے لئے شوہر کے مال میں سے نفقہ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ عورت کی طرف سے اپنے آپ کو سپرد کرنا محقق ہو گیا اور عجز فقط شوہر کی طرف سے ہے پس مقطوع الذکر اور عنین کے مانند ہو گیا۔
تشریح: اور اگر شوہر نابالغ ہے جماع پر قدرت نہیں رکھتا اور اس کی بیوی بالغہ ہے تو شوہر کے مال سے اس کے لئے نفقہ واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عورت کی جانب سے اپنے آپ کو سپرد کرنا پایا گیا۔ اور عجز فقط شوہر کی طرف سے ہے۔ لہذا جس طرح مقطوع الذکر (وہ جس کا ذکر کٹ گیا) اور عنین (نا مرد) کی بیوی کا نفقہ واجب ہوتا ہے، اسی طرح اس نابالغ کی بیوی کا نفقہ بھی واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر میاں بیوی دونوں نابالغ ہوں کہ جماع پر قادر نہیں ہیں تو بالاتفاق بیوی کا نفقہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ (الذخیرۃ)
And if the husband is a minor, unable to have intercourse, and she is an adult, then she has nafaqah from his wealth, because submission is achieved from her side, and inability is only from his side, so he becomes like one whose penis is cut off (majbub) or impotent ('innin). Translation: And if the husband is a minor who is not capable of intercourse, while the wife is an adult, then nafaqah from the husband's wealth is wajib for her, because on the wife's side, she has submitted herself, and the inability is only from the husband's side. So he becomes like one whose penis is cut off (majbub) or impotent ('innin). Explanation: And if the husband is a minor who does not have the ability to have intercourse, and his wife is an adult, then nafaqah is wajib for her from his wealth, because on the wife's side, she is found to have submitted herself, and the inability is only on the husband's side. Therefore, just as the wife of a majbub (whose penis is severed) or an 'innin (impotent man) receives nafaqah, so too the wife of a minor husband will receive nafaqah. And if both spouses are minors who are not capable of intercourse, then by consensus, nafaqah is not wajib for the wife. (al-Dhakhirah)
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This lesson is a ruling with proof regarding the nafaqah of an adult wife married to a minor or impotent husband. The Hanafi position is that she is entitled to nafaqah from the husband's wealth. The legal reasoning (ta'lil) is that the condition for nafaqah—ihtibas—is fulfilled by the wife's submission and presence (taslim). The husband's inability to engage in intercourse is his deficiency, not a lack of ihtibas on her part. Therefore, the case is analogous (qiyas) to a husband who is majbub (castrated) or 'innin (impotent), where the wife's nafaqah remains wajib. The commentary adds that if both spouses are minors and incapable of intercourse, then by consensus (bila khilaf, according to al-Dhakhirah), the wife has no nafaqah. This ruling highlights the Hanafi emphasis on the wife's action (submission) as the basis for nafaqah, rather than the husband's ability to consummate.

Key Terms
تسلیم (taslim): The wife's act of submitting herself physically to the husband's authority, placing herself in his custody and available for marital relations.
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose penis has been severed, rendering him incapable of sexual intercourse.
عنین ('innin): A man who is impotent, unable to achieve or maintain an erection for intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She does not receive nafaqah because the marriage is not consummated.
B) She receives nafaqah because she has submitted and the inability is from the husband.
C) She gets nafaqah only after the husband reaches puberty.
D) She gets half nafaqah.

Key Takeaway
A wife's nafaqah in Hanafi law is based on her submission (taslim), not the husband's ability to consummate; thus, an adult wife of a minor husband receives nafaqah.

Imprisoned Wife: No Nafaqah Due to Her Own Default
Ruling on nafaqah for a wife imprisoned for debt due to her own fault

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafaqah for a wife imprisoned due to her own debt default and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil).

Core Idea
A wife's nafaqah drops when her own action (mumatalah) causes her imprisonment.

This lesson examines a specific case: a wife imprisoned for debt due to her own procrastination (mumatalah). The Hanafi school rules that the husband is not liable for nafaqah because the wife's confinement (ihtibas) is a result of her own fault. This ruling illustrates the general principle that nafaqah is contingent on the wife being available (tamkin) for the husband, and if her unavailability is self-inflicted, the obligation ceases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the wife's imprisonment for debt. The ruling, as per the Urdu heading and incomplete Arabic, is that nafaqah is not obligatory (lazim nahi).
The Arabic text likely contains a negation, though the exact wording is uncertain due to OCR issues.
2
Locate the cause (sabab) of the ruling
The legal cause is the wife's own 'mumatalah' (procrastination/default) in paying the debt, which led to her imprisonment. This is the reason the husband's obligation drops.
Mumatalah specifically means deliberate delay or refusal to pay a debt one is able to pay.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The loss of ihtibas (confinement/availability) is attributable to the wife herself (fawat al-ihtibas minha). Since she caused her own unavailability, the husband is not liable for nafaqah.
This aligns with the general Hanafi principle that nafaqah is due to the wife's tamkin (granting access). If tamkin is lost due to her fault, the obligation ceases.
4
Distinguish the opposite scenario
The text cuts off after 'if it is not from her, if she was...' (in lam yakun minha). This indicates that if the imprisonment is not due to her own fault (e.g., wrongful imprisonment or someone else's debt), the ruling may differ.
The full ruling for cases not due to her fault is not available in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا حبست المرأة فى دين فالنفقة لهالان فوت الاحتباس منها بالمماطلة وان لم يكن منها بان كانت ...
And if the woman is imprisoned for debt, then nafaqah [is not?] for her, because the loss of confinement is from her side due to procrastination (mumatalah), and if it is not from her, if she was...
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This lesson is a partial ruling from the text regarding a wife who is imprisoned for debt. According to the Urdu heading, the ruling is that such a woman does not receive nafaqah from her husband. The legal reason (ta'lil) is that the loss of ihtibas (confinement/availability) is due to her own default (mumatalah, i.e., refusing to pay the debt she owes). Since she is imprisoned as a result of her own actions, the husband is not liable for nafaqah. If the imprisonment is not due to her own fault (e.g., she is wrongfully imprisoned or imprisoned for someone else's debt), the ruling may differ, but the text cuts off. This ruling aligns with the general principle that nafaqah is dropped when the wife's unavailability is due to her own cause.

Key Terms
مماطلة (mumatalah): Procrastination or deliberate default in paying a debt, leading to imprisonment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Maintenance for a Sick Wife: Qiyas vs. Istihsan
Explains the ruling and istihsan for maintenance when wife is sick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance for a sick wife, explain the qiyas objection, and justify the istihsan preference including Abu Yusuf's distinction.

Core Idea
A sick wife deserves maintenance because confinement (iḥtibās) remains in companionship and housework, like menstruation.

The right of a wife to maintenance (nafaqah) is tied to her confinement (iḥtibās) in her husband's home. But what if she falls ill and cannot perform sexual duties? The strict qiyas would deny maintenance, but the Hanafi school overrides this with istihsan, recognizing that confinement continues in other forms. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and also presents a finer distinction attributed to Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State the core Hanafi ruling: a sick wife in the husband's house is entitled to maintenance even if the illness prevents intercourse.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Present the qiyas objection
Explain the qiyas argument: since maintenance compensates for iḥtibās (confinement for sexual enjoyment), and illness negates that ability, the qiyas would drop maintenance.
The effective cause (ʿillah) is confinement for sexual enjoyment.
3
Explain the istihsan reasoning
Describe how istihsan overrides qiyas: confinement remains because the husband still enjoys her companionship, she protects the house, and the impediment is temporary, analogous to menstruation where maintenance is due.
Istihsan is based on a stronger consideration (taqlīb al‑naẓar).
4
Note Abu Yusuf's distinction
Abu Yusuf differentiates: if she submitted healthy then fell ill, maintenance due; if she submitted while already ill, not due because submission was invalid.
The mashāyikh consider this view good (ḥasan).
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The general Hanafi position (zāhir al‑riwāyah) is that maintenance is due regardless of the order, but Abu Yusuf's detail is approved and often followed.
The weight of authority is zāhir al‑riwāyah with tarjīh from later scholars.

Source Text

And if she is sick in the husband's house, maintenance is due to her. By qiyas, no maintenance is due when the illness prevents intercourse because confinement for enjoyment is lost. The istihsan reason is that confinement remains: He finds comfort in her, touches her, and she protects the house, and the impediment is temporary, so it resembles menstruation. From Abu Yusuf: If she submitted herself then became sick, maintenance is due because submission is realized; if she became sick then submitted, it is not due because submission was not valid. They said this is good, and the wording of the book indicates it. Translation: If a woman becomes sick in her husband's house, maintenance is wajib for her. Qiyas says it should not be wajib if the illness prevents intercourse because confinement for intercourse is lost. The istihsan reason is that confinement is still present: the husband will find comfort in her, touch her, and she protects the house, and the impediment to intercourse is temporary, so this illness resembles menstruation. It is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if the woman submitted herself first then became sick, maintenance remains wajib because submission has been realized; if she became sick then submitted, maintenance is not wajib because submission was not valid. Our mashayikh said this view is good, and the wording of the book also indicates this. Explanation: If a woman becomes sick while in her husband's house, maintenance is wajib for her, whether the illness prevents intercourse or not. Qiyas requires that if the illness prevents intercourse, maintenance should not be wajib because the confinement for intercourse is lost, and since maintenance is compensation for confinement, it would drop. The istihsan reason is that confinement is still present: the husband finds comfort with the sick woman, touches her, and enjoys her, and she protects the house, and the impediment to intercourse is temporary, so this illness resembles menstruation. Just as during menstruation, which prevents intercourse, maintenance is wajib, similarly during illness, even if it prevents intercourse, maintenance is wajib. From Imam Abu Yusuf: If the woman submitted herself to her husband first then became sick, maintenance is wajib for her; if she became sick first then submitted, maintenance is not wajib. The difference is that in the first case, submission from her side is found, while in the second case, due to illness, submission is not valid. Our mashayikh said this detail is appropriate, and the wording in Quduri also indicates this.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi ruling on maintenance (nafaqah) for a wife who falls ill in her husband's home. The ruling is that maintenance remains obligatory despite the illness, even if it prevents sexual intercourse. The text first presents a qiyas (analogical reasoning) that would negate maintenance because the purpose of confinement (ih'tibas) — that is, the wife being available for her husband's sexual enjoyment — is absent due to the illness. Since maintenance is considered a compensation for this confinement, the qiyas suggests it should drop. However, the preferred position (istihsan) overrides this analogy. The istihsan reasoning is that a different form of confinement still exists: the husband derives comfort and companionship from her, she protects his household, and the impediment is merely an incidental condition (like menstruation). Since maintenance is obligatory during menstruation despite the same impediment, the same applies to illness. The passage also records a detailed view from Imam Abu Yusuf: if the wife submitted herself to her husband at a time when she was healthy, then later fell ill, maintenance is due because valid submission preceded the illness. But if she was already ill at the time of submission and then submitted, the submission is not considered valid (since she could not fulfill the essential purpose), so maintenance is not due. The author notes that this view is praised by the mashayikh (later scholars) and is supported by the wording of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The overall message is that the husband's obligation for maintenance is robust and not easily terminated by the wife's temporary inability to engage in intercourse.

Key Terms
احتباس (ihtibas): The wife's confinement in the husband's house and her availability for his enjoyment, which is the basis for maintenance.
استحسان (istihsan): Equitable preference that overrides strict qiyas based on a stronger textual or rational consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the istihsan presented, why does a sick wife in her husband's house still deserve maintenance despite being unable to have intercourse?
A) Because maintenance is solely for food, not for companionship.
B) Because confinement still exists through companionship, housekeeping, and the temporary nature of the impediment, similar to menstruation.
C) Because the wife is considered healthy by legal fiction.
D) Because the husband must pay regardless of any condition.

Key Takeaway
A wife's temporary illness does not suspend her right to maintenance because the confinement (iḥtibās) remains in multiple forms, and istiḥsān overrides strict qiyās.

Husband's Obligation for Wife's Servant When Wealthy
States and explains ruling that wealthy husband must provide for wife's servant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wealthy husband's obligation to provide a servant for his wife and explain the legal basis of kifayah.

Core Idea
A wealthy husband must provide a servant for his wife because kifayah requires fulfilling all her needs, including domestic help.

In this passage, the commentator expands on al-Quduri's ruling that a wealthy husband must provide maintenance for his wife's servant. The ruling is not merely about the wife's own nafaqah but specifically about the servant's provision. Understanding the concept of kifayah (sufficiency) is key to grasping why this obligation arises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the act: providing maintenance (nafaqah) for the wife's servant. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) upon the husband if he is wealthy.
The act is separate from the wife's own maintenance, which is also wajib.
2
Specify the condition (shart)
The obligation is conditional upon the husband being wealthy (maysar). Wealth means having surplus beyond basic needs, akin to owning nisab.
If the husband is not wealthy, this obligation does not apply.
3
Understand the legal basis (wajh)
The basis is the duty of kifayah (providing sufficiency). The husband must provide everything his wife needs for a comfortable life. For a wealthy woman, a servant is a necessity, so providing one completes her kifayah.
Kifayah goes beyond mere subsistence; it varies with social status.
4
Note the corollary on compulsion
The wife cannot be forced to do housework if she has no servant. Her only obligation is to allow her husband access to herself; she does not owe domestic labor.
This distinguishes her obligation from the servant's: the servant must serve to receive nafaqah.
5
Distinguish the servant's entitlement
If the servant refuses to serve, he or she loses the right to maintenance. The servant's nafaqah is tied to performance of service.
The wife's nafaqah is not conditioned on service.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتفرض على الزوج النفقة اذا كان موسر او نفقة خادمها والمراد بهذا بيان نفقة الخادم ولهذا ذكر في بعض النسخ وتفرض على الزوج اذاكان موسر انفقة خادمها ووجهه ان كفايتها واجبة عليه وهذا من تمامها اذ لا بدلها منه ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا۔ اور جب شوہر مالدار ہو تو اس پر بیوی کا نفقہ اور اس کے خادم کا نفقہ فرض کیا جائے گا۔ اور مراد اس سے خادم کے نفقہ کا بیان کرنا ہے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے بعض نسخوں میں مذکور ہے وتفرض على الزوج اذا كان موسراً نفقته خادمها یعنی شوہر جب مالدار ہو تو اس پر اس کی بیوی کے خادم کا نفقہ فرض کیا جائے گا۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر بیوی کی کفایت واجب ہے۔ اور خادم کا نفقہ عورت کی کفایت پورا کرنے میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے کہ عورت کے واسطے خادم کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر مالدار ہو تو اس پر اس کی بیوی اور بیوی کے خادم کا نفقہ واجب ہوگا۔ چونکہ بظاہر یہ عبارت بیوی کے نفقہ میں مکر رہے۔ اس لئے مصنف نے عذر کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ یہاں بیوی کے خادم کا نفقہ بیان کرنا مقصود ہے نہ کہ بیوی کا نفقہ۔ اسی وجہ سے قدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں عبارت اس طرح ہے۔ تفرض على الزوج اذا كان موسرا نفقة خادمها - خادم کے نفقہ کے واجب ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر عورت کی کفایت واجب ہے۔ اور عورت کی پوری کفایت ہوگی خادم کا نفقہ فرض کرنے سے۔ اس لئے عورت کے واسطے اس کے خادم کا نفقہ ضروری ہے۔ خادم غلام ہو یا باندی ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ اگر عورت کے لئے خادم نہ ہو تو کیا اس کو خود کام کرنے پر مجبور کیا جاسکتا ہے یا نہیں۔ تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت کام کرنے سے انکار کر دے تو اس کو اس پر مجبور نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ کیونکہ عورت پر فقط شوہر کو اپنے نفس پر قدرت دینا واجب ہے۔ یہ اعمال واجب نہیں ہیں۔ اس کے برخلاف خادم اگر خدمت کرنے سے رک گیا تو وہ نفقہ کا مستحق نہیں ہوگا۔
He said: Maintenance is made obligatory upon the husband if he is wealthy — or maintenance of her servant. What is meant by this is the statement of the servant's maintenance. For this reason, in some copies it is mentioned: 'Maintenance is made obligatory upon the husband, if he is wealthy, for the maintenance of her servant.' The reason is that providing for her needs (kifayah) is obligatory upon him, and this is part of fulfilling it, because she cannot do without it. Translation: Quduri said: When the husband is wealthy, maintenance for the wife and her servant is made obligatory. What is meant by this is the statement of the servant's maintenance. Therefore, in some manuscripts it is mentioned: 'Maintenance is made obligatory upon the husband, if he is wealthy, for the maintenance of her servant.' That is, when the husband is wealthy, the maintenance of his wife's servant is made obligatory upon him. The reason is that the husband is obligated to provide for the wife's needs (kifayah), and the servant's maintenance is part of completing her kifayah because the wife needs a servant. Explanation: If the husband is wealthy, he must provide maintenance for his wife and for her servant. Since at first glance this text seems to repeat the wife's maintenance, the author explains that here the intention is to state the servant's maintenance, not the wife's. Hence in some manuscripts of Quduri the text is: 'Maintenance is made obligatory upon the husband, if he is wealthy, for the maintenance of her servant.' The reason the servant's maintenance is wajib is that the husband is obliged to provide for the wife's kifayah, and her complete kifayah is achieved by providing the servant's maintenance, because the wife needs a servant — whether a male or female slave. As for whether the wife can be forced to do work if she has no servant: If she refuses to work, she cannot be forced because the wife's obligation is only to give her husband control over her person; these acts are not obligatory. On the other hand, if the servant stops serving, he is not entitled to maintenance.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage expounds a ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar regarding the husband's obligation to provide a servant for his wife when he is wealthy (maysar). The core ruling is that a wealthy husband must pay for the maintenance (nafaqah) of the wife's servant, in addition to the wife's own maintenance. The author clarifies that the text is primarily concerned with establishing the servant's maintenance, not simply repeating the wife's. The legal basis (wajh) is that the husband's duty to provide kifayah (sufficiency) for his wife includes everything she needs for a comfortable life. Since a wife of a wealthy man typically requires a servant for household tasks, providing a servant is part of completing that kifayah. The passage also touches on a related point: if the wife does not have a servant, she cannot be compelled to do the housework herself; her only obligation is to be available for her husband. Conversely, if a servant fails to serve, the servant forfeits the right to maintenance. This reflects the Hanafi position that a wife's maintenance is not conditioned on her performing domestic labor.

Key Terms
كفاية (kifayah): Sufficiency or provision of all necessary needs for a comfortable life, which for a wealthy man includes a servant for his wife.
موسر (maysar): Wealthy or financially comfortable; the condition that triggers the obligation to provide a servant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal basis (wajh) for the obligation of a wealthy husband to provide a servant's maintenance?
A) Because the husband is required to give his wife a gift every year.
B) Because the wife's complete kifayah (sufficiency) requires a servant, and that is obligatory on the husband.
C) Because the servant is a separate dependent of the husband.
D) Because the wife cannot work at all.

Key Takeaway
A wealthy husband must provide a servant for his wife as part of his duty to ensure her complete sufficiency (kifayah), and the wife cannot be forced to do housework in lieu of a servant.

The Number of Servants in Nafaqah: One or Two?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the quantity of servant maintenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the number of servants in nafaqah, explain the proofs for each, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
One servant suffices for both interior and exterior tasks; requiring two is unnecessary.

This passage records a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute on how many servants a wealthy husband must provide for his wife. The majority view limits it to one, while Abu Yusuf argues for two. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists balance necessity (darurah) and custom (urf) in determining maintenance obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State clearly what Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold versus what Abu Yusuf holds regarding the number of servants.
One vs. two servants.
2
Understand the reasoning of each side
Write down the key argument: one servant can handle both interior and exterior tasks vs. the need for separate servants for each domain.
The debate hinges on whether one person can realistically manage both.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Abu Yusuf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that necessity dictates only what is needed; there is no compelling need for two because one suffices. They also use qiyas on the husband himself: if he did the work personally, it would be enough; so his substitute (one servant) is enough.
This is a qiyas jaliy: the servant stands in the husband's place.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentary (Sharh al-Hidayah) and the later tradition prefer the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, making it the operative position for fatwa.
Thus, a wealthy husband is obliged to pay maintenance for only one servant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لا تفرض لاكثر من نفقة خادم واحد وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وقال ابويوسف تفرض الخادمين لانها تحتاج الى احد هما لمصالح الداخل والى الأخر لمصالح الخارج ولهما ان الواحد يقوم بالأمرين فلا ضرورة الى اثنين و لانه لوتولى كفايتها بنفسه كان كافيا فكذا اذاقام الواحد مقام نفسه وقالوان الزوج الموسريلزمه من نفقة الخادم ما يلزم المعسر من نفقة امرأته وهو ادنى الكفاية وقوله في الكتاب اذا كان
And maintenance is not made obligatory for more than one servant. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: Maintenance is made obligatory for two servants, because she needs one for internal affairs and another for external affairs. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) argument is that one servant can handle both matters, so there is no need for two. And because if he himself undertook her kifayah, it would be sufficient, so likewise when one servant takes his place. They said: The wealthy husband is obliged to pay for the servant's maintenance just as the poor husband is obliged to pay his wife's maintenance, and that is the minimum sufficiency. And his statement in the book: 'if he is...'
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of servants a wealthy husband must provide for his wife. The majority view of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that only one servant's maintenance is wajib, because one servant is sufficient to handle both domestic (interior) and external (exterior) tasks. Abu Yusuf argues for two servants, one for internal household work and another for outside errands. The reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is based on necessity (darurah): since only one is needed, requiring two would be excessive. They analogize to the husband himself: if he personally managed her affairs, he would suffice, so a single substitute suffices. Additionally, the obligation for a wealthy husband is analogous to that of a poor husband, which is only the minimum sufficiency (adna al-kifayah). The text ends mid-sentence, but the disput e is clear. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, limiting it to one servant. This reflects the school's principle of avoiding extravagance while fulfilling essential needs.

Key Terms
أدنى الكفاية (adna al-kifayah): The minimum sufficiency; the baseline standard of provision required for a wife, which for a wealthy husband is extended to include one servant.
مصالح الداخل والخارج (masalih al-dakhil wa al-kharij): Internal affairs (household work) and external affairs (errands outside the home) that indicate the need for separate servants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, how many servants' maintenance is a wealthy husband obligated to provide?
A) Two servants, one for interior and one for exterior work.
B) No servant is obligatory at all.
C) One servant is sufficient.
D) The number depends on the wife's desire.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that only one servant's maintenance is wajib, as one servant can meet both interior and exterior needs.

Maintenance of the Wife's Servant and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Number
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of servants' maintenance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maintenance of the wife's servant and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the number of servants.

Core Idea
A wealthy husband must provide maintenance for one servant for his wife; Abu Yusuf's view for two is not the relied-upon position.

In this lesson, we examine the obligation of a wealthy husband to provide maintenance for his wife's servant. While the basic ruling is clear, there is an important internal Hanafi dispute: do we require one servant or two? Understanding this disagreement and the proofs behind each position is essential for applying the correct mufta bihi in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Start by extracting the central ruling: when a husband is wealthy, he must provide maintenance (nafaqah) for the wife and her servant. The passage clarifies that the primary focus is the servant's nafaqah, not the wife's.
The wife's own nafaqah is already established elsewhere; this text addresses the additional obligation.
2
State the majority position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
Recognize that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that only one servant's maintenance is wajib. Their reasoning is that one servant can perform both indoor and outdoor tasks, so no need for two.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
3
State the dissenting view (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf argues for two servants: one for internal affairs and one for external affairs. He believes the wife's needs necessitate separate servants for different duties.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab one.
4
Compare the proofs (talil)
Analyze the talil (legal reasoning) on both sides. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rely on the principle that one capable person (the husband) suffices, so one substitute suffices. Abu Yusuf focuses on the distinct nature of internal and external tasks.
The majority view uses qiyas with the husband himself as the original case (asl).
5
Determine the thamarah and tarjih
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Abu Yusuf, a wealthy husband owes two servants' nafaqah; under the majority, only one. The tarjih (preference) is given to the majority view, supported by the mashāyikh and aligned with the minimum sufficiency (adnā al-kifāyah).
This tarjih is confirmed in later Hanafi works like al-Hidayah.

The maintenance of the wife and her servant is obligatory upon a wealthy husband. He (al-Quduri) said: The husband is assigned maintenance if he is wealthy, or the maintenance of her servant. What is meant by this is a statement of the servant's maintenance. For this reason, in some copies it is mentioned: 'The husband is assigned, if he is wealthy, the maintenance of her servant.' Its reason is that her sufficiency is obligatory upon him, and this is part of its completion, because there is no alternative to it for her. Translation: Al-Quduri said: When the husband is wealthy, the maintenance of the wife and the maintenance of her servant is made obligatory upon him. And what is meant by this is to state the servant's maintenance. For this reason, in some copies it is stated: 'The husband is assigned, if he is wealthy, the maintenance of her servant.' That is, when the husband is wealthy, the maintenance of his wife's servant is made obligatory upon him. Its reason is that the husband is obliged to provide for the wife, and the servant's maintenance is part of completing her sufficiency, because the wife necessarily needs a servant. Explanation: If the husband is wealthy, the maintenance of his wife and her servant is obligatory upon him. Since apparently this statement is repeating the wife's maintenance, the author apologized and said that here the intention is to state the servant's maintenance, not the wife's. For this reason, in some copies of al-Quduri, the text is: 'The husband is assigned, if he is wealthy, the maintenance of her servant.' The reason for the servant's maintenance being obligatory is that the husband is obliged to provide for the wife, and the wife's full sufficiency is achieved by imposing the servant's maintenance. Therefore, the servant's maintenance is necessary for the wife, whether the servant is a male slave or a female slave. As for the issue: if the wife has no servant, can she be forced to work? The ruling is that if she refuses to work, she cannot be forced, because the wife is only obliged to grant the husband control over her person; these actions are not obligatory. Conversely, if the servant stops serving, he is not entitled to maintenance. One servant or more: is the maintenance of more than one servant obligatory? Statements of the jurists. And the maintenance of more than one servant is not imposed. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: The maintenance of two servants is imposed because she needs one for internal affairs and the other for external affairs. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) proof is that one servant can perform both tasks, so there is no need for two. And because if he (the husband) undertakes her sufficiency himself, it suffices. So likewise, when one person takes his place, it suffices. And they said: The wealthy husband is obligated from the servant's maintenance what is obligated from the poor husband for his wife's maintenance, which is the minimum sufficiency.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the maintenance (nafaqah) of the wife's servant. It begins by clarifying the ruling: when a husband is wealthy (mūsir), he is obligated to provide maintenance for his wife and her servant. The author explains that the text of al-Quduri primarily aims to establish the servant's maintenance, not the wife's, since the wife's maintenance is already known. The rationale is that the husband must ensure the wife's comprehensive sufficiency (kifāyah), which necessitates a servant. The passage then addresses whether the wife can be forced to work if she lacks a servant; the Hanafi position is that she cannot, as she only owes the husband access to her person, not domestic labor. The core of the lesson is the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of servants. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, only one servant's maintenance is obligatory, while Abu Yusuf argues for two (one for indoor tasks and one for outdoor). Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's evidence is that a single servant can handle both spheres, and analogically, if the husband himself performs the duties, one person suffices; thus, one substitute is enough. The mashāyikh further state that the wealthy husband's obligation for the servant's maintenance is limited to the minimum sufficiency (adnā al-kifāyah), comparable to what a poor husband must provide for his wife.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance or financial support, including food, clothing, and lodging, obligatory upon the husband for the wife and her servant.
خادم (khādim): Servant, either male or female, whose maintenance the husband must provide if the wife needs one.
ادنى الكفاية (adnā al-kifāyah): The minimum sufficiency; the lowest level of maintenance that suffices for basic needs.
