Servant's Maintenance and the Poor Husband: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on servant's nafaqah for a poor husband.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a poor husband's obligation to provide nafaqah for his wife's servant and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
A poor husband is not obligated to maintain his wife's servant; the wife's own service suffices for the minimum sufficiency.

This lesson clarifies a conditional element of servant's nafaqah in marriage. Imam al-Quduri's phrase 'إذا كان' hints that wealth is a condition. The passage explores the dispute within the Hanafi school: while the majority view from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan) holds that a poor husband owes no servant's nafaqah, Imam Muhammad makes a distinction if the wife already has a servant. We will trace the proofs and see why the mashāyikh prefer the former.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for servant's nafaqah
From the text, identify the key condition stated by Imam al-Quduri: servant's nafaqah is wajib only when the husband is wealthy (mūsir). The phrase 'إذا كان' points to this.
The condition is the husband's wealth, not the wife's.
2
Recognize the two intra-Hanafi positions
Note the difference: Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad): no obligation for a poor husband. Imam Muhammad: obligation if the wife has a servant; otherwise not.
Muhammad's view is conditional on the wife already having a servant.
3
Examine the proof (dalil) for each
Abu Hanifa's proof: the poor are only obligated for minimum sufficiency (adnā al-kifāyah), and the wife can serve herself. Muhammad's proof: if the wife has a servant, that servant's need exists and must be maintained.
The talil (reasoning) is based on what constitutes necessity.
4
Understand the tarjih mechanism
The text declares Hasan's narration as 'al-aṣaḥḥ' (most correct) and the mashāyikh prefer it. The preference is based on the strength of the dalil and practical ease.
Tarjih is not arbitrary; it follows a scholarly methodology.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: a poor husband following the preferred view pays no servant's nafaqah; following Muhammad's view, he pays if the wife has a servant.
The difference directly affects the husband's financial obligation.

طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک خادم گھر کے اندر اور باہر دونوں کاموں کو پورا کر سکتا ہے۔ لہذا دو خادموں کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر بذات خود بیوی کے کاموں کی پرداخت کرے تو کافی ہو جائے پس اسی طرح اگر شوہر نے اپنی جگہ یک شخص کو مقرر کر دیا تو بھی کافی ہے۔

And his statement in the book: 'إذا كان' (if he is). It indicates that the servant's maintenance is not obligatory when he (the husband) is poor. This is the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa, and it is the most correct, contrary to what Muhammad said, because what is obligatory upon the poor is the minimum sufficiency, and she (the wife) can suffice with her own service. Translation: Al-Quduri said in the book that the servant's maintenance is obligatory only when the husband is wealthy. This indicates that if the husband is poor, the servant's maintenance is not obligatory upon him. This is the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa, and it is the most correct, contrary to Muhammad's statement, because upon the poor, the minimum sufficiency is obligatory, and the wife can herself suffice with her own service. Explanation: The husband is not obligated to provide maintenance for more than one servant. This ruling is agreed upon by both parties, and it is the majority opinion, including Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. Imam Abu Yusuf said that the husband is obligated to provide maintenance for two servants. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that the wife needs two servants: one for indoor work and one for outdoor. Another narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is that if the wife is very wealthy and brought many female servants in her dowry, then the maintenance of all servants is obligatory. Hisham narrated this from Imam Muhammad, and Imam Tahawi adopted it. The proof of the two parties (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that one servant can perform both indoor and outdoor tasks, so there is no need for two. Another proof: if the husband himself performs the wife's tasks, it suffices; similarly, if he appoints one person in his place, it suffices. The mashāyikh said that the wealthy husband is obligated to give for the wife's servant what the poor husband is obligated for his wife's maintenance, i.e., the lowest level of sufficiency. The conclusion is that the amount that is obligatory upon a poor husband for his wife's maintenance is the same amount that is obligatory for the servant's maintenance. And what Imam al-Quduri said, 'إذا كان موسرا' (if he is wealthy), indicates that if the husband is poor, the servant's maintenance is not obligatory upon him. This is the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa, and this narration is more correct. Imam Muhammad's statement is that if the husband is poor and the wife has a servant, the servant's maintenance is obligatory upon the husband; but if she has no servant, then the husband's servant's maintenance is not imposed. The proof for Hasan's narration is that upon the poor, the minimum sufficiency is obligatory, and the wife can herself suffice with her own service. Therefore, the servant's maintenance is not obligatory upon a poor husband.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This lesson continues from the previous and addresses a critical condition: the servant's nafaqah is contingent on the husband being wealthy (mūsir). The author quotes al-Quduri's phrase 'إذا كان' (if he is) as an indicator that when the husband is poor (muʿsir), the servant's nafaqah is not obligatory. The preferred view (al-aṣaḥḥ) is the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyād from Abu Hanifa, which states no servant's nafaqah for a poor husband. This opposes Imam Muhammad's view, who differentiates: if the wife already possesses a servant, the poor husband must maintain it; otherwise not. The mashāyikh settle the matter by equating the wealthy husband's obligation for the servant's nafaqah to the poor husband's obligation for his wife's nafaqah, i.e., the minimum sufficiency (adnā al-kifāyah). The rationale for Hasan's narration is that a poor husband is only liable for the bare minimum, and the wife can manage her own affairs without a servant. Thus, the practical ruling is that a poor husband is not required to provide a servant's nafaqah, aligning with the text's indication.

Key Terms
اعسار (iʿsār): Poverty or financial inability; the condition of being unable to afford maintenance.
مفلس (muflis): Insolvent or bankrupt; used synonymously with muʿsir in this context.
اصح (aṣaḥḥ): The most correct; indicates the preferred narration or ruling among multiple options.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Can Poverty Justify Divorce? Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Nafaqah
Inter-madhhab dispute on nafaqah and tafriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on judicial separation due to poverty and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using qiyas.

Core Idea
Poverty does not dissolve a marriage — the Quran commands respite for the debtor, and nafaqah is a debt.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: can a wife seek annulment of her marriage because her husband cannot provide maintenance? Imam al-Shafi'i argues by analogy to impotence, while the Hanafi school relies on the Quranic injunction for respite and a sharp distinction between primary and subsidiary purposes of marriage. We will examine both proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate that in Hanafi law, a husband's inability to pay nafaqah does not entitle the wife to judicial separation.
The marriage remains valid; the wife must wait or take a loan.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes the insolvent husband to an impotent man (maktu' al-dhakar), where separation is allowed. He also cites a hadith and a mursal report.
The analogy is based on the idea that inability to fulfill marital duties justifies annulment.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Quranic dalil
The Hanafi school relies on Quran 2:280, which commands giving respite to a debtor in difficulty. Nafaqah is considered a debt, so the wife must wait until the husband becomes wealthy.
This is a direct textual proof (nass) overriding analogy.
4
Examine the Hanafi response: qiyas ma'a al-fariq
The Hanafi response refutes the analogy by highlighting a crucial difference: inability in the primary purpose of marriage (intercourse) vs. inability in a subsidiary matter (wealth). The qiyas is therefore invalid.
The rational argument also holds that nullifying the husband's right (marriage contract) is a greater harm than delaying the wife's right to nafaqah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In Hanafi law, a wife cannot obtain divorce due to poverty; she must wait. In Shafi'i law, she can seek judicial separation.
This affects legal advice and court decisions in different madhhabs.

باب النفقة
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر نفقہ نہ دینے کی وجہ سے امساک بالمعروف سے عاجز ہو گیا تو شوہر پر تسریح بالاحسان ( خوبصورتی کے ساتھ چھوڑنا لازم آیا۔ اور چونکہ شوہر تسریح بالاحسان سے رک گیا۔ اس لئے قاضی تسریح بالاحسان میں شوہر کے قائم مقام ہو کر میاں بیوی کے درمیان تفریق کر دے۔ جیسا کہ مقطوع الذکر اور نامراد اگر اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دیگر جدا نہ کرے تو قاضی قائم مقام ہو کر تفریق کر دے گا۔ بلکہ نفقہ سے عاجز ہونے کی صورت میں بدرجہ اولی تفریق کرے۔ اس لئے کہ بہ نسبت جماع کے نفقہ کی ضرورت بہت قوی ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک مدت تک نفقہ کا منقطع ہونا ہلاکت کا سبب ہے۔ لیکن جماع کا منقطع ہونا باعث ہلاکت نہیں ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ امام شافعی نے عاجز عن النفقہ کو مقطوع الذکر اور نامرد پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ امام شافعی کے قول کی تائید حدیث ابی ہریرہ سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔ حدیث ان النبی صلی اللہ عليه وسلم قال المراة تقول لزوجها اطعمني او طلقنی حضور اقدس صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ عورت اپنے شوہر سے کہے کہ مجھ کو کھانا دے یا طلاق دے۔
اور ابوالزناد کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے سعید بن المسیب سے دریافت کیا کہ جو شخص اپنی بیوی کو نفقہ دینے کی قدرت نہ رکھتا ہو تو کیا ان دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے گی ۔ تو سعید بن المسیب نے فرمایا ہاں۔ میں نے کہا کہ کیا یہ سنت ہے۔ سعید بن المسیب نے جواب دیا ہاں سنت ہے اور چونکہ لفظ سنت مطلق ہے۔ اس لئے سنت کا فرد کامل یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی سنت مراد ہو گی ۔ امام شافعی مراسیل کے قائل ہیں۔ اس لئے اس کو حجت میں پیش کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
اور ہماری دلیل منقول باری تعالیٰ کا قول و إن كانَ ذو عسرة فنظرة الى ميسرة ہے۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ نفقہ نتیجتا شوہر کے ذمہ دین ہوتا ہے۔ اور شوہر تنگدست ہو گیا اور قرآنی حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر مدیون تنگدست ہو جائے تو دائن یعنی قرض خواہ اس کو مالدار ہونے تک مہلت دے۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ شوہر کے مفلس ہونے کی وجہ سے تفریق نہ کی جائے بلکہ عورت اس کو مہلت دیدے۔ اور دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ اگر تفریق کی جائے تو شوہر کا حق بالکلیہ باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور عورت کا حق ایسا ہے کہ اس میں تاخیر ہو سکتی ہے کیونکہ جب قاضی نے نفقہ مقرر کر دیا تو وہ شوہر کے ذمہ قرضہ ہوتا ہے۔ پس عورت اس سے آئندہ زمانے میں وصول کر لے گی۔ اور شوہر کے حق کا بالکلیہ باطل ہو جانا ضرر میں بڑھا ہوا ہے۔ پس اعلیٰ ضرر کو دور کرنے کے لئے ادنی ضرر کو برداشت کر لیا جائے گا۔ وفوت المال سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ عاجز عن النفقہ یعنی مفلس شوہر کو مقطوع الذکر اور نامرد پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جو شخص نفقہ سے عاجز ہے وہ صرف مال سے عاجز ہے اور نکاح میں مال مقصود اصلی نہیں بلکہ تابع ہے اور جو شخص مقطوع الذکر اور نامرد ہونے کی وجہ سے بیوی کے ساتھ جماع سے عاجز ہے وہ نکاح کے مقصود اصلی یعنی تو الدم تناسل سے عاجز ہے۔ پس اگر نکاح کے مقصود اصلی یعنی توالد و تناسل سے عاجز ہونے کی صورت میں تفریق کو جائز قرار دیا گیا تو اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا کہ جو چیز نکاح میں تابع ہے۔ یعنی مال اگر اس سے عاجز ہو جائے تو بھی تفریق جائز ہوگی۔ رہی یہ بات کہ جب قاضی نے عورت کے لئے نفقہ مقرر کر دیا تو عورت کو قرضہ لینے کی اجازت دینے میں کیا فائدہ ہے۔ کیونکہ قاضی کے مقرر کر دینے سے نفقہ شوہر کے ذمہ قرضہ ہو گیا۔ جواب قاضی کے نفقہ مقرر کر دینے کے باوجود قرضہ لینے کی اجازت دینے میں یہ فائدہ ہے کہ عورت اپنے قرض خواہ کو اپنے شوہر پر حوالہ کر سکتی ہے۔ اور اگر عورت نے بغیر قاضی کے حکم کے قرضہ لیا ہے تو قرض خواہ صرف عورت سے مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے۔ شوہر سے مطالبہ کا حق نہیں ہوگا۔
Chapter of Nafaqah. Imam Shafi'i's proof: Since the husband becomes unable to retain [his wife] with kindness due to not giving nafaqah, then releasing with kindness becomes necessary upon him. And since he refrains from releasing with kindness, the qadi acts in his place in releasing with kindness and separates them. Just as in the case of a man with severed penis or impotent man who does not divorce his wife, the qadi acts in his place and separates. Rather, in the case of inability to pay nafaqah, separation is more appropriate because the need for nafaqah is stronger than intercourse, since cutting off nafaqah for a period causes destruction, while cutting off intercourse does not cause destruction. In summary, Imam Shafi'i analogized the one unable to pay nafaqah to the man with severed penis and the impotent man. His view is also supported by the hadith of Abu Hurairah: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'The woman says to her husband: Feed me or divorce me.' And Abu al-Zinad said: I asked Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab about a man who cannot provide nafaqah to his wife, will they be separated? He said yes. I said, is this Sunnah? He said yes, and since the word Sunnah is absolute, it refers to the complete individual of Sunnah, i.e., the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Imam Shafi'i accepts mursal [hadith], so this can be presented as proof. Our proof from transmission is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And if [the debtor] is in difficulty, then postpone until ease.' The reasoning is that nafaqah becomes a debt upon the husband, and the husband has become impoverished, and the Quranic command is that if the debtor becomes poor, the creditor gives him respite until he becomes wealthy. Thus it is established that separation is not caused by the husband's insolvency; rather the woman should give him respite. And rational proof: If separation is made, the husband's right would be completely nullified, while the woman's right can be delayed because when the qadi fixes nafaqah, it becomes a debt upon the husband, so she can collect it in the future. And completely nullifying the husband's right is a greater harm, so the lesser harm is tolerated to remove the greater harm. 'Wa fawt al-mal' is the response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy. The essence of the response: comparing the one unable to pay nafaqah (the insolvent husband) to the man with severed penis and impotent man is an analogy with a difference, because the one unable to pay nafaqah is only unable in terms of wealth, and wealth in marriage is not the primary purpose but subsidiary, while the man with severed penis or impotent man is unable to perform intercourse, which is the primary purpose of marriage (i.e., procreation). So if separation is permitted for inability in the primary purpose of marriage, it does not follow that separation is permitted for inability in a subsidiary matter (wealth). As for the point: when the qadi fixes nafaqah for the woman, what benefit is there in allowing her to take a loan? Because by the qadi's fixing, the nafaqah becomes a debt upon the husband. The answer: the benefit of allowing her to take a loan despite the qadi's fixing is that the woman can refer her creditor to her husband. And if she took a loan without the qadi's order, the creditor can only demand from the woman; he has no right to demand from the husband.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a husband's inability to pay nafaqah entitles the wife to seek judicial separation (tafriq). Imam al-Shafi'i argues that just as a husband with erectile dysfunction or an impotent man (maktu' al-dhakar or 'innin) who cannot fulfill the purpose of marriage (intercourse) is subject to judicial separation, similarly a husband unable to pay nafaqah should face separation, because inability to provide sustenance poses a greater harm (destruction) than inability to have intercourse. He supports this with a hadith where the wife may demand food or divorce, and a mursal report from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab. The Hanafi position, presented as the author's own, relies on the Quranic verse (2:280) which demands respite for the debtor in difficulty. Nafaqah is a debt; poverty does not nullify the marriage. Rational argument: separation would completely void the husband's right (the marriage contract), while the wife's right can be delayed; she can collect nafaqah later when he becomes wealthy. The Hanafi response refutes the analogy (qiyas) by distinguishing between inability in the primary purpose of marriage (intercession/procreation) and inability in a subsidiary matter (wealth). The latter does not warrant separation. Additionally, the qadi's fixing of nafaqah helps the wife by allowing her to refer creditors to the husband; without it, she alone is liable.

Key Terms
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance, food, clothing, and lodging that a husband must provide to his wife.
امساك بالمعروف (imsak bi al-ma'ruf): Retaining one's wife with kindness as commanded by Allah; usually fulfilled by providing nafaqah.
تسريح بالاحسان (tasrih bi al-ihsan): Releasing a wife with kindness, i.e., proper divorce without harm.
مقطوع الذكر (maktu' al-dhakar): A man whose penis is cut off, unable to have sexual intercourse.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because there is a legally significant difference between the original case and the new case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i analogy between inability to pay nafaqah and impotence?
A) Impotence is a greater harm than poverty.
B) Wealth is a subsidiary purpose of marriage; intercourse is the primary purpose.
C) The hadith of Abu Hurairah is not authentic.
D) The Quran allows divorce for any harm.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a husband's poverty does not dissolve the marriage; the wife must wait until he can pay, as nafaqah is a debt subject to Quranic respite.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Slave's Marriage to Free Woman: Maintenance as Debt
Ruling with qiyas proof on slave's maintenance debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's maintenance obligation for a free wife, explain the qiyas proof that makes it a debt attachable to his neck, and apply the rule to scenarios of death or ransom.

Core Idea
A slave's maintenance debt for his free wife attaches to his neck and he can be sold, like a trading slave's debt.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a specific question: When a slave marries a free woman with his master's permission, who is responsible for her maintenance? The Hanafi school rules that the maintenance becomes a debt on the slave, enforceable by selling him. The proof is a clear qiyas (analogy) to the trading slave's debt. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the analogy, and the consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
State the ruling: the free wife's maintenance is a debt (dayn) upon the slave. Note the condition: the marriage must be with the master's permission. Without permission, the ruling differs (though not covered here).
The text explicitly says 'with the master's permission' (باذن المولى).
2
Understand the legal nature: maintenance as debt
Maintenance is not a direct obligation on the slave's person in the same way as a free husband's. Rather, it becomes a debt that attaches to his 'neck' (raqabah), meaning his person becomes a security for the debt.
The term 'dayn' implies a financial liability that can be enforced by selling the slave.
3
Trace the qiyas proof
The text compares to a trading slave (عبد تاجر): just as a master's permission to trade makes the slave's trade debts attach to his neck, the master's permission to marry makes the marriage maintenance debt attach to the slave's neck.
The illa (effective cause) is the master's permission leading to a debt with a known cause.
4
Note the master's option and the fall of debt upon death
The master may ransom (يفتدي) the slave by paying the maintenance amount to avoid sale. If the slave dies or is killed, the maintenance debt falls completely because it is a grant (صلة) that only subsists during life.
The text says 'if the slave dies, it falls off; likewise if killed, in the correct view.'

ترجمہ اور اگر غلام نے کسی آزاد عورت سے نکاح کیا تو اس کا نفقہ غلام پر قرض ہو گا کہ وہ نفقہ میں فروخت کیا جائے گا۔ اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ غلام نے مولی کی اجازت سے نکاح کیا۔ اس لئے کہ نفقہ ایک قرضہ ہے جو غلام کے ذمہ واجب ہوا ۔ کیونکہ اس کے (واجب ہونے کا سبب پایا گیا۔ اور قرضہ کا واجب ہونا مولی کے حق میں بھی ظاہر ہوگا۔ پس ( یہ قرضہ ) غلام کی گردن کے ساتھ متعلق ہوگا۔ جیسے تاجر غلام کی گردن سے تجارت کا قرضہ متعلق ہوتا ہے۔ اور مولیٰ کو یہ اختیار ہے کہ وہ ( غلام کا فدیہ دیدے۔ کیونکہ عورت کا حق صرف نفقہ ہیں ہے ۔ نہ کہ غلام کی گردن ہیں ۔ اور اگر وہ غلام مر گیا تو نفقہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر قتل کیا گیا تو بھی صحیح قول پر ( ساقط ہو جائے گا) کیونکہ نفقہ تو زندگی کا عطیہ تھا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر غلام نے اپنے مولی کی اجازت سے کسی آزاد عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کیا ، تو اس عورت کا نفقہ غلام پر قرضہ ہو گا اور یہ غلام اپنی بیوی کے نفقہ میں فروخت کر دیا جائے گا۔

باب النفقة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفقہ ایک قرض ہے جو غلام کے ذمہ واجب ہوا۔ کیونکہ نفقہ واجب ہونے کا سبب یعنی عقد نکاح پایا گیا اور نفقہ واجب ہونا اس کے مولیٰ کے حق میں بھی ظاہر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مولی نے راضی ہو کر اجازت دی تھی۔ تو گویا مولی بھی وجوب نفقہ پر راضی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے یہ قرضہ غلام کی گردن کے ساتھ متعلق ہوگا ۔ جیسے تاجمد غلام جس کو اس کے مولی نے تجارت کی اجازت دی ۔ بچہ اس نے ادھار معالمانہ گئی کے اپنی گردن پر قبضہ کر لیا۔ تو یہ نام قرضہ میں فروخت کیا جائے گا۔ لیکن مولی کو یہ اختیارات کہ وہ اس کا فدیہ دیدے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کا حق نفقہ میں ہے نہ کہ نام کی گردن میں پس جب عمل نے عورت کا نفقہ ادا کردیا تو اس کے بعد نفقہ میں عورت کا حق باقی نہیں رہا۔ اس محبت ندیدینے کے بعد عورت کے تختہ میں فارم فر وخت نہیں یا سجات

And if a slave marries a free woman, her maintenance is a debt upon him, for which he is sold. The meaning is: when he marries with the master’s permission, because it is a debt that became obligatory in his liability due to the presence of its cause, and its obligation has become apparent with respect to the master, so it attaches to his slave as a debt of trade attaches to a trading slave. The master may ransom him because her right is in maintenance, not in the slave himself. If the slave dies, the maintenance falls off; likewise if he is killed, in the correct view, because it is a grant. [Urdu translation: ...Then explanation: if the slave with his master’s permission marries a free woman, her maintenance becomes a debt on the slave, and this slave will be sold for his wife’s maintenance. The proof: maintenance is a debt that became obligatory on the slave due to the marriage contract, and its obligation is also apparent regarding the master because he consented; thus the debt attaches to the slave’s neck like a trading slave. The master may ransom the slave. The wife’s right is only in maintenance, not in the slave’s physical being. When the slave dies, maintenance is waived; likewise if he is killed, in the correct view, because it is a grant of life.]
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling (hukm) regarding the maintenance of a free woman married to a slave, with proof. The ruling: if a slave marries a free woman with his master’s permission, her maintenance becomes a debt (dayn) on the slave, and he can be sold to pay it. The proof is based on qiyas: just as a trading slave’s debt attaches to his neck because his master allowed trade, similarly the maintenance debt attaches to the slave’s neck because the master allowed marriage. The master has the option to ransom the slave (fidyah) to prevent sale. If the slave dies or is killed, the maintenance is waived because it is a grant (silah) that only applies during life. The passage follows the author’s order: first the Arabic ruling, then Urdu translation, then explanation, then additional application to mukatib and umm walad mentioned later (though OCR garbled). The authority weight is from the zahir al-riwayah as indicated by the matn style.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): A financial obligation owed by the slave, enforceable upon his person (neck) but not upon his physical being if he dies.
رقبة (raqabah): The slave's person or 'neck' as a legal entity that can be sold to satisfy debts.
فدية (fidyah): Ransom paid by the master to redeem the slave from being sold for the wife's maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the slave's maintenance obligation if he dies?
A) It continues against his estate.
B) It must be paid by the master.
C) It is completely waived.
D) It becomes a debt on his heirs.

Key Takeaway
The slave's maintenance for a free wife is a debt on his person, enforceable by sale, analogous to a trading slave's debt, and falls off at his death.

Maintenance for Slave Wife: Condition of Tabwiya
Ruling on maintenance for slave wife due to tabwiya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a husband's maintenance to his slave wife and identify the ruling when the master interferes with her service.

Core Idea
Maintenance for a slave wife is wajib only upon the master's tabwiya — compensation for exclusive confinement.

In Hanafi fiqh, a free man's marriage to a slave woman does not automatically obligate him to provide maintenance. The key is whether the master provides a separate home (tabwiya), enabling exclusive confinement (ihtibas) for the husband. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the conditions and consequences, grounding the ruling in the legal cause of ihtibas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? A free man marrying a slave woman owned by another. Determine the ruling on maintenance: it is wajib only when the master provides a separate dwelling (tabwiya).
The ruling is conditional, not absolute.
2
Understand the cause ('illa): ihtibas
Why is maintenance wajib? Because tabwiya leads to exclusive confinement (ihtibas) of the wife for the husband. Maintenance is compensation for her availability. Without ihtibas, no compensation is due.
This is a teleological reasoning (ta'lil).
3
Examine the effect of master's actions after tabwiya
If the master employs the slave woman after providing a separate home, ihtibas is lost and maintenance ceases. However, voluntary service by the slave without the master's command does not break ihtibas.
The master's explicit recall is required.
4
Apply the ruling to similar categories
The same ruling applies to mudabbara (deferred manumission) and umm walad (mother of master's child). All slave women are treated equally regarding maintenance in marriage.
Consistency across slave categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوج الحرامة فبواها مولا هامعه منزلا فعليه النفقة لانه تحقق الاحتباس و ان لم يُبوء ها فلانفقة لها لعدم الاحتباس والتبوية ان يخلى بينها وبينه في منزله ولا يستخدمها ولو استخدمها بعد التبوية سقطت النفقة لانه فات الاحتباس و التبوية غير لازمة على ما مر فى النكاح ولو خدمته الجارية أحيانا من غيران يستخدمها لا يسقط النفقة لانه لم يستخدمها ليكون استردادا والمديرة وام الولد في هذا كالامة

ترجمہ اور اگر آزاد مرد نے ( کسی شخص کی ) باندی سے نکات گیا اور مولی نے اپنی باندی کو اس کے ساتھ رات کو الگ رہنے دیا تو اس پر نفقہ واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ احتباس پایا گیا اور اگر رات میں الگ نہیں بسایا تو باندی کے واسطے نفقہ نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ احتباس نہیں ہے اور رات کو الگ بہانے سے مراد یہ ہے کہ ) مولی باندی کو شوہر کے ساتھ ان کے گھر میں تنہا چھوڑ دے اور باندی سے اپنی خدمت نہ لے اور اور موالی نے بہانے کے بعد باندی کو اپنی خدمت میں لے لیا تو نفقہ ساتھ ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ احتباس فوت ہو گیا اور بسانا ( مولی پر لازم نہیں ہے جیسا کہ کتاب النکاح میں گذرا اور اگر باندی نے خود بھی بھی مول کی خدمت کی۔ بغیر اسکے کہ ولی اس سے خدمت لے تو نفقہ سا تو نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ مولی نے اس کو واپس لینے کے طور پر خدمت نہیں کی اور مد برو با ندی او رام والد اس حکم میں باندی کے مانند ہے۔
And if a free man marries a slave woman, and her master gives her a separate dwelling with him (tabwiya), then maintenance is obligatory upon him because confinement (ihtibas) is realized. But if he does not give her a separate dwelling, then there is no maintenance for her due to lack of confinement. Tabwiya means that the master leaves her alone with him in his house and does not employ her. If, after tabwiya, the master employs her, maintenance falls off because confinement is lost. Tabwiya is not obligatory upon the master, as has passed in the Book of Marriage. If the slave woman sometimes serves the master without him employing her, maintenance does not fall off because he did not employ her in a manner that constitutes taking her back. The mudabbara and umm walad are like the slave woman in this ruling.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling: when a free man marries a slave woman, the husband is liable for her maintenance only if the master provides a separate home (tabwiya) for the couple, thereby enabling exclusive confinement (ihtibas) for the husband. If no separate dwelling is provided, no maintenance is due. The master's act of taking the slave woman back for service after having provided a separate dwelling cancels maintenance. However, if the slave woman serves voluntarily without the master's command, maintenance continues. The ruling is based on the cause ('illa) of confinement: maintenance is compensation for the wife's availability, which is only possible if she is exclusively with the husband. The same applies to mudabbara (one whose freedom is deferred) and umm walad (a slave who bears the master's child). The authority weight is from the zahir al-riwayah as part of the standard text.

Key Terms
تبویہ (tabwiya): The master providing a separate home for the slave wife and her husband, not employing her.
احتباس (ihtibas): Confinement of the wife for the husband: her being available exclusively for him, which is the basis for receiving maintenance.
مدبرة (mudabbara): A slave woman whose manumission is deferred upon the master's death.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears her master's child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a free man marries a slave woman, when does the husband's maintenance obligation arise?
A) Immediately upon marriage
B) Only if the master provides a separate home for the couple
C) Only if the wife requests it
D) Never, because the master is responsible

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a free husband's maintenance to his slave wife is conditional on the master's provision of a separate home (tabwiya), because maintenance compensates exclusive confinement.

Nafaqah of a Slave-Girl Married to a Free Man
Ruling on nafaqah conditional upon ihtibas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for a free husband's nafaqah obligation when married to a slave-girl, and apply the rule to scenarios involving tabwiyah and ihtibas.

Core Idea
Nafaqah for a slave-girl wife is compensation for ihtibas, not merely the marriage contract.

In this passage, al-Hidayah clarifies a nuanced ruling: when a free man marries a slave-girl, his obligation to provide maintenance is not automatic. It hinges on the master's 'tabwiyah' (providing separate lodging) and refraining from using her for service. This lesson unpacks the concept of ihtibas as the trigger for nafaqah, and how subsequent actions affect the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the hukm level for nafaqah when tabwiyah is provided? It is wajib (obligatory) on the husband because ihtibas is realized.
Nafaqah is compensation for the wife's availability.
2
Understand the condition: tabwiyah
Tabwiyah means the master provides a separate dwelling for the couple and does not employ the slave-girl for service. Note that tabwiyah is not obligatory on the master.
This distinguishes the slave-girl's situation from a free wife's automatic nafaqah.
3
Trace the consequence of absence or loss of ihtibas
If no tabwiyah, no nafaqah. If after tabwiyah the master employs her, ihtibas is lost and nafaqah falls.
The key is the master's active retrieval of service.
4
Distinguish voluntary service
If the slave-girl serves the master voluntarily without his demand, ihtibas remains and nafaqah continues.
The determining factor is the master's intention: taking service as a retrieval ('istirdad').
5
Extend the ruling to mudabbara and umm walad
The same conditions apply to a mudabbara (slave promised freedom on master's death) and umm walad (slave who bore her master's child).
Their special status does not change the nafaqah rule.

And if a free man marries a slave-girl and her master provides her with a dwelling with him, then the maintenance is obligatory upon him because ihtibas (seclusion) is realized. And if he does not provide a dwelling, then no maintenance for her because ihtibas is absent. And tabwiyah means that he leaves between her and him in his house and does not employ her. And if he employs her after tabwiyah, the maintenance falls because ihtibas is lost. And tabwiyah is not obligatory upon the master as passed in the chapter on marriage. And if the slave-girl serves him occasionally without him employing her, the maintenance does not fall because he did not employ her as a retrieval. And the mudabbara and umm walad are like the slave-girl in this.
Translation: And if a free man marries a slave-girl of someone, and the master lets his slave-girl spend the night separately with him, then maintenance is obligatory on him because ihtibas is found. And if he does not give separate lodging at night, then no maintenance for the slave-girl because ihtibas does not exist. And 'giving separate lodging at night' means that the master leaves the slave-girl alone with the husband in their house and does not take service from her. And if the master after providing lodging takes her into his service, then maintenance falls because ihtibas is lost. And providing lodging is not obligatory on the master, as passed in the Book of Nikah. And if the slave-girl herself sometimes serves the master without him asking for service, then maintenance does not fall because the master did not take service as a retrieval. And mudabbara and umm walad are like the slave-girl in this ruling.
Explanation: Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume three. The issue is that if a free man marries a slave-girl of someone, and the master lets this slave-girl spend the night separately with her husband, then maintenance is obligatory on the husband because ihtibas from the slave-girl's side is found, and maintenance is the reward for ihtibas. And if the master does not give separate lodging, then maintenance is not obligatory on the husband because ihtibas is not found. And tabwiyah, i.e., giving separate lodging at night and providing accommodation, means that the master lets this slave-girl live in the husband's house and does not take service from her. And if the master first gave lodging and then took her into his service, then maintenance falls because ihtibas which causes maintenance is lost. Therefore, maintenance is not obligatory on the husband. And providing lodging and accommodation is not obligatory on the master, as passed in the chapter on marriage of slaves. And if the slave-girl herself sometimes serves the master without the master asking for service, then in that case maintenance does not fall because the master did not take service as a retrieval. And mudabbara and umm walad are like the slave-girl in this ruling, i.e., just as before providing lodging, there is no maintenance for the slave-girl, similarly for mudabbara and umm walad, there is no maintenance before providing lodging.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling statement from al-Hidayah regarding the maintenance (nafaqah) of a slave-girl who is married to a free man. The key condition is ihtibas, meaning the master allows the couple conjugal seclusion by providing a separate dwelling and not using the slave-girl for service. The author explains that nafaqah is a compensation for ihtibas. If the master does not provide such seclusion (tabwiyah), no maintenance is due. If after providing seclusion the master reclaims her for service, maintenance falls. However, if the slave-girl voluntarily serves without the master demanding it, maintenance remains. The same rule applies to mudabbara (a slave promised freedom upon master's death) and umm walad (a slave who bore her master's child). The master is not obligated to provide this seclusion, as earlier stated in the chapter on marriage of slaves.

Key Terms
احتباس (iḥtibās): Conjugal seclusion; the master's allowing the slave-girl to live with her husband without demanding service.
تبویہ (tabwiyah): Providing a separate dwelling; the master's act of lodging the slave-girl with her husband.
مدبرہ (mudabbara): A slave-girl who has been promised freedom upon her master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Nafaqah for a slave-girl wife in Hanafi fiqh is contingent upon the master providing ihtibas — conjugal seclusion without service — and is lost if the master reclaims her for work.

Wife's Right to Separate Housing
Ruling on husband's obligation to provide separate dwelling for wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the wife's right to separate housing, identify the Quranic proof, and explain the condition of waiver.

Core Idea
Housing is wajib maintenance for the wife, separate from in-laws, unless she consents otherwise.

In this lesson, we examine the husband's obligation to provide his wife with a private dwelling free of his relatives. The Hanafi school derives this from the Quranic command of maintenance, treating housing as an essential part of kifayah. You will learn the proof, the reasoning, and the wife's option to waive this right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What does the text obligate upon the husband? State the ruling: he must provide a separate house for his wife.
2
Locate the condition
The obligation has an exception: if the wife chooses to live with the husband's family, her consent overrides the default requirement.
This shows the wife's right is hers to exercise or waive.
3
Trace the proof
The text cites Quran 65:6 (with Ibn Mas'ud's reading) where Allah commands lodging and spending. The Hanafi school takes the imperative 'lodging' as proof of obligation.
The coupling of lodging with nafaqah in the verse reinforces its wajib status.
4
Understand the rationale
Why must the house be separate? The harm principle: sharing with in-laws compromises her security, property, and marital intimacy.
This harm-based reasoning is typical in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note the epistemological weight
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and considered the mufta bihi position. There is no intra-Hanafi dispute mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وعلى الزوج ان يسكنها فى دار مفردة ليس فيها احد من اهله الا ان تختار ذالك لان السكنى من كفايتها فيجب لها كالنفقة وقد وجبه الله تعالى مقرونا بالنفقة واذا وجب حقالها ليس له ان يشرك غيرها فيه لانها تتضرربه فانها لاتامن على متاعها ويمنعها عن المعاشرة مع زوجها ومن الاستمتاع الا ان تختار لانها رضيت بانتقاص حقها
ترجمہ اور شوہر پر واجب ہے کہ عورت کو علیحدہ گھر میں جس میں شوہر کے اہل میں سے کوئی نہ ہو بسادے ۔ مگر یہ کہ عورت خود اس کو پسند کرے۔ کیونکہ عورت کی کفایات میں سے سکونت بھی ہے۔ تو نفقہ کی طرح وہ بھی عورت کے لئے واجب ہوگا اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے نفقہ کے ساتھ ملا کر اس کو بھی واجب کیا ہے اور جب ( سکونت ) عورت کے واسطے حق واجب ہے تو مرد کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس کے حق میں غیر کو شریک کرے۔ کیونکہ عورت کو اس سے ضرر ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ اس اپنے اسباب سے بے خوف نہ ہوگی اور اشتراک اس کو اپنے شوہر کے ساتھ ہل مل کر رہنے سے روکے گا اور جماع اور اس کے متعلقات سے ( روک ) ہوگی مگر یہ کہ عورت ہی اختیار کرے کیونکہ وہ اپنے حق کی کمی پر راضی ہوگی۔
تشریح بیوی کے نفقہ کو بیان کرنے کے بعد اب سکنی کے احکام بیان فرمائیں گے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ شوہر پر واجب ہے کہ وہ اپنی بیوی کو علیحدہ مکان میں آباد کرے جس میں شوہر کے گھر والوں میں سے کوئی نہ رہتا ہو۔ ہاں اگر عورت ہی شوہر کے گھر والوں کے ساتھ رہنا پسند کرے تو اس کو اختیار ہے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کی ضروریات میں سے سکونت بھی ہے۔ لہذا نفقہ کی طرح وہ بھی شوہر پر واجب ہے اور ابن مسعود کی قرات میں ہے۔ اسكنوهن من حيث سكنتم وانفقوا عليهن من وجدكم یعنی تم ان عورتوں کو اپنی وسعت کے موافق رہنے کا مکان دو جہاں تم رہتے ہو اور ان کو نفقہ دو (۲) ۔ اس آیت میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے نفقہ کے ساتھ ملا کر سکنی کو بھی واجب کیا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ
Section: And upon the husband is to provide her accommodation in a separate house in which none of his family reside, unless she chooses that. Because accommodation is part of her maintenance (kifayah), so it is obligatory for her like nafaqah. And Allah the Exalted has made it obligatory coupled with nafaqah. And when her right becomes obligatory, it is not for him to share others with her in it because she is harmed by it. For she is not secure over her belongings, and it prevents her from socializing with her husband and from intimacy. Unless she chooses, because she has agreed to the diminution of her right.
Translation: And it is obligatory upon the husband to provide the wife in a separate house in which none of his family reside, unless the wife herself prefers that. Because accommodation is among her maintenance (kifayah). So like nafaqah, that too is obligatory for her. And Allah the Exalted has made it obligatory coupled with nafaqah. And when accommodation is a right obligatory for the wife, it is not permissible for the husband to share others with her in that right because she suffers harm from it. For she will not be secure over her possessions, and sharing will prevent her from freely associating with her husband and from intercourse and its related matters. Unless the wife herself chooses, because she has agreed to the deficiency of her right.
Explanation: After explaining the wife's nafaqah, now the rulings on suknah (housing) are given. Thus he said: It is obligatory upon the husband that he settle his wife in a separate house in which none of his family reside. Yes, if the wife herself prefers to live with the husband's family, then she has the choice.
The proof is that accommodation is among the wife's necessities. Therefore, like nafaqah, it is obligatory upon the husband. And in the recitation of Ibn Mas'ud [the verse] is: "Lodge them where you lodge, and spend on them from your wealth" (Quran 65:6). In this verse, Allah the Exalted has made accommodation obligatory coupled with nafaqah. Thus it is established that
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) from the Quran regarding the wife's right to separate housing (suknah). The author states that the husband must provide his wife a private dwelling free from his relatives, unless the wife consents to live with them. The reasoning is that housing is part of the wife's kifayah (maintenance), similar to food and clothing. The proof is the Quranic verse (65:6) where Allah commands lodging and spending. The commentary notes that the reading of Ibn Mas'ud clarifies the obligation. The prohibition of sharing the house with others is to protect the wife's privacy, security, and marital intimacy. She may waive this right by choice. The Hanafi position is that separate housing is a wajib right unless waived.

Key Terms
سکنی (suknā): The wife's right to separate housing provided by the husband.
کفایت (kifāyah): Maintenance covering food, clothing, and housing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is providing a separate house for the wife obligatory on the husband?
A) Because the wife's family demands it.
B) Because housing is part of kifayah, just like nafaqah, as indicated in the Quran.
C) Because the marriage contract specifies it.
D) Because the husband has the means.

Key Takeaway
The husband must provide separate housing for his wife as wajib, proven by Quran 65:6, and the wife may waive this right by choice.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Judge's Authority to Order Maintenance from Absent Husband's Property
Ruling with proof on judge's authority and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a judge can order maintenance from an absent husband's property and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on selling the property.

Core Idea
A judge can only give maintenance from an absent husband's property if it matches the type; selling is prohibited.

When a husband is absent and his wife needs maintenance, the judge has authority to order payment from his property. However, this authority is not absolute. The Hanafi school imposes a critical condition: the property must match the type of maintenance the wife is entitled to. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this rule and the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions on whether the judge can sell the absent's property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the judge permitted to do? The judge can order maintenance for the wife and children from the absent husband's property, but only if the property is of the same type as the maintenance entitlement (e.g., money, grain, clothing).
2
Understand the condition: matching type
The judge cannot order maintenance from property that does not match the type (e.g., a house or slave) because that would require selling the property, which is not allowed for an absent person.
This condition applies by consensus among the Hanafis.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on selling
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that selling an absent person's property is never allowed, because even a present person cannot be forced to sell. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that if the judge knows the husband refused to pay, he could order a present person to sell, but for an absent, the refusal is unknown, so sale is also prohibited.
Both sides agree that sale is ultimately not permitted, but the reasoning differs.
4
Evaluate the proof (dalil)
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas: since a present person cannot be forced to sell, an absent person (who is more vulnerable) also cannot. The Sahibayn base their view on the condition of known refusal, which is absent for an absent person.
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: absolute prohibition of sale.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the wife's maintenance type is cash and the husband left only a house, the judge cannot order maintenance from that house. The wife must wait or seek other means.
This highlights the importance of property type in enforcement.

جواب یہ ہے کہ غائب کے حق میں قاضی اسی چیز کا حکم دے سکتا ہے۔ جو اس کے حق میں مفید اور کار آمد ہو اور جس میں غائب پر نظر و شفقت نہ ہو اس کے بارے میں قاضی حکم دینے کا مجاز نہیں ہوگا۔ پس بیوی بچوں کیلئے نفقہ کا حکم دینے میں مرد غائب پر نظر و شفقت ہے اسلئے کہ اس کی ملک باقی رہے گی اور قرضہ ادا کرنے میں اس کی ملک کو باقی رکھنا نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ ایک اجنبی کے کہنے سے اس کے خلاف حکم کرنا ہے پس اس فرق کی وجہ سے قاضی بیوی بچوں کے واسطے نفقہ کا حکم کرسکتا ہے۔ مگر قرضہ ادا کرنے کا حکم نہیں کر سکتا۔ واقرار صاحب الید سے بھی ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ جس شخص کے پاس غائب شخص کا مال ودیعت ہے اس کا اقرار صحیح نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ یہ اقرار علی الغائب ( غائب کے خلاف اقرار کرنا ) ہے۔ جواب قابیض یعنی جسکے پاس غائب کا مال ودیعت ہے اس کا اقرار اپنے حق میں مقبول ہے حضوصاً اس مقام پر۔ کیونکہ اگر وہ زوجیت یا ودیعت میں سے کسی امر کا انکار کرتا تو اس پر عورت کے گواہ قبول نہ ہوتے۔ کیونکہ عورت کا بینہ اگر زوجیت اور نکاح ثابت کرنے کے لئے ہے تو اس لئے قبول نہیں ہوگا۔ کہ مودع ( ودیعت رکھنے والا ) نائب شخص پر نکاح ثابت کرنے میں مدعی علیہ نہیں ہوسکتا اور اگر عورت نے ودیعت پر بعینہ قائم کیا ہے تو اس لئے قبول نہیں ہوگا۔ کہ مرد غائب کے حقوق ثابت کرنے میں وہ مدعی نہیں ہو سکتی ہے ۔ بہر حال جب عورت کے گواہ قبول نہیں ہوئے تو مودع ( ودیعت رکھنے والے کا) اقرار ضرور قبول ہوگا۔ پس جب مودع کا اقرار خود اس کے حق میں ثابت ہو گیا تو غائب کے حق میں بھی متعدی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مودع نے جس چیز کا اقرار کیا ہے وہ اس مرد غائب کی ملک ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کہ ایک مرد نے رمضان کا چاند دیکھا تو پہلے اس کے حق میں رمضان ہونا ثابت ہوگا ۔ پھر اس کے علاوہ کی طرف متعدی ہوگا اور یہی حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ مال اس شخص کے پاس بطور مضاربت ہو۔ یعنی اگر قابض اس مال مضاربت کا اور زوجیت کا اقرار کرتا ہے یا قاضی کو ذاتی علم ہو تو قاضی اس مال مضاربت میں سے ان لوگوں کا نفقہ مقرر کر دے گا اور اسی طرح اگر اس شخص پر غائب آدمی کا قرضہ ہے، اور یہ اس قرضہ اور زوجیت کا اقرار کرے یا قاضی کو ذاتی علم ہو تو بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ یعنی قاضی اس مال میں سے ان لوگوں کا نفقہ مقرر دے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ سب تفصیل اس صورت میں ہے کہ یہ مال عورت کے حق کی جنس سے ہو۔ مثلا روپے ہوں یا اشرفیاں یا اناج یا عورت کے حق کی جنس کا لباس ہو ۔ یعنی جیسا کپڑا اس عورت کیلئے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اگر اسی جنس کا کپڑا حامد کے پاس ودیعت ہو، تو قاضی اس میں سے کپڑا دلوا دے گا اور اگر یہ مال عورت کے حق کی جنس کے خلاف ہو۔ مثلاً مکان غلام یا دیگر سامان ودیعت رکھ گیا ہو تو قاضی اس میں سے نفقہ مقررنہیں کرے گا۔ کیونکہ نفقہ دینے کے واسطے اس کے بیچنے کی ضرورت ہے اور غائب کا مال بالا تفاق نہیں بیچا جاتا ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ شخص موجود ہوتا اور حاضر ہوتا تو قاضی کو اس کا مال بیچے کا اختیار نہ ہوتا۔ کیونکہ قاضی کی بیع اسلئے درست ہوتی ہے کہ مالک کو بیع کرنے سے روک دیا گیا ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک آزاد عاقل بالغ کو بیچ کرنے سے روکنا باطل ہے۔ پس جب حاضر کا مال نہیں بیچا جا سکتا تو غائب کا بدرجہ اولیٰ نہیں بیچا جائے گا۔ اور رہا صاحبین کے نزدیک تو اس واسطے کہ قاضی اگر چہ حاضر پر اس کا مال فروخت کرنے کا حکم دے سکتا ہے اس وجہ سے کہ ادائے حق سے انکار کرنا قاضی کو معلوم ہو جاتا ہے اور ادائے حق سے انکار کرنا ہی قاضی کیلئے جواز بیع کی شرط ہے۔ لیکن غائب پر یہ حکم نہیں کرے گا کیونکہ غائب کا ادائے حق سے انکار کرنا قاضی کو معلوم نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ ادائے حق سے انکار کرنا ہی جواز بیع کی شرط ہے۔
Chapter of Maintenance. This is the answer: The judge can only give a ruling regarding an absent person that is beneficial and useful for him, and regarding that which does not show consideration and care for the absent, the judge is not authorized to give a ruling. So in ordering maintenance for the wife and children, there is consideration and care for the absent man because his ownership will remain, but in paying a debt his ownership will not remain. Rather, it is ruling against him at the behest of a stranger. Due to this difference, the judge can order maintenance for the wife and children, but cannot order payment of a debt. Also, this is an answer to a question regarding the confession of the possessor of the property. The question is: the confession of the person who has the absent person's property as a deposit should not be valid, because this is a confession against the absent. The answer: the confession of the receiver, i.e., the one who has the absent's property as a deposit, is acceptable in his own right, especially in this context. Because if he denied either the marriage or the deposit, then the woman's witnesses would not be accepted. If the woman's proof is to establish the marriage and nikah, then it will not be accepted because the depositor cannot be the defendant in proving the marriage against the absent person. And if the woman established the very deposit, it will not be accepted because she cannot be the plaintiff in proving the rights of the absent man. In any case, when the woman's witnesses are not accepted, then the confession of the depositor must be accepted. So when the depositor's confession is established in his own favor, it will also be transferred to the absent, because what the depositor confessed is the property of the absent man. This is like a man seeing the moon of Ramadan: first Ramadan is established in his favor, then it transfers to others. The same ruling applies when the property is with that person as mudaraba. That is, if the possessor confesses to this mudaraba property and the marriage, or the judge has personal knowledge, then the judge will fix their maintenance from this mudaraba property. Similarly, if that person owes a debt to the absent man, and he confesses to this debt and the marriage, or the judge has personal knowledge, then the same ruling applies. The author of Hidayah says that all this detail applies when this property is of the same type as the woman's entitlement. For example, rupees, gold coins, grain, or clothing of the type the woman is entitled to. That is, if the clothing that is obligatory for this woman is in Hamid's possession as a deposit, then the judge will have that clothing given. But if this property is opposite to the type of the woman's entitlement, e.g., a house, a slave, or other goods were deposited, then the judge will not fix maintenance from it, because giving maintenance requires selling it, and the property of an absent person is not sold by consensus. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that if that person were present, the judge would not have the authority to sell his property, because the judge's sale is valid only when the owner is prevented from selling, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa, preventing a free, sane, adult person from selling is invalid. So when the property of a present person cannot be sold, even more so the property of an absent person cannot be sold. As for the position of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is because the judge can order a present person to sell his property when the judge knows of his refusal to pay the right, and the refusal to pay the right is the condition for the permissibility of sale. But he will not order this against the absent, because the judge does not know whether the absent has refused to pay the right, while the refusal to pay is the condition.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the judge's authority to order maintenance from the property of an absent husband. The author explains that the judge can only issue rulings that benefit the absent person. Ordering maintenance for the wife and children is beneficial because the husband's property remains in his ownership (the maintenance is a debt against him), whereas paying a debt to a creditor would diminish his ownership without a direct benefit to him. Thus, the judge can order maintenance but not debt payment. The passage then addresses a related question: if a person holds the absent husband's property as a deposit (wadi'ah) and confesses that it belongs to the husband, is that confession valid? The answer is yes, because the depositary's confession is in his own favor (it protects him from liability), and the woman cannot prove her case otherwise. The confession then extends to the absent husband, similar to how a person's sighting of the moon establishes Ramadan for him and then for others. The same applies if the property is held as mudaraba or if the depositary owes a debt to the absent person. However, the judge can only order maintenance if the deposited property matches the type of maintenance the wife is entitled to (e.g., cash, grain, or clothing). If it is a different type (e.g., a house or slave), the judge cannot order maintenance because selling the property would be required, and selling an absent person's property is not permitted. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that even a present person's property cannot be sold by the judge without consent, so an absent's property also cannot be sold. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that a judge can order a present person to sell if he refuses to pay, but for an absent, the refusal is not known, so the judge cannot order the sale. This difference affects whether the judge can order maintenance from non-liquid assets.

Key Terms
غائب (gha'ib): A person who is absent from the jurisdiction and whose whereabouts are unknown to the judge.
ودیعت (wadi'ah): A deposit; property left with someone for safekeeping without compensation.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance; the financial support a husband must provide to his wife and children, including food, clothing, and shelter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why can't the judge sell the absent husband's property?
A) Because the judge does not know if the husband has refused to pay maintenance.
B) Because a free, sane adult cannot be forced to sell his property, whether present or absent.
C) Because the wife must first prove the marriage in court.
D) Because the property is not in the judge's possession.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a judge can order maintenance from an absent husband's property only if the property matches the type of maintenance; selling the property is not allowed.

Nikah — Marriage

Taking a Guarantor and the Distinction Between Maintenance and Inheritance
Ruling with proof on maintenance procedure and distinction with inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires a guarantor from the wife in maintenance cases but not in inheritance, and apply the distinction to determine when a guarantor is needed.

Core Idea
A guarantor protects the absent husband's property when the wife may not be entitled; no guarantor is needed when the beneficiary is unknown.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the procedure when a wife seeks maintenance from an absent husband: the judge takes an oath and a guarantor from her. It also distinguishes this from inheritance cases, where no guarantor is taken because the potential absent heir is unknown. Understanding this distinction reveals the Hanafi school's careful balance between protecting the rights of both the wife and the husband.

Guided Path
1
State the procedure for maintenance from an absent husband
Identify the ruling: the judge takes a guarantor (kafil) from the wife and administers an oath that she has not received maintenance. Understand the purpose: to protect the absent husband's property in case the wife was not actually entitled.
The oath is taken first, then the guarantor.
2
Identify the proof for taking a guarantor
The text gives a rational proof: it is possible that the wife already received maintenance before the husband's absence, or that he divorced her and her 'iddah has expired. Because of this possibility, the judge takes a guarantor to safeguard the husband's interest.
This is a precautionary measure based on potential harm.
3
Contrast with inheritance cases
Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes this from inheritance: when heirs present witnesses and no other heir is known, the judge distributes inheritance without taking a guarantor from the heirs. Why? Because the potential absent heir is unknown, so a guarantor would have no identifiable beneficiary.
In inheritance, the guarantor would be for an unknown person, which is pointless.
4
Identify the basis of the distinction
The key difference is that in maintenance, the beneficiary (the husband) is known ('ilm), so a guarantor can be taken for his benefit. In inheritance, the beneficiary of the guarantee (any unknown heir) is unknown, so taking a guarantor is not applicable.
This is a clear rational distinction (ta'lil).
5
Recognise the limitation on who receives maintenance
The judge only orders maintenance from the absent's property for specific relatives: parents, wife, and minor children. Their maintenance is obligatory before the judge's order. For other relatives, maintenance becomes obligatory only by the judge's order, but judgment against an absent is not valid.
This further shows the Hanafi caution in dealing with absent persons' property.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم

باب النسبية
قاضی عورت سے کفیل لے لے
قال وياخذ منها كفيلا نظر اللغائب لانهار بما استوفت النفقة او طلقها الزوج وانقضت عدتها فرق بين هذا و بين الميراث اذا قسم بين ورثة حضور بالبيئة و لم يقولوا لا نعلم له وارثا اخر حيث لا يؤخذ منهم الكفيل عنه ابي حنيفة لان هناك المكفول له مجهول وههنا معلوم و هو الزوج و يحلفها بالله ما اعطاها النفقة نظر للغائب ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور قاضی اس عورت سے کفیل لے لے گا۔ تا کہ مرد غائب کی نگہداشت رہے۔ کیونکہ وہ سکتا ہے کہ اس عورت نے (اپنا) نفقہ پیشگی وصول کر لیا ہو یا شوہر اس کو طلاق دے چکا اور عدت گذر چکی ہو۔ ( امام ابوحنیفہ نے ) اس کے درمیان اور میراث کے درمیان فرق کیا ہے۔ جبکہ میراث تقسیم کی گئی موجود ورثہ کے درمیان (جن کا ثبوت ) گواہوں کے ذریعہ سے ہوا اور انہوں نے یہ نہیں کہا ہم ان کے سوا دوسرا وارث نہیں جانتے ہیں ۔ تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ان سے کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ وہاں ممکفول لۂ مجہول ہے اور یہاں معلوم اور وہ شوہر ہے اور قاضی اس عورت کو قسم دے گا کہ خدا کی قسم اس کو شوہر نے نفقہ نہیں دیا تا کہ مرد غائب کی نگہداشت رہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قاضی اس عورت سے کفیل لے لے گا یعنی ایک شخص ذمہ دار ہو کہ اگر یہ عورت نفقہ کی مستحق نہ ہو گی تو غائب کا مال واپس ملے گا تا کہ مرد غائب کی نگہداشت رہے۔ امام سرخسی نے کہا کہ عورت سے کفیل لینا بہتر ہے اور اگر نہیں لیا تو بھی جائز ہے اور صدر الشہید نے کہا کہ غائب شوہر کی رعایت کے پیش نظر کفیل لینا درست ہے۔ لیکن قاضی اولاً اس عورت سے اس بات پر قسم لے کہ اسکے شوہر نے اس کو نفقہ نہیں دیا ہے۔ کیونکہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ شوہر نے سفر میں جانے سے پہلے اس عورت کو نفقہ دے دیا ہو اور یہ عورت قاضی پر معاملہ کو مشتبہ کر کے دوبارہ نفقہ لے لے ۔ پس جب اس عورت نے قسم کھالی تو قاضی اس عورت کو نفقہ دے دے اور اس سے کفیل لے لے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ممکن ہے کہ عورت نے اس سے اپنا نفقہ پیشگی وصول کر لیا ہو یا شوہر اس کو طلاق دے چکا اور عدت گذر چکی ہو تو یہ عورت مستحق نفقہ نہ ہوگی ۔ اسلئے شوہر کی رعایت کے پیش نظر اس سے کفیل لیا جائے گا۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ نے نفقہ کی صورت میں کفیل لینے کا حکم دیا اور میراث کی صورت میں کفیل لینے کا حکم نہیں دیا۔ تو امام صاحب نے ان دونوں صورتوں میں فرق کیا۔ یعنی جبکہ ایک شخص مرا اور اس کے موجود ورثہ نے گواہ پیش کیئے۔ جنہوں نے گواہی دی کہ یہ لوگ اس کے وارث ہیں اور یہ نہیں کہا کہ ہم ان کے علاوہ دوسرا وارث نہیں جانتے ہیں۔ تو قاضی ان میں میراث تقسیم کر دے گا اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ان لوگوں سے کفیل نہیں لے گا۔ اسلئے کہ میراث کی صورت میں و شخص معلوم نہیں جس کیلئے کفیل لیا جائے گا اور نفقہ کی صورت میں مکفول یا معلوم ہے کہ وہ عورت کا شوہر ہے۔ قاضی غائب کا مال میں والدین، بیوی اور اولادصغار کے علاوہ کا نفقہ مقرر نہ کرے
قال ولا يقضى بنفقة في مال غائب الالهؤلاء ووجه الفرق هو ان نفقة هولاء واجبة قبل قضاء القاضي ولهذا كان لهم ان ياخذو اقبل القضاء فكان قضاء القاضى اعانة لهم اما غيرهم من المحارم فنفقتهم انما تجب بالقضاء لانه مجتهد فيه والقضاء على الغائب لايجوز ولولم يعلم القاضى بذالک ولم یكن مقرابه فاقامت البيئة على الزوجية اولم يخلف مالا فاقامت البيئة ليفرض القاضي نفقتها على الغائب
Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Bidaya Volume Five. Chapter of Maintenance. The judge takes a guarantor from the woman. He (al-Quduri) said: And he (the judge) will take a guarantor from her, out of consideration for the absent (husband), because she may have already received the maintenance, or the husband may have divorced her and her 'iddah has expired. He (Imam Abu Hanifa) distinguished between this and inheritance: when inheritance is divided among present heirs with evidence, and they did not say 'We know of no other heir,' then according to Abu Hanifa, a guarantor is not taken from them, because there the beneficiary is unknown, while here it is known, and it is the husband. And he (the judge) will administer an oath to her by Allah that the husband did not give her maintenance, out of consideration for the absent. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the judge will take a guarantor from the woman, so that the absent man's interest is protected, because she may have already received her maintenance in advance, or the husband may have divorced her and her 'iddah has expired. (Imam Abu Hanifa) distinguished between this and inheritance: when inheritance is divided among present heirs whose evidence (is accepted) through witnesses, and they did not say 'We do not know of any other heir besides them,' then according to Abu Hanifa, no guarantor is taken from them, because there the beneficiary is unknown, and here it is known, and it is the husband. And the judge will administer an oath to the woman: 'By Allah, the husband did not give me maintenance,' to protect the absent man. Explanation: The issue is that the judge will take a guarantor from the woman, i.e., a responsible person who will guarantee that if the woman is not entitled to maintenance, the absent's property will be returned, to protect the absent man. Imam Sarakhsi said that taking a guarantor from the woman is better, and if not taken, it is still permissible. Sadr al-Shahid said that taking a guarantor is correct for the consideration of the absent husband. But the judge first takes an oath from the woman that her husband did not give her maintenance, because it is possible that the husband gave her maintenance before traveling and she confuses the matter to get maintenance again. So when the woman takes the oath, the judge gives her maintenance and takes a guarantor from her. The proof is that it is possible that she already received her maintenance in advance, or the husband divorced her and her 'iddah expired, so she would not be entitled to maintenance. Therefore, for the husband's consideration, a guarantor is taken from her. Imam Abu Hanifa ordered taking a guarantor in the case of maintenance, but did not order taking a guarantor in the case of inheritance. So Imam Abu Hanifa distinguished between these two cases: When a man dies and his present heirs present witnesses who testify that these are his heirs and do not say 'We do not know of any other heir,' then the judge will distribute the inheritance among them, and according to Abu Hanifa, he will not take a guarantor from them, because in inheritance the person for whom the guarantor would be taken is unknown, while in maintenance, the one for whom the guarantor is taken is known, i.e., the husband. The judge does not order maintenance from the property of the absent except for these (i.e., parents, wife, and minor children). And the difference is that the maintenance of these is obligatory before the judge's order, so they could take it before the order; thus the judge's order is an assistance to them. As for other relatives, their maintenance is only obligatory by the judge's order because it is a matter of ijtihad, and judgment against an absent person is not permissible. Even if the judge does not know this and there is no confession, and the woman establishes evidence of marriage, or he has left no property, and she establishes evidence so that the judge may fix her maintenance from the absent's property.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the procedure when a wife seeks maintenance from an absent husband. The judge takes a guarantor (kafil) from the wife to protect the absent husband's rights, because it is possible she has already received maintenance or her 'iddah has expired. The judge also administers an oath to her that she has not received maintenance. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes this from inheritance cases: when heirs present witnesses and do not mention other possible heirs, the judge distributes the inheritance without taking a guarantor, because the beneficiary (the absent person who might have a claim) is unknown. In maintenance, the beneficiary is known (the husband). The passage also notes that the judge only orders maintenance from the absent's property for specific relatives: parents, wife, and minor children, because their maintenance is obligatory before the judge's order. For other relatives, maintenance becomes obligatory only by the judge's order, and since judgment against an absent is not permissible, the judge cannot order it. Imam Sarakhsi considers taking a guarantor recommended but not obligatory; Sadr al-Shahid deems it correct for the absent's protection.

Key Terms
کفیل (kafil): A guarantor; a person who guarantees that the property taken for maintenance will be returned if the wife was not entitled.
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The person in whose favor the guarantee is given; here, the absent husband.
قسم (qasam): An oath administered by the judge to the wife that she has not received maintenance from her husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa distinguish between taking a guarantor in maintenance cases and inheritance cases?
A) Because maintenance is a debt, while inheritance is not
B) Because the beneficiary of the guarantor is known in maintenance (the husband) but unknown in inheritance
C) Because inheritance involves multiple heirs
D) Because maintenance must be paid immediately

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school safeguards the absent husband's property through oath and guarantor, and limits maintenance to close relatives whose obligation is established before judicial intervention.

Hiring Wife to Breastfeed a Child from Another Woman
States ruling on hiring one's wife to breastfeed a child from another wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring one's wife or iddah woman to breastfeed a child from another woman and explain the rationale based on the absence of obligation.

Core Idea
A wife cannot be hired to breastfeed her own child, but she can be hired to breastfeed another woman's child because it is not wajib upon her.

In Hanafi fiqh, a wife is generally not obligated to breastfeed her own child unless the father cannot provide a wet nurse. However, when it comes to a child from another woman, there is no obligation at all. This opens the door for a valid ijarah (hiring) contract. In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from Al-Hidayah that confirms this permissibility and the simple logic behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on: hiring one's wife or iddah woman to breastfeed a child from another woman. The ruling is 'jā'iz' (permissible).
2
Distinguish the child's relation to the woman
The child is from another woman, not her own. This is the crucial factor. The passage contrasts this with the case where the child is her own, where hiring would not be permissible because she may already be obligated.
The obligation (wujub) of breastfeeding a stepchild or child from another wife is absent.
3
Apply the principle of obligation
The rationale given: 'it is not obligatory upon her.' Since the act is not wajib, she can enter into an ijarah contract and receive wages. If it were wajib, taking wages would be problematic.
The absence of obligation is the illah (ratio legis) for permissibility.
4
Conclude the permissibility
Thus, the ijarah is valid and permissible. The passage ends by stating that the proof is clear.
No further details are given; the ruling is straightforward based on the absence of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منکوحہ یا معتدہ کو بیٹے کے ارضاع کیلئے اجرت پر لیا جولٹڑ کا کسی اور عورت سے ہے لینا جائز ہے ولواستاجرها وهى منكوحة او معتدته لارضاع ابن له من غيرها جاز لانه غير مستحق عليها ترجمہ اور اگر اس نے اپنی منکوحہ یا معدہ کو اس واسطے اجرت پر لیا کہ جو اس کا بچہ دوسری بیوی سے ہے اس کو دودھ پلائے تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دودھ پلانا اس پر حق واجب نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ اور دلیل واضح ہے۔
And if he hires his wife or his iddah woman to breastfeed a son of his from another woman, it is permissible because it is not obligatory upon her. Translation: And if he hired his wife or iddah woman to breastfeed his child from another wife, it is permissible. Because this breastfeeding is not a right obligatory upon her. Explanation: The case and the proof are clear.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This short passage presents a subsidiary ruling: if a man hires his current wife or a woman in his iddah (from a previous marriage) to breastfeed a child that he has from another woman, it is permissible. The reason is that this particular child is not her own, and she has no legal obligation to breastfeed him. Therefore, the general prohibition against taking wages for breastfeeding one's own child does not apply here. The text simply states the ruling and its rationale without further elaboration, noting that the proof is clear.

Key Terms
منکوحہ (mankuha): A woman who is currently married to the man (his wife)
معتدہ (mu'taddah): A woman who is in her iddah (waiting period) after divorce or death of her husband, still legally connected to him.
ارضاع (irdā'): Breastfeeding; the act of nursing an infant.
اجرت (ujrah): Wage, fee, or compensation paid for a service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is it permissible for a man to hire his wife to breastfeed a child for wages?
A) When the child is her own biological child
B) When the child is from another woman
C) Never, because a wife cannot take wages from her husband
D) Only if the child is an orphan

Key Takeaway
A wife can be hired to breastfeed a child that is not her own because she has no legal obligation to do so, making the ijarah contract valid.

Maintenance of Ascendants: Parents and Grandparents
Ruling with proof on nafaqah for ascendants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on maintenance of needy parents and grandparents, explain the proofs from Quran and qiyas, and identify the exception for harbi parents.

Core Idea
Maintenance of needy parents is wajib even if they are non-Muslim, except if they are harbi.

In this lesson, we examine the obligation of nafaqah (maintenance) for ascendants. The source passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah establishes that a person must support his parents and grandparents if they are poor, regardless of religious difference. We will go through the textual proof (Quran) and analogical reasoning (qiyas) used by the Hanafi school, and note the important limitation for harbi parents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening of the passage: maintenance is wajib for parents and grandparents if they are poor, even if they differ in religion. Note the conditions: poverty, and not harbi (enemy combatant).
The condition of poverty is essential; a wealthy parent is not entitled to maintenance from the child.
2
Examine the primary proof for parents
The author cites the Quranic verse: 'And accompany them in this world with kindness' (Luqman 31:15). This verse was revealed about Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas's non-Muslim mother. The commentator argues that kindness includes material support; letting parents starve is not kindness.
The command is general, covering both Muslim and non-Muslim parents.
3
Understand the secondary proof from the hadith
The commentator also uses the hadith: 'The best of a man's wealth is from his earnings, and his child is from his earnings.' This implies the father can consume from the child's earnings, so maintenance is owed.
This hadith supports the obligation from a different angle.
4
Apply qiyas for grandparents
Grandparents are included by analogy because they are also ascendants and causes of the child's existence. The grandfather takes the father's place in his absence.
The illa is that they are from the fathers and mothers (lineage and cause of existence).
5
Recognize the exception for harbi parents
The verse 'Allah does not forbid you from those who do not fight you...' (Al-Mumtahanah 60:8-9) limits the obligation to non-combatant parents. Parents who are harbi (enemy combatants) are not entitled to maintenance.
This exception distinguishes the Hanafi position from Malik and Shafi'i, who do not make the harbi distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النفقة
آدمی پر اس کے ابوین اور اجداد اور جدات کا نفقہ لازم ہے اگر وہ فقراء ہوں
اگر چہ وہ دین میں مخالف ہوں
فصل وعلى الرجل ان ينفق على ابويه واجداده وجداته اذا كانوا فقراء وان خالفوه في دينه اما الابوان فلقوله تعالى وصاحبهما في الدينا معروفا نزلت الاية فى الابوين الكافرين وليس من المعروف ان يعيش في نعم الله تعالى ویترکهمايموتان جوعا واما الاجدادو الجدات فلانهم من الاباء والامهات ولهذا يقوم الجد مقام الاب عند عدمه ولانهم سيبو الاحيائه فاستوجبوا عليه الاحياء بمنزلة الابوين وشرط الفقر لانه لو كان ذا مال فایجاب نفقته في ماله اولى من ايجابها في مال غیره ولا يمنع ذالك باختلاف الدين لماتلونا
ترجمہ فصل ! آدمی پر واجب ہے کہ اپنے والدین اور اجداد اور جدات کو نفقہ دے جبکہ وہ محتاج ہوں۔ اگر چہ دین میں اسکے مخالف ہوں۔ بہر حال والدین ) کے نفقہ میں دلیل ) باری تعالیٰ کا قول و صاحبهما في الدنيا معروفا یعنی دنیا میں والدین کے ساتھ اعتدال کے طور پر رہا کر ۔ یہ آیت کا فروالدین کے حق میں نازل ہوئی اور معروف ( اعتدال کا رہنا ) یہ نہیں ہے کہ خود نعمت الہی میں عیش کرے اور والدین کو چھوڑ دے کہ بھوکے مرجائیں اور اجداد و جدات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ بھی باپوں اور ماؤں میں سے ہیں اور اسی وجہ سے باپ کی عدم موجودگی میں دارا باپ کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے اور اسلئے کہ وہ بھی آدمی کے زندہ ہونے کا سبب ہیں۔ تو وہ اس آدمی پر اپنی زندگی کا استحقاق رکھتے ہیں۔ جیسے والدین میں ہے اور محتاجی کی شرط اسلئے لگائی کہ اگر باپ مالدار ہو تو اس کا نفقہ اپنے مال میں واجب ہونا اولیٰ ہے بہ نسبت مال غیر کے اور اختلاف دین نفقہ واجب ہونے سے مانع نہیں ہوتا۔ اس آیت کی وجہ سے جو ہم تلاوت کر چکے۔
تشریح اولاد کے نفقہ سے فراغت کے بعد اس فصل میں والدین، دادا، دادی اور خادم کو نفقہ بیان کریں گے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ انسان پر واجب ہے کہ وہ اپنے ماں باپ، دادا دادی کو نفقہ دے، بشرطیکہ وہ محتاج ہوں اگر چہ دین میں اسکے مخالف ہوں ۔ پس والدین کے نفقہ میں دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول وان جاهداک علی ان لا تشرک بی ما لیس لک به علم فلا تطعهما و صاحبهما في الدنيا معرفا واتبع سبیل من اناب الی ہے۔ یعنی اگر وہ دونوں تجھ پر اس بات کا زور ڈالیں کہ میرے ساتھ ایسی چیز کو ٹھہرائے جس کی تیرے پاس کوئی دلیل نہ ہو تو ان کا کہنا نہ مانا اور دنیا میں انکے ساتھ خوبی سے بسر کرنا اور اسی کی راہ پر چلنا جو میری طرف رجوع ہو ۔ (سورہ لقمان ) یہ آیت سعد بن ابی وقاص کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے۔ یہ خود مسلمان ہو گئے تھے اور ان کی والدہ جمیلہ نامی کافرہ تھیں اور اس نے سعد کے اسلام لانے کی وجہ سے کھانا پینا بھی چھوڑ دیا تھا تو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت میں حاضر ہوئے تو یہ آیت نازل ہوئی۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ دین کے معاملہ میں ان کی اطاعت مت کرو۔ البتہ دنیا میں انکے ساتھ معروف طریقہ پر رہو اور معروف طریقہ سے رہنا یہ نہیں ہے کہ خود تو اللہ کی نعمتوں میں عیش کرے اور والدین کو چھوڑ دے کہ وہ بھو کے مرجائیں۔ اس آیت سے واضح ہوا کہ ماں باپ اگر محتاج ہوں تو بیٹے پر ان کا نفقہ واجب ہے اگر چہ دین میں دونوں کا اختلاف
ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔
اور شمس الائمہ سری نے شرح کافی میں باری تعالیٰ کے قول ولا تقل لهما اف سے استدلال کیا ہے۔ بایں طور کہ اس آیت میں
والدین کو اف کہنے یعنی ایذاء پہنچانے سے منع کیا گیا ہے اور ضرورت کے وقت ان کو نفقہ نہ دینے میں زیادہ اذیت اور تکلیف ہے۔ اسلئے آدمی پر اپنے ماں باپ کو نفقہ دینا واجب ہوگا اور چونکہ آیت مطلق ہے اسلئے یہ حکم عام ہو گا۔ خواہ والدین مسلمان ہوں یا کافر ہوں۔ نیز حضور اقدس صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ان اطيب مال الرجل من كسبه و أن ولده من كسبه فكلوا من كسب اولادکم یعنی آدمی کا بہترین کھانا اس کی کمائی سے ہے اور اس کا بچہ بھی اس کی کمائی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے تم اپنی اولاد کی کمائی سے کھاؤ۔ اس حدیث سے بھی ثابت ہوا کہ باپ کا نفقہ اس کی اولاد کی کمائی میں واجب ہے۔
