ظاهروا على اخراجكم ان تولوهم و من يتولهم فاولئك هم الظالمون - (پ ۲۸، ع ) یعنی اللہ تم کو ان لوگوں کے ساتھ احسان اور انصاف کا برتاؤ کرنے سے منع نہیں کرتا جو تم سے دین کے بارے میں نہیں لڑے اور تم کو تمہارے گھروں سے نہیں نکالا۔ اللہ تعالیٰ انصاف کا برتاؤ کرنے والوں سے محبت رکھتے ہیں۔ صرف ان لوگوں کے ساتھ دوستی کرنے سے اللہ تعالیٰ تم کو منع کرتا ہے جو تم سے دین کے بارے میں لڑے ہوں (خواہ بالفعل یا بالعزم ) اور تم کو تمہارے گھروں سے نکالا ہو اور اگر نکالا بھی نہ ہو لیکن تمہارے نکالنے میں ( نکالنے والوں کی مدد کی ہو اور جو شخص ایسوں سے دوستی کرے گا سو وہ گنہ گار ہوں گے۔ (تھانوی) اس آیت سے ثابت ہوا کہ محاربین کے ساتھ حسن سلوک نہ کیا جائے اور جو کا فر غیر محارب ہیں ان کے ساتھ حسن سلوک کرنے سے دریغ نہ کرو۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ ماں باپ اگر غیر حربی ہوں تو بیٹا ان کو نفقہ دے گا اور اگر حربی ہیں تو ان کا نفقہ بیٹے پر واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور باپ اور ماں کے علاوہ دادا، دادی کے واسطے وجوب نفقہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ بھی باپوں اور ماؤں میں سے ہیں ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر باپ نہ ہو تو دادا اس کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔
اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دادا اور دادی بھی آدمی کے زندہ ہونے کا سبب ہیں تو اسی آدمی پر اپنی زندگی کا استحقاق رکھتے ہیں جیسے والدین میں ہے اور محتاج ہونے کی شرط اسلئے لگائی کہ اگر باپ مالدار ہو تو اس کا نفقہ اپنے مال میں واجب ہونا اولیٰ ہے بہ نسبت غیر کے مال میں واجب ہونے کے حضور اقدس صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بھی فرمایا کل من کد یمینک و عروق جنبک یعنی اپنے ہاتھ اور خون پسینہ کی
محنت سے کھاؤ۔
اور ر باذین کا اختلاف تو یہ نفقہ واجب ہونے سے مانع نہیں ہوتا ۔ دلیل آیت و صاحبهما في الدنيا معروفاً ہے ۔ یہ آیت دلالت کرتی ہے کہ والدین خواہ مومن ہوں یا کافرہوں ان کے ساتھ اعتدال کا برتاؤر کھے۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک اور امام
شافعی ہیں۔
Chapter of Maintenance. Maintenance of a person's parents and grandparents and grandmothers is obligatory if they are poor, even if they oppose him in religion. Section: It is obligatory upon a man to spend on his parents and his grandfathers and grandmothers if they are poor, even if they oppose him in his religion. As for the parents, due to His statement: 'And accompany them in the world with kindness' — the verse was revealed regarding disbelieving parents. It is not from kindness that he lives in the blessings of Allah and leaves them to die of hunger. As for the grandfathers and grandmothers, because they are from the fathers and mothers; for this reason the grandfather takes the place of the father in his absence, and because they are causes of his existence, so they become entitled to maintenance from him like the parents. The condition of poverty is because if he is wealthy, making his maintenance obligatory from his own wealth is more appropriate than from the wealth of others. Difference in religion does not prevent that, due to what we recited. Translation: Section! It is obligatory upon a man to give maintenance to his parents and grandfathers and grandmothers when they are needy, even if they oppose him in religion. However, for parents, the proof is the saying of Allah: 'And accompany them in this world with kindness' — meaning live with parents in moderation. This verse was revealed concerning disbelieving parents, and kindness is not that he himself enjoys divine blessings and leaves his parents to die of hunger. For grandfathers and grandmothers, the proof is that they are also from the fathers and mothers; for this reason, in the absence of the father, the grandfather takes his place, and because they too are a cause of his life, so they have a claim to life maintenance from him, like parents. The condition of need was imposed because if the father is wealthy, then his maintenance being obligatory from his own wealth is more appropriate than from another's wealth. Difference in religion does not prevent the obligation of maintenance, due to this verse we recited. Explanation: After finishing the maintenance of children, in this section we will discuss maintenance for parents, grandfather, grandmother, and servant. The issue is that it is obligatory for a person to give maintenance to his mother, father, grandfather, grandmother, provided they are needy, even if they oppose him in religion. So for parents, the proof is the saying of the Almighty: 'But if they strive to make you associate with Me that of which you have no knowledge, then do not obey them, but accompany them in this world with kindness and follow the path of those who turn to Me.' (Surah Luqman). This verse was revealed concerning Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas. He had become Muslim, and his mother, named Jamilah, was a disbeliever. She stopped eating and drinking because of Sa'd's acceptance of Islam. He came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and this verse was revealed. Its conclusion is: do not obey them in matters of religion, but in this world treat them with kindness. And treating them with kindness is not that you enjoy Allah's blessings and leave them to die of hunger. This verse makes clear that if parents are needy, then it is obligatory upon the son to provide for them, even if there is a difference in religion between them. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, in Sharh al-Kafi, deduced from the saying of the Almighty: 'Do not say to them 'uff'.' In this way, that verse prohibits saying 'uff' to parents, i.e., causing them harm. And not giving them maintenance when in need causes greater harm and distress. Therefore, it becomes obligatory for a person to give maintenance to his parents. And since the verse is absolute, this ruling is general, whether the parents are Muslim or disbeliever. Also, the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, the best of a man's wealth is from his earnings, and his child is from his earnings, so eat from the earnings of your children.' This hadith also proves that the father's maintenance is obligatory from his child's earnings. It should be clear that the verse 'And accompany them in this world with kindness' applies to non-harbi parents. If the parents are harbi (enemy combatants), even if they have come to Dar al-Islam with aman, the son will not be forced to give them maintenance. Because Allah Almighty says: 'Allah does not forbid you from those who do not fight you because of religion and do not expel you from your homes from being righteous toward them and acting justly toward them. Indeed, Allah loves those who act justly. Allah only forbids you from those who fight you because of religion and expel you from your homes and aid in your expulsion from taking them as allies. And whoever takes them as allies, then those are the wrongdoers.' (Surah Al-Mumtahanah). From this verse it is established that we should not treat combatants kindly, but do not refrain from treating non-combatant disbelievers kindly. So it is established that if parents are non-harbi, the son will give them maintenance; if they are harbi, their maintenance is not obligatory upon the son. Apart from father and mother, the proof for the obligation of maintenance for grandfather and grandmother is that they too are from the fathers and mothers. For this reason, when the father is absent, the grandfather takes his place. And the second proof is that grandfather and grandmother are also causes of a person's existence, so they have a claim to maintenance from that person, like the parents. The condition of need was imposed because if the father is wealthy, his maintenance being obligatory from his own wealth is more appropriate than from another's wealth. The Holy Prophet (peace be upon him) also said: 'Eat from the earnings of your hands and your sweat.' And difference in religion does not prevent the obligation of maintenance. The proof is the verse 'And accompany them in this world with kindness.' This verse indicates that parents, whether believers or disbelievers, should be treated with moderation. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i also hold this view.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of Nafaqah (maintenance) in Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah, discusses the obligation of providing for one's ascendants (parents and grandparents) when they are poor, even if they are non-Muslim. The author begins by stating the ruling: a man must support his parents, grandfathers, and grandmothers if they are poor, regardless of religious difference. Then he provides the proof: for parents, the Quranic verse 'And accompany them in this world with kindness' (Surah Luqman) was revealed about disbelieving parents, indicating that kindness includes material support; neglecting them to die of hunger is not kindness. For grandparents, the reasoning is qiyas: they are like parents in lineage and cause of existence, so they deserve maintenance similarly. The condition of poverty is necessary because a wealthy person's maintenance is from his own wealth, not another's. Religious difference does not prevent obligation, as the verse is general and applies to both Muslim and non-Muslim parents. The commentary then elaborates on the proofs: the story of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and his mother, and the argument from the prohibition of saying 'uff' (harm) to parents; withholding maintenance is greater harm. Additionally, the hadith that a child is from the father's earnings implies the father can consume from the child's wealth, thus maintenance is due. However, an exception is made for harbi (enemy) parents: they are not entitled to maintenance because the verse of kindness applies only to non-combatants. This is supported by the Quranic verse from Surah Al-Mumtahanah distinguishing between those who fight and those who do not. The passage ends by noting that Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i agree that religious difference does not prevent maintenance. The passage type is a ruling supported by textual proofs (ruling_with_proof) with detailed commentary expanding the matn.

Key Terms
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance, including food, clothing, and shelter, that one is obligated to provide for certain relatives.
اجداد/جدات (ajdaad/jiddaat): Grandfathers and grandmothers (both paternal and maternal) from the lineage of ascendants.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims, including those who actively fight or support the enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for the obligation of maintenance of parents?
A) The parents must be Muslim.
B) The parents must be poor and needy.
C) The parents must be elderly.
D) The son must be wealthy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates maintenance for needy ascendants, even if non-Muslim, but excludes those who are enemy combatants (harbi).

Nikah — Marriage

Automatic Freedom by Owning a Mahram Relative
Expanding the ruling on automatic freedom through qiyas and refutations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a minor's ownership of a dhu rahim mahram causes automatic freedom, explain the qiyas to nafaqah, and distinguish between lineage-based and fosterage-based mahramiyyah.

Core Idea
Owning a lineage mahram automatically frees them, even for a child or insane person.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a critical nuance in the law of emancipation: when a child or insane person becomes the owner of a close blood relative who is a mahram (unmarriageable), that relative is freed immediately. The ruling is not based on a conscious act but on the legal effect (hukm wad'i) triggered by the relationship. The author uses qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) to nafaqah (maintenance) to extend the ruling to minors and the insane, and distinguishes fosterage from lineage. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi approach to automatic legal consequences and the role of illah in extending rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Determine what happens when a person owns a dhu rahim mahram (lineage-based unmarriageable relative). The text states that the owned relative becomes free. This applies even to minors and the insane upon acquisition of ownership.
The freedom is automatic (hukm wad'i), not requiring a verbal act of emancipation.
2
Unpack the proof: qiyas to nafaqah
Examine the analogy used: just as nafaqah (maintenance) for a needy mahram is wajib upon the wealth of a minor or insane person, so too the right of the slave (haqq al-'itq) attaches when that mahram is owned. The common illah is the presence of mahramiyyah and a need-related right.
This is qiyas khafi because the illah (mahramiyyah) is not explicit in the nafaqah ruling but is derived by taḥqīq al-manāṭ.
3
Address the objection: ownership of a foster relative
Consider the counterexample: a man buys his paternal cousin who is also his foster sister. The text explains she is not freed because the mahramiyyah from fosterage is not the effective cause; only lineage-based mahramiyyah triggers freedom.
The illah is 'mahramiyyah due to qarabah (lineage)', not mahramiyyah due to radā'ah (fosterage).
4
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i does not accept that ownership automatically frees a mahram relative. The Hanafi school responds by rejecting the objection as unfounded, relying on the analogy to nafaqah and the established principle of haqq al-'itq.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different methods of qiyas and recognition of automatic legal effects.

اور یہی صاحبین کا قول ہے۔ لہذا امام شافعی نے جو امتناع بیان کیا تھا۔ ہمیں وہی تسلیم نہیں ۔ کیونکہ ہم اس کو منہ نہیں جانتے ہیں۔ و هذا بخلاف ما اذا ملک ابنة عمه سے بھی ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر ذی رحم محرم کا مالک ہونا علت ہے اس کے آزاد ہونے کی اس شخص پر جو اس کا مالک ہوا ہے تو چا کی بیٹی جو اسکی رضاعی بہن بھی ہے اس کو اپنے چچا کے بیٹے پر آزاد ہو جانا چاہئے اگر وہ اس کو خرید لے۔ حالانکہ آزاد نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ محرمیت سے وہ محرمیت مراد ہے جس میں قرابت مؤثر ہو اور یہ ایسا نہیں ہے کیونکہ محرمیت رضاعت کی وجہ سے ہے نہ کہ قرابت کی وجہ سے۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر بچہ یا مجنون اپنے کسی قریبی محرم کا مالک ہوا تو وہ بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس آزادی کیساتھ بندے کا حق متعلق ہو گیا اور علت یعنی ذور حجم محرم کا مالک ہونا بھی پایا گیا اس لئے وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا ، پس نفقہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا یعنی جیسے قریب محرم محتاج کا نفقہ بچہ اور مجنون کے مال میں واجب ہوتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی اگر یہ کسی ذورحم محرم کے مالک ہوں تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
And this is the saying of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Therefore, what Imam Shafi'i mentioned as prohibition, we do not accept it, because we do not know its basis. And this is in contrast to the case when one owns his paternal cousin's daughter, which is also an answer to a question. The question is: If owning a dhu rahim mahram is the cause (illah) for the slave's freedom upon the one who has owned him, then the daughter of one's paternal uncle (who is also his foster sister) should be freed on the person who buys her, even though she is not freed. The answer is that 'mahramiyyah' here refers to that which is effective due to lineage, and this is not the case because the mahramiyyah is due to fosterage, not lineage. The author of Hidayah said: If a child or an insane person becomes the owner of any close mahram relative, that relative will also be freed. Because the right of the slave becomes attached to this freedom, and the cause (being the owner of a dhu rahim mahram) is present, so he becomes free. It then resembles nafaqah: just as nafaqah of a needy close mahram is wajib upon the child's and insane person's wealth, similarly, if they own a dhu rahim mahram, that relative will be freed. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling that ownership of a dhu rahim mahram (a relative within the prohibited degrees of marriage due to lineage) automatically frees that relative. The text first clarifies that the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that such ownership causes freedom, contrary to Imam Shafi'i's view. It then addresses an objection: if a man buys his paternal cousin's daughter who is also his foster sister (due to rada'ah), why isn't she freed? The answer is that the effective cause (illah) for freedom is mahramiyyah based on lineage (qarabat), not fosterage. Even though she is a mahram due to fosterage, that does not trigger freedom. The key point is that the freedom is an automatic right (haqq) that attaches to the slave, and the presence of the cause (ownership of a lineage-based mahram) suffices. The ruling is extended to minors and the insane by analogy (qiyas) to nafaqah: just as they are obligated to provide nafaqah to a poor close relative, so too if they own such a relative, that relative becomes free. This analogy is based on istihsan, as direct qiyas might not yield this result. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is from the Hidayah.

Key Terms
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rahim mahram): A relative within the prohibited degrees of marriage (mahram) due to lineage (nasab), not fosterage or marriage.
عتق (itq): Emancipation of a slave; here, it occurs automatically upon the occurrence of ownership over a dhu rahim mahram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a minor becomes the owner of his maternal aunt (who is a mahram by lineage), what happens?
A) The aunt becomes free.
B) The aunt remains a slave.
C) The aunt is freed only if the minor is adult.
D) The aunt is sold to someone else.

Key Takeaway
Ownership of a lineage-based mahram by a minor or insane person automatically frees the relative, based on the illah of mahramiyyah and analogy to nafaqah.
